Once considered the heralds of a new, revolutionary world order for China, the Kuomintang has been much reduced and fractured in recent years. Following the death of its founder and primary leader, Sun Yat-sen, the party largely split into intense factionalism over the true successor to the Guofu (Sun's honorary title as eternal premier). By orthodoxy it was the currently acting-generalissimo Hu Hanmin. However through political machinations, he would see his position abrogated and replaced by a ruling \
KMT-CRS
China Revival Society (Zhongguo Guomindang Zhonghua Fuxingshe)\n§LThe China Revival Society (CRS) was a collection of radical Whampoa military circles, united in their shared sense of ultra-nationalist fervour. The failure of the leftist committee's most recent adventure into China has broken the sway of their firebrand, leaving them a shell of what they once were. Still, a small remnant of their movement remains, built around a small core group of confidants surrounding men like Hu Zongnan, He Zhonghan, and Deng Wenyi. Having embedded themselves into our military, there is a growing sense of worry that our amnesty will breathe new life into the smouldering embers of this cult.§!\n
CSP-R
Chinese Syndicalist Party - Radical Faction (Zhongguo Gongtuandang-jijin pai)\n§LThe Chinese Syndicalist Party has splintered thanks to the continuing failure of the Chinese Revolution, with many disillusioned by the lack of progress by the Orthodox Faction in implementing syndicalism in the nation and perceived passivity in handling the united front with the Kuomintang splintering off into the so-called Radical Faction. They have called for a much more authoritarian, confrontational approach - challenging their fellow socialists as well as imperialists, warlords, and capitalists. Like many other Radicals, Zhang Tailei also went to Europe to study but became disillusioned with the main branch of the CSP-Radicals led by Qiu Qibai and Chen Shaoyu. The Guangdong branch is particularly vanguardist in their demands for social emancipation and revolutionary in their methods - advocating that the proletariat align even with bandits and thieves to drive out imperialists and reactionaries to build a true worker's commune in Guangzhou.§!\n
World Society
New World Society (Shijie She)\n§LThe World Society enjoys the distinction of being the first organised anarchist organisation (anarchists groups traditionally avoid referring to themselves as parties) in China. Led by the Four Elders (Zhang Renjie, Li Shizeng, Wu Zhihui, and Cai Yuanpei), these Paris-based anarchists became mentors for many prominent Kuomintang figures. Their influence was eclipsed however by the rise of the Chinese Syndicalist Party, especially as their relationship with other anarchists deteriorated and they were forced to retreat into their positions in the Kuomintang establishment.\n\nHu Hanmin's rise has given them a political comeback of sorts. Sympathetic to anarchist principles and more understanding than the actual anarchists themselves of the compromises the Four Elders had to make during the Chinese revolution, Hu Hanmin has offered the World Society a lifeline by funding their institutions such as the Chinese Labour University. In return, the World Society has provided a useful check to the influence of the Chinese Syndicalist Party, quashing the threat of Marxism to anarchist influence within the League of Chinese Syndicalists.§!\n
CSP-O
Chinese Syndicalist Party - Orthodox Faction (Zhongguo Gongtuandang-Zhengtong Pai)\n§LThe Chinese Syndicalist Party may have been founded in Shanghai, but their home base has long been in Guangzhou. Guangzhou (often referred to as Canton) is home to considerable union activity and syndicalist firebrands, and it is no surprise that the city has been particularly receptive to the syndicalist message. The Orthodox Faction of the CSP was built on a compromise between Chen Duxiu's councilist faction and Li Lisan's union-based faction, influenced by the French syndicalist model and sharing Marxist-influences.\n\nGuangzhou, as one of the two pillars of the Chinese Syndicalist Party, has seen a slight divergence from the Nanjing-Shanghai branch. Led by Deng Zhongxia and Su Zhaozheng, tensions with the implementation of the Li Lisan line and general distance from the other Syndicalist outpost has encouraged a more independent streak from their fellow Orthodox members.§!\n
KMT-PAC

KMT-RC
Revolutionary Committee of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Gemingweiyuanhui)\n§LThe ultimate (if belated) victory of the Chinese Civil War, Tan Pingshan has emerged as the foremost leader of the Kuomintang in a stunning upset. Gathering various party leaders, particularly those of his former allies in the Provisional Action Committee, though not forgetting to draw useful cadres from the RCA and even the CSP, Tan has reorganised the party under one Revolutionary Committee under his control. He has promised to heal divisions between the party's factions and chart a third path, his own path, going forward to preserve China's revolutionary values.§!\n
CRP
Chinese Revolutionary Party (Zhonghua Gemin Dang)\n§LFirst conceived by Tan Pingshan and Zhang Bojun in 1931 Shanghai, the Chinese Revolutionary Party represents the final manifestation of Tan's dream of establishing a third party independent of the KMT and CSP's shortcomings. Rallying defectors from both parties under Tan Pingshan's leadership, it aims to chart a new direction to bring the syndicalist revolution to China. This party, freed from the shackles of their predecessors' bureaucracy and infighting, aims to bring the unbridled spirit of the Chinese proletariat to the forefront and wash away the old reactionary order.§!\n
LCS
League of Chinese Syndicalists (Zhongguo Gongtuanzhuyi Tongmeng)\n§LThe League of Chinese Syndicalists was first founded in 1925 in response to the Hong Kong-Canton strikes. Dominated by the Chinese Syndicalist Party, it also included various other factions such as the anarchist World Society as well as disparate independent Chinese socialists seeking a space independent of Kuomintang control. The League's viability was always in doubt, especially with its perennial instability, but the rise of Tan Pingshan and his Guangdong syndicalist movement has allowed him to eclipse other leftist groups and take leadership of the movement. Harnessing the power of the Chinese proletariat, Tan and his revitalised League now aim to bring the syndicalist message from the urbanised coast into the Chinese hinterland!§!\n
KMT-L
Kuomintang - Leftist Remnant (Guomindang - Zuopai Canbu)\n§L$GXC_starting_KMT_intro$\n\nWhilst far from an entirely diminished force due to the heavy presence of the urban workers and agrarian peasant movements within Liangguang, the leftist remnants of the Kuomintang within Liangguang are largely found within the Guangdong Provincial Farmers' Association of Peng Pai. An infamous local revolutionary and pioneer of agrarian socialism, Peng has continued to herald the cause of revolutionary socialism against all local bullies and evil gentry alike. Operating just outside the borders of Guangdong however, is one Chen Mingshu. Leading his 10th Division of the National Revolutionary Army, he has collaborated with the likes of Tang Shengzhi of the 8th NRA to conduct a guerilla campaign in Eastern and Northern Guangdong; acting on behalf of the Leftist Central Executive Committee, and the MinGan revolutionaries.§!\n
KMT-PAC

KMT-GPFA
Guangdong Provincial Farmers' Association (Guangdong Sheng Nongmin Xiehui)\n§LPeng Pai was the son of the local Cantonese elite and was able to afford advanced schooling abroad. Upon his return, he turned his attention to the plight of the poor farmers, undertaking a tenure as Education commissioner of Haifeng in 1921. Growing more radical and embracing a socialist following, he burned the deeds of the land he inherited and announced the creation of the Haifeng County General Farmers' Association. This movement, which provided mutual protection and aid for farmers in the region, quickly swelled in numbers and was reformed into the Guangdong Provincial Farmers' Association.\n\nRepressed by Chen Jiongming and gentry forces, they aligned with the Kuomintang and became an important organ within the party for mobilising the peasants for the revolution. The failure of the Northern Expedition saw Peng Pai and his men retreat back to Haifeng, where they maintained a tenuous connection with the broader network of Kuomintang insurgents. They retain a stubborn hold over the area, resisting efforts to root them out.§!\n
KMT-RC
Revolutionary Committee of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang gemingweiyuanhui)\n§LThe ultimate (if belated) victory of the Chinese Civil War, Peng Pai has emerged as the foremost leader of the Kuomintang in a stunning upset. Gathering various party leaders, particularly those of his former Guangdong Provincial Farmers' Association, though not forgetting to draw useful cadres from the RCA, PAC and even the CSP, Peng has reorganised the party under one Revolutionary Committee under his control. He has sought to emphasise the peasant's role in the national revolution, though not entirely dismissing the contributions of the proletariat and petty bourgeoisie.§!\n
CPP
Chinese Peasants' Party (Zhongguo Nongmin Dang)\n§LAn outgrowth of Peng Pai's old Guangdong Provincial Farmers' Association, the Chinese Peasants Party has replaced the discredited Kuomintang as China's leading socialist party under Peng's rule. Emphasising the peasant's role in the national revolution, though not entirely dismissing the contributions of the proletariat and petty bourgeoisie, the Chinese Peasants' Party has been quick to spread its message of mutual cooperation, defence, and education to the impoverished farmers across the nation. Aggressive in their tactics and tightly knit in their solidarity, in hindsight their victory was no surprise though some worry about Peng's growing cult of personality.§!\n
KMT-RCA
$GXC_rca_party_long_tt$\n§LThe Reorganisation Comrades Association was founded by Chen Gongbo, Gu Mengyu and other Kuomintang leftists to defend the 1924 Reorganisation and later to advance the rule of their champion: Wang Jingwei. Internally, the RCA was divided between the Radicals under Chen, who advocated violent class warfare and Marxism, and the Moderates under Gu who preferred class collaboration.\n\nWang Jingwei's decision to join our government has shattered the RCA with many of the rank and file denouncing him as a sell-out. Chen Gongbo has refrained from directly criticising his friend, but has retreated into the shadows as Wang throws his weight behind Gu Mengyu's wing and emphasised his left-nationalist credentials. The RCA retains some sway within our party, particularly among the civilian bureaucracy, parts of the intelligentsia, and overseas chapters, but it's clear that they are well past their heyday.§!\n
Reorganisation Comrades Association of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Gaizu Tongzhi Hui)
KMT-NFA
New Fourth Army of the National Revolutionary Army (Guomingeminjun Di Si Jun)\n§LUpon the collapse of the League of Eight Provinces, the insurgents in the MinGan zone ordered their besieged troops to sally out and break their encirclement - making one last do-or-die attempt to liberate the Eastern seaboard. General Chen Mingshu and his Tenth Division were ordered southwards into Guangdong, hoping to rally other leftist cells along the way to Guangzhou in a diversion operation.\n\nThey proved more successful than expected, aided by the sudden successes of rightist cells across Liangguang. Tensions have arisen in Guangdong however, with the wealthier south having fallen under the control of General Chen Jitang. The growing leftist force in the north has been reorganised into the New Fourth Army, claiming the proud mantle of its Northern Expedition predecessor and signifying its dream of liberating all of the province. While allied with radical leftist factions, Chen Mingshu and his allies' moderate stances have given them access to sympathetic republicans within Guangzhou.§!\n
KMT-RC
Revolutionary Committee of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Gemingweiyuanhui)\n§LThe ultimate (if belated) victory of the Chinese Civil War, Chen Mingshu has emerged as the foremost leader of the Kuomintang in a stunning upset. Gathering various party leaders, particularly those of his former allies in the MinGan insurgency, though not forgetting to draw useful cadres from the RCA, World Society, and even RCF, Chen has reorganised the party under one Revolutionary Committee under his control. He has promised to heal divisions between the party's factions and chart a more moderate, stable path going forward.§!\n
PPP
Productive People's Party (Shengchan Renmin Dang)\n§LDissatisfied with the undemocratic nature of the Kuomintang government, its inaction against imperialism, and concerns over the practicality of its socialist agenda, Chen Mingshu and the New Fourth Army revolted and brought down the corrupt party-state. In its place they have created a new Productive People's Party, meant to bring about the political tutelage in a more stable, more moderate pace.§!\n
KMT-RCF
Reconstruction Faction of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Zaizao Pai)\n§LThe Crown Prince's Clique was a loose collection of (then Mayor of Guangzhou) Sun Fo friends and allies, most of whom were recent graduates of western universities. Liberal, technocratic, and often having ties to wealthy donors of the party, it straddled the line between the factions of the growing party divide. After the Northern Expedition, it more formally coalesced into the Reconstruction Faction in Hawaii. Seeing the restoration of the Kuomintang in Guangzhou as an opportunity, Sun Fo has dispatched his right hand man Liang Hancao to the city, cosying up with Cantonese officials, intellectuals and the urban elite in hopes of building a power-base for his mentor.§!\n
KMT-RCF
Reconstruction Faction of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Zaizao Pai)\n§LThe Crown Prince's Clique was a loose collection of (then Mayor of Guangzhou) Sun Fo friends and allies, most of whom were recent graduates of western universities. Liberal, technocratic, and often having ties to wealthy donors of the party, it straddled the line between the factions of the growing party divide. After the Northern Expedition, it more formally coalesced into the Reconstruction Faction in Hawaii. Sun Fo's decision to join our government has brought with him the bulk of the Reconstruction Faction, as well as their powerful Overseas Chinese Commission networks in Southeast Asia and various military officers associated with the India Clique.§!\n

PSC
$GXC_Old_PSC_party_long_tt$\n§LOwing its origins to its first iteration founded in 1913 by Tongmenghui party members whom rejected Dr. Sun's demand for personal loyalty oaths after the failure of the Second Revolution against Yuan Shikai, the Political Science Clique is an odd bunch amongst Beiyang parliamentarians. They established the European Affairs Research Society in Tokyo, which later evolved into the Political Science Society in 1916. Rejecting the need for a Northern Expedition to unite China as espoused by Dr. Sun and his Kuomintang, they instead worked with southern warlords like Cen Chunxuan, and Lu Rongting, to topple Sun Yat-sen and his Constitution Protection Government.\n\nInstead opting to participate in the Beiyang electoral system and promote peaceful negotiations with the Northern Warlords, they would find themselves in many high up positions within the senate, assembly and even cabinet. When Sun, with the aid of Guangdong warlord Chen Jiongming drove out Cen and Lu from Guangdong, joined by Tang Jiyao's rejection of Gu Pinzhen from Yunnan, the Old Political Science Clique effectively collapsed. Losing the majority of their greatest influential positions, they all but submitted entirely to the Beiyang political order. With their last ascension to prominence being that of Huang Fu, leading a briefly liberal interim government after the Beijing Coup.\n\nWelcomed back by their mutual compatriots in the Western Hills Clique, the Old Political Science Clique has once more been thrust into the annals of power within the Kuomintang sphere. Keen to help with the new constitutional path that the party has begun to pursue, political science has rapidly become one of the Western Hills Clique's greatest allies and assets.§!\n
Old Political Science Clique (Jiu Zhengxue Xì)
KMT-WHC
Western Hills Clique of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Xishan Huiyi Pai)\n§LAfter the Reorganisation in 1924, Sun Yat-sen took the party in a drastically left-wards, vanguardist direction. Many of his old Tongmenghui allies departed the Guangzhou government as a result, disgusted by the flirtation with socialism and/or Sun's assumption of extraordinary powers. Those who stayed hoped to convince the Premier to reverse the reorganisation, growing increasingly discontented with the Chinese Syndicalist Party and other socialists assembling in the city.\n\nSun's death in 1925 saw many of his followers in Beijing assembled by the Western Hills for his funeral and discussions about the future of the party. Split initially into moderate and radical camps regarding how to address the fall of Hu Hanmin and the rise of Wang Jingwei, the radicals sought Wang's overthrow won out. Ejected from the party after the disastrous Fourth Plenum, most retreated to party bases in Shanghai and Beijing. Eventually, with Hu's own flight from Guangzhou they joined him in exile in Moscow where they provided a large number of anti-socialist, civilian conservatives for his coalition.§!\n
KMT-NGDC
New Guangdong Clique of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Xinyuexi)\n§LGuangdong has always been a major power player in the warlord era, boasting a wealthy economic base and long-held legislative autonomy which gave rise to an independent military force that became known as the Guangdong Army. Commanded by Chen Jiongming, it hosted Sun Yat-sen and the Kuomintang during the Constitutional Protection War but Chen Jiongming soon broke with Sun. Many of those who remained loyal to the Kuomintang slowly coalesced around Chen Jitang, who leveraged his connections with Kuomintang elder Gu Yingfen and other conservative gentrymen as well as fellow officers in the Fourth Army (based out of Guangdong) to rise in status.\n\nDespite collaborating with the Chen Lianbo government after the Northern Expedition collapsed, General Chen successfully led the Guangdong Army to rebel against their nominal masters to lead a Kuomintang restoration with himself as Governor. Benefiting from an entrenched web of political patronage he and his cronies have established for themselves, they have sought to protect their gains by keeping their focus local while parleying their critical support for nationally focused leaders to maintain Guangdong's treasured autonomy.§!\n
KMT-EDC
Elders Clique of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Yuanlao Pai)\n§LHu Hanmin was once Sun Yat-sen's closest deputy, chosen to be his successor as Generalissimo of the Guangzhou Government. But in the power struggle that emerged shortly after Sun's death, Hu was outflanked and demoted by a coalition of rivals including the perfidious Wang Jingwei and upstart Chiang Kai-shek. His commitment to the cause prevented him from openly breaking from the party as many of his allies recommended, and so he spent the next few years struggling to steer the party back on the right track.\n\nHis closest followers became known as the Elders faction, an odd grouping among the right because of their support for the principles of the Reorganisation although rejecting Wang Jingwei and socialist infiltration of the party. Vanguardist and with eclectic beliefs that draw inspiration from Marxism, Anarchism, Liberalism, and traditional Chinese philosophy, they believe themselves to be the true followers of Dr. Sun.§!\n
KMT-NGXC
New Guangxi Clique of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Xinguixi)\n§LIn the wars that ravaged Guangxi, various clans of soldiers and bandits (the lines often blurring) rose in prominence. As Lu Rongting's hold over the region began to falter, one of those bands rose in its place - led by the ambitious Li Zongren, ingenious Bai Chongxi, and diligent Huang Shaohong. This New Guangxi Clique overthrew the old one in the aftermath of the Yue-Gui wars, loosely aligning themselves with the Kuomintang government. Their forces became organised as the Seventh Army, and fought with distinction during the Northern Expedition.\n\nThe bitter aftermath of the Long March saw the clique forced out of Guangxi and into exile, resorting to petty border raids for supplies. During that time, Li and Huang further integrated themselves into the Kuomintang apparatus and fully adopted their ideology, while Bai began to theorise about drastic reforms needed for the National Revolutionary Army. They returned to Guangxi a changed movement, and the conquest of their home province is now but a stepping stone to their dreams of a changed China.§!\n
Warlords
$GXC_warlord_remnant_party_long_tt$\n§LDefeat on the battlefield has not eradicated all vestiges of warlordism in China. Across the nation, there remain plenty of hangovers from destroyed major warlord factions, whether it be petty warlord cliques who submitted to new masters at the right moment, lower ranking subordinates who were hired by the new administration, or sometimes new strongmen who arose from the ensuing power vacuum and took advantage of their affiliation with the winners. The fact that many are merely feigning loyalty to the national cause to bully and exploit the people does not mean others are not genuinely popular - even the most avaricious men of the high warlord era were careful to build strong guanxi networks spanning military, civilian, and social circles. Charismatic, connected, and often corrupt, those that survived the changing order are masters at tapping into regionalist sentiment as well as discontent with the status quo, determined to outlast efforts to purge them. Only time will tell how many generations it will take to truly eliminate the harrowing legacy of the warlord era.§!\n
Assorted Regionalists and Strongmen
KMT-R
Kuomintang - Rightist Remnant (Guomindang - Youpai Canbu)\n§L$GXC_starting_KMT_intro$\n\nCentred around the enigmatic Hu Hanmin, the Rightist Kuomintang Remnants within Liangguang politics hold very little sway from their far away Central Executive Committee in exile. However, on the ground there are many actors in the region that share sympathies with the Old Right of the party, namely Chen Jitang (formerly of the 4th National Revolutionary Army, and founder of the New Guangdong Clique), and Li Zongren of the 7th National Revolutionary Army, and the New Guangxi Clique. Operating as fairly independent actors, it awaits to be seen if either man could bring the revolution back to its birthplace.§!\n
KMT-WPC

Combining (relatively) modern Russo-French doctrine, socialist-inspired ideological indoctrination, and the powerful personality of Headmaster Chiang Kai-shek, it provided the party-state an army of fanatically loyal cadets willing to carry out its directives.\n\nIts influence soon became a target for political actors. Leftist Generals such as Deng Yanda and Zhou Enlai, Internationale Advisors, and Chiang Kai-shek soon fought for influence among the students, with Chiang's followers coalescing into what became known as the Whampoa Clique. KMT-RRC
$GXC_reconstruction_research_committee_long_tt$\n§LFounded by the New Guangxi Clique in a bid to minimise the influence of Hu Hanmin and the Moscow Committee within their province, the Revolutionary Comrades Association of the Kuomintang became Guangxi's leading secret society headquartered in a garden bungalow in Nanning. Reconstruction Research Committee of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Jianshe Yanjiu Hui)
The Grand Republican Alliance is a quasi-legal political coalition of largely Southern Chinese parties operating in opposition towards the established Beiyang political order. Formed in 1931 after the swelling of anti-concessionist energy and nationalist agitation following the failure of the Zhili-Fengtian negotiation discussions, the Grand Republican Alliance would briefly ally with the retired Duan Qirui, and be joined by other \
The China Democratic League would find its origins in the Fall of 1929, wherein after the National Assembly Elections and the resulting Harmony Association majority a group of endeavouring intellectuals would found the United National Construction League with the hopes of promoting democracy in China, albeit with the rather controversial inclusion of Zhang Bojun and Tan Pingshan. Ultimately banned in 1932 following the Shanghai Uprising, its component parties would continue to meet in the new underground Federation of Chinese Democratic Parties, without the aforementioned socialist revolutionaries.\n\nWhilst largely a force of all participating liberals and independents, including but not limited to the Political Science Clique, Chinese Constitutionalist Party, National Salvation Federation, China Vocational Education Society and Endeavour Society, the FCDP in the South would see itself coalesce and emerge from quasi-legal status to that of a fully fledged political alliance known as the China Democratic League. Including the Democratic Socialist Party, Crescent Moon Society, China National Democratic Construction Association and components of the aforementioned factions, it remains a force spearheading legitimate democracy within China.
CCP-NRS
$GXC_CCP_NRS_party_long_tt$\n§LThe Chinese Constitutionalist Party, formally led by Xu Qin has many disparate branches across the nation. Largely led by the successors of the Reformist Liang Qichao strain of political ideology, its main arbiters in the South of the nation are Liang's two last protégés, Zhang Dongsun and Junmai. At their mentor's side since his days in Japan, the two Zhangs were similarly by and large followers of Zhang's political ideology as it morphed throughout the Warlord Era. With him during the Progressive Party, and during the Research Clique era, Zhang Dongsun and Junmai would join in the renewal and revival of the Chinese Constitutionalist Party.\n\nWhilst the North followed and toed the line of the Right Wing of Liang's thoughts, his early, more moderate beliefs, the South by and large stuck to Liang's last intellectual developments. Taking on a more reformist, socialistic view of politics, Zhang Junmai's preference for Social Democracy akin to that of the Social Democratic Party in Germany has ferried his wing of the Chinese Constitutionalists into the leftist vacuum left by the Kuomintang's failures in 1927. Joined by notable democratic guild socialist Zhang Dongsun, the duo have largely split from the mainstream CCP.\n\nA composite faction of the United National Construction League, and later the Federation of Chinese Democratic Parties, Zhang Junmai's National Institute of Political Science would be purged by his former patron Sun Chuanfang for leftist sympathies. Taking his followers and retreating to Liangguang upon Chen Lianbo's invitation, Dongsun and Junmai would form the National Renaissance Society as an association of Left-Liangists, largely disagreeing with the Party Centre in Beijing.§!\n
Chinese Constitutionalist Party - National Renaissance Society (Xianfa Yanjiu Hui Guojia Fuxing Xiehui)
GRA-DSP
$GXC_GRA_DSP_party_long_tt$\n§L$GXC_GRA_intro$\n\nEvolving from Zhang Junmai's National Renaissance Society founded in 1932, the Democratic Socialist Party found itself formed under the pretence of the Seven Gentlemen Incident of 1936. Formally breaking away from all ties to their Party Headquarters in Beijing on opposition to the Beiyang Line, the National Renaissance Left-Liangist clique would promulgate their own party. Inspired by reformist socialism, the Democratic Socialist Party combines the ideals of Zhang Junmai's German Social Democracy inspired politics with Zhang Dongsun's Democratic Guild Socialism.\n\nRejecting violent class struggle in the quest for a constitutional, democratic, and republican China, it is far more of an intellectual circle than a traditional party. Pressuring the Public Interest Party to remain true to the cause of democracy, the Democratic Socialists are rather relentless in their hounding of the \
Grand Republican Alliance - Democratic Socialist Party (Gonghe Datongmeng Zhongguo Minzhu Shehui Dang)
CDL-DSP

Championed by the Social Democrat Zhang Junmai and Guild Socialist Zhang Dongsun, their rejection of violent class struggle and focus on constitutional democracy has won them much popularity amongst the people and intellectuals alike. With the formation of the CDL, the DSP has been selected as the forefront runner in the electoral race, intent on seeing a democratic mandate to implement their \

GIMA
$GXC_GIMA_party_long_tt$\n§LThe Grain Industry Maintenance Association was established by Haifeng's local gentry in response to the rise of the Haifeng County General Farmers' Association, with the aim of protecting their landed interests and opposing the peasant organisation. The association has gone through several iterations throughout its history, having been dissolved and reformed several times as the political winds of Guangdong ebbed and flowed. It was dissolved when its first chairman, Chen Yuebo, fled to Hong Kong in the face of unfavourable political headwinds, and again, when Chen Jiongming was ousted from Guangdong by the Kuomintang.\n\nAs the Northern Expedition fractured and Haifeng came under the control of Ye Ju, the association was reformed under the chairmanship of Qiu Jingyun. With many of its members having close ties and even familial relations with Chen Jiongming, the association renewed its political backing of Chen in the Provincial Assembly, as well as assisting his ally, Ye Ju, in rooting out the lingering Farmers' Association within Haifeng.§!\n

PSC
Owing its origins to its first iteration founded in 1913 by Tongmenghui party members whom rejected Dr. Sun's demand for personal loyalty oaths after the failure of the Second Revolution against Yuan Shikai, the Political Science Clique is an odd bunch amongst Beiyang parliamentarians. They established the European Affairs Research Society in Tokyo, which later evolved into the Political Science Society in 1916. Rejecting the need for a Northern Expedition to unite China as espoused by Dr. Sun and his Kuomintang, they instead worked with southern warlords like Cen Chunxuan, and Lu Rongting, to topple Sun Yat-sen and his Constitution Protection Government.\n\nInstead opting to participate in the Beiyang electoral system and promote peaceful negotiations with the Northern Warlords, they would find themselves in many high up positions within the senate, assembly and even cabinet. When Sun, with the aid of Guangdong warlord Chen Jiongming drove out Cen and Lu from Guangdong, joined by Tang Jiyao's rejection of Gu Pinzhen from Yunnan, the Old Political Science Clique effectively collapsed. Losing the majority of their greatest influential positions, they all but submitted entirely to the Beiyang political order.
Old Political Science Clique (Jiu Zhengxue Xì)\n§L$GXC_psc_party_intro$\n\nFollowing the collapse of the Northern Expedition, the Old Political Science Clique would see something of a revival within Liangguang. With prominent positions such as Speaker of the Guangzhou Assembly being held by its coterie, and key warlords including Lin Hu, Yang Ximin, Shen Hongying, and Liu Zhenhuan all retaining vocal ties to the clique, they have become somewhat ingratiated with establishment politics, representing a more warlord strain of the faction.§!\n
Old Political Science Clique (Jiu Zhengxue Xì)\n§L$GXC_psc_party_intro$\n\nThe Political Science Clique has achieved a revival following the unification of the country under Liangguang. This has allowed the Cantonese branch to unite with their counterparts into a loose but broader bloc with Liu Zhenhuan as their warlord figurehead.§!\n
AACSG
Association of All Classes to Save Guangdong (Gejie jiu Yue lianhehui)\n§LThe Association is the political front for the Canton Merchants' Public Safety Organisation, better known as the Merchant Corps, which found its beginning in the turbulent years following the Xinhai Revolution. Formed to protect the merchant interests of Guangzhou, the Corps came to be welcomed by the city's populace for providing security in a time of chaotic uncertainty. With Chen Lianbo elected as commander of the Merchant Corps and Director of Finance, the volunteer corps grew in number during the 1910s and was reformed based on Western parliamentary politics.\n\nAlthough maintaining a neutral attitude towards the constant regime change in Guangzhou, the Merchant Corps eventually came into conflict with Sun Yat-sen Nationalist Government, culminating in the Merchant Corps Incident of 1924. Swiftly defeated by Chiang's army of Whampoa Military Academy cadets, the Corps was dissolved with many of the Corps leadership fleeing to Hong Kong. There they formed the Association of All Classes to Save Guangdong, backing Chen Jiongming unsuccessfully during the Eastern Expedition.\n\nWhen the Germans seized Guangzhou, Chen Lianbo appointed as interim Mayor of Guangzhou where he reformed and deployed the Merchant Corps to ensure public order. With the Kuomintang vanquished, the Association endured as a Guangdong regionalist movement, seeking to protect the province from further Old Guangxi Clique encroachment.§!\n
AACSC
Association of All Classes to Save China (Gejie jiu Zhongguo lianhehui)\n§LThe successor to the Association of All Classes to Save Guangdong, the backbone of this national variant remains in the various merchant associations, chambers of commerce, and merchant corps established throughout warlord China seeking an alternative to the arbitrary brutality of warlord rule. It represents the full manifestation of Chen Lianbo's ambitions of a merchant government and his wildest ambition of merchants across China uniting with each other and others to ensure public order and prosperity.\n\nDespite its lofty name, the Association remains dominated by Cantonese figures and the upper classes, though the new association is able to draw in elites from outside merchant circles. These include various politicians, military officers, gentrymen, scholars, and even middle class skilled professionals as well.§!\n
OGXC-YGF
Old Guangxi Clique - Young Guangxi Faction (Jiuguixi - Shaozhuang Pai)\n§L$GXC_OGXC_intro$\n\nAs inheritors of Lu Rongting's legacy and at the helm of a disunited Old Guangxi Clique, the Young Guangxi Faction is centred around Lu's adopted sons and heirs, led by a quadrumvirate between Lu Yuguang, Ma Ji, Liu Zhilu, and Lin Hu. The nominal masters of the Liangguang provinces with Lu inheriting his father's title as the Viceroy of Liangguang, nonetheless, their hold on the region continues to be challenged by Kuomintang insurgents as well as their rivals in Shaoguan, the Shen Army Faction.\n\nPragmatic in their approach and focused on extending their influence in Southern China, the Young Guangxi Faction also harbours ties to the Political Science Clique and various other political groups, harkening back to the Old Guangxi Clique's legacy in the National Protection War.§!\n
Old Guangxi Clique - Young Guangxi Faction (Jiuguixi - Shaozhuang Pai)\n§L$GXC_OGXC_intro$\n\nThe Young Guard of the Old Guangxi Clique, led by the triumvirs Ma Ji, Liu Zhilu, and Lin Hu managed to stage a revival, helping to restore Lu Rongting to power after the Northern Expedition. But after he died, he pass the torch to his adopted son Lu Yuguang, who managed to stun the nation by doing what his father only dreamed of - uniting the nation under his banner. Now all are silent as they wait to see what comes next.§!\n
JXS
Jingxing Society (Jingxing Hui)\n§LThe Jingxing Society was founded in 1921 as the personal brainchild of the eccentric Li Linsi as a loose association of German-educated intellectuals seeking to promote Westernisation and Sino-German relations. Though the core society was made up of scholars, it also attracted diplomats, businessmen, and even military officers as associates. As Sino-German ties improved, so did its prominence and the Society began to sponsor several major programs, including the establishment of the Sino-German Cultural and Economic Association in 1935.\n\nThis project attracted the interest of Zhu Jiahua, a German trained engineer and professor who helped co-found the Association. Noted for his diplomatic and administrative skills while handling Sino-German relations for Chen Lianbo, Sun Chuanfang, and Shen Hongying, he was able to parlay this into a major role in General Shen's government. Selected for his respectability and his supposed nonpartisanship, Zhu has proven to be a very capable politician in his own right and has allied and installed other Jingxing Society members to major positions of power as an extension of his smaller Zhu Jiahua clique.§!\n
OGXC-SAF
Old Guangxi Clique - Shen Army Faction (Jiuguixi - Shenjun Pai)\n§L$GXC_OGXC_intro$\n\nAppointed by the Southern Zhili as Governor of Guangdong during the final days of the Northern Expedition, Shen Hongying's position in Liangguang was tenuous at best, made worse when League forces retreated from Liangguang to focus on quelling the 1932 Shanghai Uprising. This opportunity led Lu Rongting to coordinate an alliance with Chen Lianbo and Deng Benyin to push Shen out of major positions in Guangxi and Guangdong, as well as knocking him out of his traditional power base in Guilin.\n\nWith a tepid alliance with the Jingxing Society as well as pro-German and pro-South Zhili groups in Liangguang, the Shen Army Faction seeks to realise the power that was promised to them back in 1927 and bring Guangdong under their control.§!\n
OGXC-ZAF
$GXC_ogxc_saf_party_zhao_army_long_tt$\n§L$GXC_OGXC_intro$\n\nShen Hongying built up a tight-knit faction of his own over the years, first in his base of operations in Guilin and later in Shaoguan. He supplemented his forces with various opportunists, Zhili officers, and German support, allowing him to become a dark horse candidate for leadership of China. Though he has since passed, his followers have coalesced around an uneasy pact between his son Shen Rongguang and his deputy Li Yaohan.\n\nUnder Li, the Zhao Army faction of the Old Guangxi Clique appears to have mustered enough strength to thrust his candidacy for the presidency, but many fear that Li has hardly a full term left in him.§!\n
Old Guangxi Clique - Zhao Army Faction (Jiuguixi - Zhaojun Pai)
Assorted Leaders
Hu Hanmin
Steadfast, incorruptible, stubborn. Many words can be used to describe Dr. Sun Yat-sen's most adamant protégé, and with such a career, it is unsurprising. One of the Kuomintang's most premier statesmen, Hu Hanmin would be a gifted student, having already mastered calligraphy by the age of 13. During his young teaching career at 16, Hu would become involved with the writings of Kang Youwei, Sun Yat-sen, and in 1900, when his dear friend Shi Jianru became a martyr, Hu would become resolute in the revolutionary struggle to save the nation.\n\nStudying in Japan with the likes of Wang Jingwei, Hu would meet Liao Zhongkai, and aid in the founding of the Tongmenghui, meeting his mentor, Dr. Sun, for the first time. Becoming enamoured with the man, Hu would develop into his most orthodox disciple, accompanying Sun everywhere he went.\n\nBecoming Commander-in-Chief of the Guangdong military government during Xinhai, Hu would oversee the first implementation of Dr. Sun's principles within the nation. Assisting Sun both in his Southern Revolutionary Governments, and in conducting the 1924 reorganisation, Hu would transform into the archon of the party's \

With extensive political experience and the backing of the National Revolutionary Army, Hu valiantly strides forward as Dr. Sun's orthodox successor.§!

Li Wenfan
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 20th, 1884 in Nanhai, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gElders Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA fervent democratic revolutionary, Li Wenfan would begin his republican career in 1905 as after studying in Japan at his own expense the previous years, he would become a member of the Tongmenghui. Soon after, Wenfan would return to China to serve as a teacher at the Guangdong School of Law and Politics whilst simultaneously leading the Guangdong branch of Tongmenghui operations, even participating in the short Second Guangzhou Uprising.\n\nIn the aftermath of Xinhai, Li became the Secretary-General of the Guangdong Provincial Department of Military Affairs, and active opposed Yuan Shikai's failed monarchy attempt, participating in the National Protection War. By September 1924, Li had been named director of the Guangdong Provincial Department of Governmental Affairs under Hu Hanmin, later on serving as secretary-general of the Nationalist government. A steadfast ally and friend of Hu Hanmin, Li Wenfan is seen as a protégé of sorts, and a key figure within the Elders Clique.§!
Yu Youren
§YBorn:§! §LApril 11th, 1879 in Sanyuan, Shaanxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gElders Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA famed calligrapher, writer and devout republican, Yu Youren would start his early years studying at various institutions: Sanyuan Hongdao Academy, Jingyang Wei Jing Academy and Xi'an Guanzhong Academy. Ultimately resulting in Youren's selection as a scholar at the age of 17, and later achieving the Juren status at the age of 23. In 1904 Youren published the 'Half Crying and Half Laughing Lou Poems', ridiculing the current state of the Great Qing, resulting in a bounty placed by the Qing authorities. Upon a trip to Japan in 1906 Youren came across Dr. Sun Yat-sen, subsequently joining both the Guangfuhui and later, the Tongmenghui.\n\nUpon his return to China, Youren founded multiple journalistic agencies intent on publicising anti-Qing sentiment. After the Xinhai revolution, Youren briefly served a tenure as Deputy Minister of Transportation for Dr. Sun's provisional government, and followed him into exile the following year. Youren later returned to his home province in 1918, serving as commander-in-chief of the Jingguo Army, contending with the warlords of the region for many years. Founding Shanghai University in 1922, Youren would later attend the First National Congress of the Kuomintang in 1924 and promptly accompany Sun Yat-sen north to Beijing.\n\nUpon the eve of the failed Northern Expedition, Youren would attempt to rally the Northern Kuomintang and Feng Yuxiang's Guominjun to support the Southern Kuomintang's advance but to little effect. Whilst not particularly affiliated with any faction, Youren most closely aligns with the orthodox Elders Clique but remains a neutral figure.§!\n\n§YNotes: A master of the cursive script, Youren is known as the \
Gu Yingfen
Born into both wealth and education, a young Gu Yingfen would quickly befriend his fellow compatriots sent to study in Japan, Hu Hanmin and Wang Jingwei. From there Gu Yingfen would live a life devoted to the Tongmenghui and later the Kuomintang, becoming an integral part in the organisation of both the Xinhai and Second Revolution of 1911 and 1913, the failure of the latter landing him in exile. Endeavouring to continue his efforts, Gu would play a critical role in fundraising for the Party within Southeast Asia.\n\nAfter returning home in 1917, Gu would take it upon himself to try and reconcile the rapidly deteriorating relationship between Dr. Sun Yat-sen and Chen Jiongming. His efforts were in vain, and he would eventually stay loyal to Dr. Sun and against Chen Jiongming. From there Gu would serve in various financial offices of the KMT Government, up until the failure of the Northern Expedition upon which he once again retreated into obscurity acting as the financial backer of the remnant of the Kuomintang.\n\nAs one of the Kuomintang's most elder members, Gu Yingfen is a strong proponent of destroying intra-party factionalism but is also keen in sharing his disdain for the Leftist committee. Orthodox in approach, Gu finds himself disdainful of the Left's populist rhetoric. Similarly, Gu has played a significant part in ensuring Hu Hanmin's return to China, as he has extensive ties and a mentor relationship with Chen Jitang.

Ma Chaojun
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 17th, 1886 in Guangzhou, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gElders Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a rather downtrodden family, Ma Chaojun would seek advancement in Chinese society by studying to become a Scholar-Bureaucrat, passing the children's exam. However in a change of pace, at the age of 15 he would move to Hong Kong, attending a night school to learn English, and in the following year he would move to the United States, studying at a machinery school in San Francisco.\n\nDuring his tenure in the United States, he would join both the Chinese Federalist movement and later, after meeting Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Tongmenghui. Following Dr. Sun to Japan, and then to Hong Kong, Ma Chaojun would use his background in Mechanical Engineering to found the Chinese Machinery Union, and various other localised trade union organisations.\n\nSeeing service as a diplomat in the Xinhai revolution, where he successfully convinced the Hubei provincial army to switch sides to the revolution, Ma Chaojun would serve as Li Yuanhong's advisor, yet would later be arrested due to his opposition to Yuan Shikai. Following his escape from prison with the assistance of revolutionaries, Ma Chaojun would serve in Dr. Sun's 1917 Guangzhou government, in which he would oversee the organisation of the labour movement. Serving in various capacities in relation to coordination between workers and government.\n\nIn opposition towards various leftist figures such as Chen Mingshu, and supportive of individuals like Sun Fo and Hu Hanmin, Ma Chaojun would follow Hu Hanmin and his Committee into exile within Moscow. Solidifying his position as an efficient labour manager during his tenure within Dr. Sun's government, he has once again returned to the role of labour coordination, ensuring that the various unions within China fully support the Kuomintang and its war effort.§!
Chen Jitang
Born to a family that had been farming for generations, Chen Jitang would receive what was considered to be a traditional Confucian education at a young age. In 1907, he would be admitted to the Guangdong Army Primary School at the age of 17, beginning his journey navigating the world of military policy. During his tenure at the school, one of the instructors — Deng Zhongyuan — would introduce Chen and his classmate — the renowned Deng Yanda — to the revolutionary politics of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Tongmenghui.\n\nBeing embroiled in revolutionary politics from that point onwards, Chen would see action in the Xinhai Revolution, and later would find himself under the command of Lin Hu, receiving a promotion from company commander to battalion commander. In 1920, Chen would be transferred to the new First Division of the Guangdong Army, however following Chen Jiongming's betrayal of Dr. Sun, Chen's immediate superior, Chen Mingshu, would resign and so Chen Jitang would be promoted to take his place.\n\nConsidering himself to be a \

Chen Weizhou
§YBorn:§! §L1888, in Fangchenggang, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gNew Guangdong Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA Guangdong native through-and-through, Cheng Weizhou would accompany his brother - Chen Jitang - in his various positions within various armies, always serving in minor assisted roles or delegated to tasks by his brother. Whilst nominally a member of the Kuomintang, his true loyalties lie with that of his home province, and so when the Northern Expedition dawned Chen Weizhou chose to stay put with his brother, assisting him in fighting off the remnants of Chen Jiongming's Guangdong Army and the later desperate last stand of the Fourth Army against the German onslaught. Having followed Chen Jitang in reconciling with Chen Lianbo, he has acquired a swath of influence governing the rivers and coastline of Guangdong, functioning as Chen Jitang's naval asset.§!\n\n§YNotes: A fairly self-serving man, and apolitical at heart, Chen Weizhou has received numerous accusations of corruption and charges of smuggling from the more noble individuals in Guangdong, and his capability of naval warfare leaves much to be desired. Despite this, Chen Jitang continues to protect his brother, and will do so until physically incapable.§!
Huang Guangrui
§YBorn:§! §LJune 5th, 1898, in Taishan, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gNew Guangdong Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to an overseas Chinese family, Huang Guangrui was almost immediately whisked away to the United States at a young age. During his tenure in the States, he enrolled in the American Flight School - founded by fellow overseas Chinese Cai Sidu - acquiring a U.S. pilot's license. In 1917, on the recommendation of the American branch of the Kuomintang, Huang Guangrui further enlisted in the Guoqiang Aircraft Company and later joined the Kuomintang that same year.\n\nIn 1921 he concluded his training by entering the Northern California Flight School, and in the following year he accompanied a selection of overseas Chinese pilot trainees to return to Guangzhou with several aircraft to join the burgeoning Kuomintang air force. Throughout his daring service, he served as captain of the First Air Force of the Grand Marshal's Office and participated in vanquishing Chen Jiongming's rebellion against Dr. Sun, personally flying a multitude of missions against Federalist forces.\n\nIn the following years he served as both director of the base camp aviation bureau, flight instructor of the Central Aviation School and later principal of the same institution. Due to the upcoming Northern Expedition, in 1926 he was sent to Russia to purchase aircraft and study at the aviation schools there.\n\nHe later returned to China to serve in the Northern Expedition as the captain of the 1st Battalion of the Guangdong Air Force. Following the collapse of the Northern Expedition, Huang Guangrui would follow Chen Jitang to Guangdong to serve under the new Yue government, working to aid the New Guangdong air force - having now become a half-hearted ally of Chen.§!
Fan Hanjie
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 29th, 1894, in Dabu, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gNew Guangdong Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA capable commander from a young age, Fan Hanjie would study at Guangzhou Polytechnic School and Guangdong Surveying and Mapping School, later enlisting in Chen Jiongming's Guangdong Army, serving as platoon leader, company commander, major staff officer and battalion commander. In 1918 Fan Hanjie would serve as military commissar of the General Headquarters of the Guangdong Army - at this time developing an excellent relationship with the director of the depot, Chiang Kai-shek. Joining the fight against Chen Jiongming's rebellion in 1923, he would serve as senior staff officer for Liu Zhenhuan's Guangxi army, commander of the Sixth Route army and later even county magistrate of Sanshui County.\n\nIn 1924 at the recommendation of Liu Zhenhuan and Zou Lu, Fan Hanjie applied for Whampoa Military Academy entering the fourth team of the first phase of the school, being the only cadet in the first phase to reach the rank of major general. Having achieved great success in Whampoa academy, Fan Hanjie would go on to serve as major staff officer of the First Division of the Guangdong Army.\n\nParticipating in the Northern Expedition, Fan Hanjie would excel in a multitude of battles despite the odds - even making connections with fellow generals Chen Mingshu and Jiang Guangnai. However as the German advance thundered forwards, Fan Hanjie would follow Chen Jitang back to Guangdong - and as a military man at heart - providing his expertise to the various army reforms Chen Jitang undertook.\n\nWhilst lacking nominal experience in leading troops in the new age, Fan Hanjie has displayed daring tenacity and excellent potential in the face of superior foes, and knows exactly how to extract the most out of his men in any given situation.§!
Li Yangjing
§YBorn:§! §LMarch 11th, 1894, in Dongguan, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gNew Guangdong Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LHailing from a poor family, diligent Li Yangjing graduated from the Army Primary School in Huangpu, where he met his lifelong friend Chen Jitang. After studying infantry and serving briefly as a junior officer in the Guangdong Army, he went to Wuchang and joined the Tongmenghui in 1914, and he took part in the uprising in Nanchang during the National Protection War against Yuan Shikai. Before starting his Sixth-form studies at Peking University in 1919, he studied logistics for two years in the 6th Class of Baoding Military Academy in 1917.\n\nLi Yangjing returned to his home province as a staff officer with the rank of major and became a commander of Dr. Sun's regimental guards in 1921. A year later, when Chen Jiongming bombarded and besieged Dr. Sun's revolutionary headquarters and his presidency, Li Yangjing, who personally escorted Madame Sun (Song Qingling) and fought their way out of the revolt, was injured in battle and had to recuperate in Hong Kong for years.\n\nThis brave and well-trained soldier would pick up his military career again when Li's friend, Chen Jitang became the commander of the 11th Division of the NRA in 1925 as Li was appointed as his chief of staff with the rank of colonel. Although Chen's division stayed in Guangdong during the Northern Expedition, Li would still fight a series of hopeless battles when the German forces landed in China. Afterwards, Li Yangjing would follow Chen Jitang and assist him in taking care of military affairs. As a longtime follower and friend of Chen, Li will always obey and support his orders.§!
Yu Hanmou
§YBorn:§! §LSeptember 22nd, 1896, in Gaoyao, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gNew Guangdong Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a downtrodden salt merchant family, Yu Hanmou would finish rudimentary schooling at the age of 14, and enter Guangzhou Army Primary School in 1910, continuing to Baoding Army Officer School in 1916. During his time in Baoding, Yu Hanmou would join the Kuomintang, and would later graduate in 1919. Serving in various capacities as an infantry officer, platoon commander and company commander in the Beiyang Army, Yu would transition to the Guangdong Army in 1920 as a battalion commander.\n\nFollowing the reorganisation of the Guangdong Army into the Fourth Army of the National Revolutionary Army, Yu would serve as the commander of the 31st Regiment of the 11th Division, with his direct superior being Chen Jitang, forging a lifelong association. Participating in the Yue-Gui wars, Yu would experience his true baptism in the fires of war upon the execution of the doomed Northern Expedition, fighting valiantly yet ultimately in a doomed effort.\n\nWith the Kuomintang crumbling, and splitting off into various disparate insurgencies, Yu would continue to faithfully follow his fellow New Fourth Army officers Fan Hanjie and Chen Jitang into Guangdong, ultimately positioning themselves as Guangdong regionalists first, Kuomintang Revolutionaries second.§!
Li Zongren
Li Zongren is one of the National Revolutionary Army's most competent and skilled military leaders, and yet his humble beginnings would betray such a concept. Born to a poor farming family in rural Guangxi, Li would enrol in a variety of military schools, in which he would meet his lifelong comrades Bai Chongxi, and Huang Shaohong. On the eve of the Xinhai Revolution, Li would be enticed by the ideals of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Tongmenghui, and join them in the year 1910.\n\nLater enrolling in the Guilin Military Cadre Training School, in which he would be taught by the renowned Cai E, and in the year 1916, Li would enlist as a platoon commander in Lu Rongting's Guangxi Army, gaining prominence and fame serving as a lieutenant under Lin Hu and Ma Ji.\n\nFollowing Lu Rongting's deposition in 1921, Li would become a minor local warlord, reuniting with Huang Shaohong, and forming an alliance. Keen to surpass being a mere bandit of chance, Li's ambition would lead to him consolidating his influence within Guangxi, reconnecting with Bai Chongxi and aligning himself with Dr. Sun's Kuomintang movement upon their establishment in Guangdong.\n\nWith Lu Rongting's second ousting, and the occupation of Nanning by Li's forces, Sun would recognise Li's newly inundated New Guangxi clique as the rightful governors of Guangxi. Applying his full force behind the Kuomintang movement — despite his lack of true understanding behind the Three Principles — Li would serve with distinction in the doomed Northern Expedition, notably defeating the Jade Marshal on the battlefield, however following the stalling of the expedition, Li and the KMT would be forced into disparate KMT armies, leading insurgencies within MinGan and Guizhou.
§YBorn:§! §LAugust 13th, 1890, in Guilin, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$GXC_li_zongren_bio$§!

Huang Shaohong
Born to a notable noble family within his home-town village, Huang Shaohong received a personal education designed by his former Qing Juren father, Huang Yuliang. Receiving an incredibly gentle upbringing, he ended up developing a quite fierce, brave and authoritative personality. With a revolutionary mindset already developing, when the news of the martyrs of the Guangzhou Uprising reached Huang's ears, he sprung into action developing an arms smuggling operation - with future New Guangxi member Xia Wei - to aid the revolutionaries but was halted by his father, fearing Central Government reprisals on his own son.\n\nFollowing the upheaval of the Xinhai revolution, Huang Shaohong would enlist in Baoding Military Academy in 1915, graduating and returning to Guangxi the following year. Garnering a plethora of experience serving as a commander in Lu Rongting's Guangxi Army and local warlord, he would develop an almost sibling-like relationship with fellow Guangxi leaders Bai Chongxi and Li Zongren, to the point that he would describe Li as \

Huang Xuchu
§YBorn:§! §L1892, in Rong, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §PNew Guangxi Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LComing from a scholar's family much like other New Guangxi leaders, Huang Xuchu opted for the inglorious life of a soldier. Graduating from the fourth batch of students in the Beijing Army University, he would return home to Guangxi to serve in various local warlord armies finally ending up in the command of Li Zongren's Guangxi army. After the incorporation of the Guangxi army into the National Revolutionary Army, he would see service in the Northern Expedition as a brigade commander, division commander and deputy army commander.\n\nA trusted and appreciated affiliate of Li Zongren, he would follow the rest of the New Guangxi Clique into Yunnan and would utilise his penchant for organisation and administration to aid Huang Shaohong in acting as the civilian wing of the New Guangxi Clique. A skilled prodigy and respected commander, some within the clique believe that Huang Xuchu acts as the unofficial fourth member of the Triumvirate, with his opinions highly valued. Albeit the clashing roles of both Huang Shaohong and Huang Xuchu serves to develop tension within the clique, with Huang Shaohong fighting to remain the military quartermaster of the clique.§!
Bai Chongxi
§YBorn:§! §LMarch 18th, 1893, in Guilin, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §PNew Guangxi Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a Hui Muslim family of Persian descent within rural Guangxi, Bai would enlist into the Guangxi Military Cadre Training School in Guilin, to be tutored by Cai E himself. During his tenure, Bai would meet his lifelong comrades of Huang Shaohong and Li Zongren, crafting an unbreakable bond. With the outbreak of the Xinhai revolution in 1911, Bai and Huang would enlist in a Students Dare to Die corps led by Zhao Hengti to fight in the revolution. Following a series of various enrolments in military preparatory schools, Bai would attend the third class of Baoding Military Academy in 1915, and after graduation, would find himself serving under Lu Rongting's Guangxi army.\n\nAfter an injury sustained in combat, Bai would find himself in Guangzhou at the same time as Kuomintang leader Dr. Sun Yat-sen, and with his connections to Huang Shaohong, appealed to Sun to launch a final expedition to secure Guangxi for the National Revolution. With such backing, Bai and Huang — later adjourned by Li Zongren — would rise to power within Guangxi province, defending it against incursions from minor warlords and Tang Jiyao alike.\n\nFormerly joining the National Revolutionary Army in 1926, Bai would serve as deputy chief of staff, and chief of the general staff for the 7th army, aiding in Li Zongren's defeat of Wu Peifu within Hunan during the Northern Expedition. However with the collapse of the Northern Expedition, Bai would find himself following the 7th Army and New Guangxi Clique to Guizhou. Not one to sit idly by, Bai Chongxi continued to hone his skills on the battlefield, becoming one of the NRA's brightest tactical geniuses, and even pioneering the Guangxi Militia system alongside Li Zongren and Huang Shaohong. Xia Wei

At only 18, he would join the Guilin Student Army Death Squadron - alongside fellow native Huang Shaohong - to aid in the success of the revolt against Qing rule. Once things had settled, he enlisted in the Baoding Army Officer School, graduating within a year and being assigned to the First Division of the Guangxi Army by the Beiyang Government.\n\nIn 1917 he was transferred to the Model Army Battalion - alongside fellow future New Guangxi members Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi and Huang Shaohong - participating in the National Protection War against Yuan Shikai. Garnering invaluable commanding experience in the years that followed, Xia Wei would follow the other members of the Guangxi Army in being integrated into the National Revolutionary Army. Lin Sen
A Republican since the turn of the century, Lin Sen has seen a lot happen in his lifetime. Fighting in the Sino-Japanese War, Lin would continue to organise resistance in Taiwan, inflicting heavy casualties on the Japanese. He would escape to the mainland, joining the Xingzhonghui. Meeting Dr. Sun in 1899, Lin would found the Fujian Xingzhonghui branch. With the founding of the Tongmenghui, Lin would lead all of his followers to join. Persuading Xu Chongzhi to join the revolutionary's ranks, Lin would work to launch the Jiujiang Uprising in solidarity with Xinhai.\n\nElected Chairman of the Provisional Senate, and helping draft the Provisional Constitution, Lin would ultimately resign in face of Yuan Shikai's abuses, constructing the Fujian branch of the Kuomintang. Joining the Gemingdang in Japan, Lin would be sent to America to help fundraise. Returning to China in 1916, Lin would return to collaborate with Zhang Ji and Ju Zheng to establish the Constitutional Club.\n\nFollowing Sun to his Constitutional Protection Government, Lin would become Speaker of the Extraordinary Assembly, and later acting Foreign Affairs Minister. Later Lin would be elected Chairman of the Assembly. Deeply trusted by Sun, Lin would briefly become Governor of Fujian Province. Being a leading architect in the Reorganisation, Lin would lead its implementation with Hu and Wang. However he detested Sun's Pro-International, Pro-CSP and Pro-Populist turn, and would host the Xishan conference with Zou Lu and others; forming the Western Hills Clique.\n\nAnd yet as the hammer of the warlords arrived Lin would flee the nation, having his safety and transport secured by Hu Hanmin's rival Central Executive Committee in Moscow. A veteran, devout upholder of justice, and above all else humble, it would appear that Lin's trials are not over, and yet his heart forever remains with the people.\n\n§YNotes: Lin is reputed for his homely, down to earth demeanour, choosing to live a simple life, shying away from excess.§!

Ju Zheng
A chivalrous man in his youth, Yang Jun — or as he is now called Ju Zheng — would begin his revolutionary career joining the Tongmenghui. Ju would ultimately prepare to join the Hekou Uprising in Yunnan, unfortunately learning that the uprising had failed without him. Travelling to Singapore to meet Dr. Sun Yat-sen, he would run Zhongxing Daily with Hu Hanmin and Wang Jingwei. Becoming head of the Hubei Tongmenghui in 1910, Ju would go on leave to finance a future uprising just to return to Hubei to find that Xinhai had already started without him.\n\nFighting in the Second Revolution, Ju would help form the Gemingdang in 1914, and would return to the National Assembly in 1917 to serve as Senator for Hubei. Aiding in the formation of the Kuomintang, Ju would serve as senator of Sun's Presidential Palace; then as Minister of the Interior. However during the 1924 Reorganisation of the Party, Ju was a privately outspoken critic of cooperation with the Chinese Syndicalist Party, yet he did not act due to his blood oath to Sun.\n\nAfter Sun passed away, Ju would travel to Beijing to first pay his respects, and second, to organise the Xishan Conference with Lin Sen, Zou Lu and others. Ultimately becoming a core member of the Western Hills Clique. Expelled from the party in 1926 for his actions, Ju would have his membership restored in 1927 due to the influence of Cheng Qian. Following the Northern Expedition, Ju opted to instead travel to Moscow rather than live in the squalor of Guizhou, or the corrupt hive of Shanghai. Travelling alongside Lin Sen, the two would be elected to Hu Hanmin's rival Central Executive Committee.\n\nA notable proponent of the primacy of law and orthodoxy, Ju has seen himself commonly serve as a mediator between Kuomintang internal factions. Make no mistake, whilst Ju may be a \

Zou Lu
§YBorn:§! §L1885, in Chaozhou, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cWestern Hills Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LPolitician, Composer, Calligrapher, Statesman, Teacher, to call Zou Lu a man of many talents would be an understatement. Believing from a young age that only revolution as advocated by Dr. Sun could be the salvation of the nation, Zou would ultimately join the Xingzhonghui in 1900, and the Tongmenghui in 1905. Entering law school that same year, he would become close friends with one Chen Jiongming, and the two would work closely as fellow revolutionaries for a decade. Instigating the Shantou Uprising in 1910 on behalf of the revolutionaries, Zou's uprising would meld into the Xinhai Revolution.\n\nAssisting Chen during the Second Revolution, Zou would travel to Japan in light of its failure and organise the Gemingdang with Sun and Hu Hanmin. Zou would see himself appointed in various military staff capacities before ultimately becoming Special Commissioner in charge of leading the suppression of his dear friend Chen in 1922. Becoming Minister of Finance, Zou would also be made President of the newly created National Guangdong University, even writing the school's song. Agreeing with the necessity for the 1924 Reorganisation, but disagreeing with the United Front Policy, Zou would remain in silent opposition due to respect for Sun.\n\nFollowing the rapid deterioration of Sun's health in Beijing however, Zou would uproot himself and rush to the Guofu to sign his will. And in the following year would collaborate with Lin Sen and Ju Zheng, amongst others, to hold the Xishan Conference. Denouncing cooperation with the International, Populism and the United Front Policy with the Chinese Syndicalist Party, Zou would ultimately be purged by the Central Committee.\n\nNoticing which way the wind was blowing, Zou would flee China as the Northern Expedition collapsed, regrouping with Hu Hanmin and his exiled Elders Clique in Moscow. During his exile he was a major force in shaping the curriculum of the Sun Yat-sen University in Moscow, serving as its President. A close friend of Hu, and skilled not only in the arts but also in military affairs and economic management, Zou is a force to be reckoned with.§!
Xu Chongzhi
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 14th, 1887, in Panyu, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cWestern Hills Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LLosing both his parents at a young age, Xu Chongzhi would nonetheless serve as the chief instructor of Fujian Military Academy. Participating in Li Liejun's Second Revolution, Xu would join the Gemingdang in 1913, meeting the likes of Chiang Kai-shek, Ju Zheng, Chen Qimei, Yu Youren and Hu Hanmin. Fighting alongside Ju, he would become a sworn brother of Chiang and serve as Sun's Chief of Staff and Chief of Army in 1917. Leader of the Second Guangdong Army alongside Chen Jiongming's first, Xu would defend Guangdong against Lu Rongting and Mo Rongxin's, ejecting them from the province in 1920. Further working to quell Old Guangxi's ambitions, Xu would support Sun to launch the Northern Expedition, yet with Chen Jiongming's betrayal in 1922, Xu would have to halt his advance in Jiangxi and return to Guangdong.\n\nSeeing service in both Yue-Gui Wars, Xu was supportive of the Reorganisation and United Front policy. Placing Chiang as Principal of Whampoa, Xu would become Minister of Military Affairs in the wake of Sun's demise. Unfortunately with the attempted assassination of Liao Zhongkai, Xu would become isolated by Wang Jingwei and Chiang. With Hu Hanmin's informal exile from China, Xu would be forcefully restrained in his own home by Chiang's Whampoa Cadets, and forced to resign. Exiled to Shanghai in a rather lavish house in the British Concession, Xu would engage in a rapport with Zhang Ji, attempting to make a political comeback under the Western Hills banner. Following the Northern Expedition's demise, Xu would extradite himself and his belongings to Moscow at the suggestion of Zhang, joining Hu's rival Central Executive Committee.§!\n\n§YNotes: Xu once received handwritten calligraphy from Sun: \
Li Liejun
§YBorn:§! §LFebruary 23rd, 1882, in Nanching, Jiangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cWestern Hills Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LPerhaps one of China's most devout, ardent, and infamous revolutionary figures. Li Liejun's name is much renowned in Southern Revolutionary circles, and much despised in the North. Practicing martial arts at a young age, Li would be selected amongst the likes of Ouyang Wu to travel to Japan to study. Aiming for artillery at the Shinbu Gakko, Li would enter the Japanese Army Noncommissioned Officer School. Befriending Yan Xishan, Li Genyuan, Tang Jiyao, Sun Chuanfang and Cheng Qian, Li would become enamoured in the Tongmenghui movement believing wholeheartedly that China's salvation lied in revolution.\n\nTravelling to Kunming to serve as a military instructor thanks to Feng Guozhang, Li would aid in spreading revolutionary sentiment within the academy. To the point where he was even reassigned elsewhere due to becoming too overt for even Li Genyuan to cover for him. Immediately springing into action in the Xinhai Revolution would hold off Feng Guozhang from advancing down the Yangtze.\n\nGovernor of Jiangxi in 1912, he would rebel against Yuan Shikai with the rest of the Kuomintang in 1913. Perhaps his most striking moment would be his part in the organisation of the National Protection War. Cooperating with Cai E, Li would drive Tang Jiyao to waging their patriotic war. Commanding the Second Army of the Huguojun, Li would clamour for the army to march all the way to Beijing. Leader of the Yunnan Army in Guangdong, he would be an integral power player in the politics of the region, ultimately remaining with Dr. Sun Yat-sen. Liang Hancao
§YBorn:§! §LJuly 19th, 1899, in Sanshui, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §lReconstruction Faction§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA gifted academic, the young Liang Hancao's life is filled with an eager hunger for learning: learning to read at the age of four, write at the age of 6, admitted to Zhaoqing Prefecture Middle School at age 12, ranking first in every exam for his tenure. Upon his father's death at 16, he started his career in education serving as a teacher in Jiangmen Mingde Primary School.\n\nHowever this was not enough for him, as in 1918 he enlisted in Shanghai Hujiang University, graduating in 1923 and finally putting his hat into the revolutionary fray serving as a secretary for Wang Jingwei. Later, in 1924, Liang Hancao was transferred to party secretary and youth department officer of the 4th District of Guangzhou, and later served as a teacher at Peizheng Middle School.\n\nIn 1925, Liang was once again recruited by Wang Jingwei into serving as a propagandist in the Secretariat of the National Government, and as a lecturer on the Three Principles at various influential institutions. Having become acquainted with Sun Fo's ideas through an introduction by Wang, Liang aligned himself closely with Sun Fo's steadfast support for democracy and anti-corruption.\n\nA keen legislator and intellectual, Liang can be regarded as Sun Fo's deputy, regrouping in Hawaii with the rest of the Reconstruction Faction.§!
Huang Hanliang
§YBorn:§! §L1893, in Xiamen, Fujian Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §lReconstruction Faction§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAn economically minded figure, Huang Hanliang begins his career entering Tsinghua University in 1911. Being one of the first students to receive the Boxer Indemnity Scholarship, Huang Hanliang was able to study at the University of Michigan, Princeton University and Columbia University.\n\nDuring his tenure in the United States, Huang Hanliang became closely acquainted with Sun Fo, beginning a lifelong friendship. After graduating from Columbia with a doctorate in philosophy, he returned to China to serve as president of the Hong Kong Branch of Ho-feng Bank, gaining experience in the banking and finance trade.\n\nUtilising his close friendship with Sun Fo, Huang provides his financial experience whenever the Reconstruction Faction requires it - albeit not without scrutiny and unpopularity from those outside the Crown Prince's circle.§!
Wu Chaoshu

With expenses paid for by the Qing, Wu was able to study in England, entering the University of London and graduating with a bachelor's degree in law, qualifying as a barrister later in 1911. Returning to what was now the Republic of China in 1912, he served as Director-General of the Foreign Affairs Department of Hubei, and Chairman of the Treaty Committee of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.\n\nIn 1913, Wu participated in the House of Representatives of Congress, and later served as a member of the Constitution Drafting Committee. In 1915, he once again acquired a position in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, albeit opposing Yuan Shikai's Imperial attempt and resigning soon after.\n\nParticipating in the Constitution Protection Movement, Wu later served as Deputy Minister of Foreign Affairs and Director of the General Affairs Department in Guangdong. During his tenure in Sun Yat-sen's government, Wu served as Foreign Affairs minister, member of the Guangzhou National Government, Chairman of the Guangzhou Municipal Committee among others, and within his extensive work in Canton he became closely associated with Sun Fo. Chen Mingshu
Born into a rural village in Guangdong, Chen would embark on his political and military career at the age of 17 in 1906, entering the Guangdong Army Primary School, and simultaneously joining Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Tongmenghui. Following the outbreak of the Xinhai Revolution, Chen would follow Song Jiaoren to Wuhan to participate in the revolution, becoming a member of the Second Death Squadron of the Central Committee.\n\nOnce again swept up in revolutionary fervour, Chen would see service in Li Yaohan's anti-Yuan Shikai army, albeit following their defeat by the Old Guangxi Clique, Chen's soldiers would fold into the command of Lin Hu. Utilising his connections, when Guangxi invaded Guangdong in 1920, Chen would gather the remnants of Li Yaohan's army, mutiny against the Old Guangxi Clique, and later fold his troops into the Guangdong Provincial Army.\n\nAfter Chen Jiongming's betrayal of Dr. Sun, Chen would resign from military service, and travel to Nanjing to study Buddhism, however following the re-establishment of Nationalist rule in 1924, Chen Mingshu was personally recruited by the esteemed Deng Yanda to return to Guangdong and offer his services once more. Chen would be organised into the Fourth Army of the National Revolutionary Army under the command of Li Jishen, becoming the commander of the 10th Division.\n\nSeeing amicable service in the Northern Expedition, Chen would have to witness the disintegration of his Fourth Army under the pressures of the German and Warlord forces, and join his men in forming the backbone of the MinGan Insurgency. Cooperating with the likes of Deng Yanda, Li Jishen and Song Qingling during his time in MinGan, Chen is thoroughly in the camp of the Provisional Action Committee.
