Jiang Guangnai
§YBorn:§! §LDecember 17th, 1888, in Dongguan, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SProvisional Action Committee§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a reasonably stable family environment in urban Guangdong, Jiang Guangnai would be destined to serve in the military, being admitted to Guangdong Army Primary School in Huangpu, and later radicalising in the Xinhai Revolution. In 1912, he was selected by Baoding Military Academy to attend there due to his impressive military merit, and would graduate from the first cavalry department in 1913.\n\nFinding himself once again in the service of revolutionaries, Jiang would join the First Division of the Guangdong Army, later reorganised into the renowned Fourth Army of the National Revolutionary Army, under the auspices of Li Jishen. Being attached to the 10th Division as deputy division commander, Jiang would begin his lifelong association and friendship with the 10th Division's commander, Chen Mingshu, forging a bond in blood and the fires of the Northern Expedition.\n\nServing amicably in the ill-fated endeavour, Jiang Guangnai would follow Chen and the likes of Cai Tingkai into the MinGan Insurgency zone as the Fourth Army disintegrated, biding their time to return to national prominence at the slightest hint of Zhili weakness. Dutiful and loyal, Jiang is much relied upon by Chen in all matters ranging from politics to field command.§!
Cai Tingkai
§YBorn:§! §LApril 15th, 1892, in Luoding, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SProvisional Action Committee§!\n§YBackground:§! §LGraduating from Baoding Army Officer School, and joining the Tongmenghui at a fairly young age, Cai Tingkai would find himself serving as a police officer in Dapeng District, wherein he would be introduced to Dr. Sun Yat-sen, formerly joining the Guangdong Army during the Xinhai revolution, becoming a company commander at the age of 19. Following his service in the Yue-Gui wars, Cai would distinguish himself for peerless divisional leadership, and would be attached to the First Division of the Guangdong Army.\n\nLater remaining in his post during its reorganisation into the famed Fourth Army of the National Revolutionary Army, toting the likes of Deng Yanda, Li Jishen, and his esteemed friend Chen Mingshu, who would serve as his commander in battle, alongside the likes of Jiang Guangnai.\n\nOnce again displaying his pure potential and talent on the battlefield during the Northern Expedition, Cai would follow his commander and various other Kuomintang figures into the MinGan Insurgency zone due to the Fourth Army's splintering, with the intent to wage a guerilla war in the hopes of returning to the national stage. Earning his stripes in MinGan, Cai has distinguished himself as Chen Mingshu's most skilled subordinate, and has won praise from Cadre and Peasant alike.§!
Dai Ji
§YBorn:§! §L1895, in Suzhou, Jiangsu Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SProvisional Action Committee§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to poverty and losing his parents as a kid, Dai Ji worked as an apprentice in a store and lived a tough childhood as he was often abused by the store owner. He later joined the student army in Shanghai when he was 15 for this reason.\n\nIn 1914, Dai Ji enrolled in the 3rd class of the Baoding Military Academy and studied infantry for two years. After graduating, he served as a junior officer in Anhui until he was influenced by the revolutionary spirit during the National Protection War and joined the Yunnan Army. Joinined the Guangdong Army later, Dai rose from a platoon commander to a deputy regimental commanderand served briefly as a military tutor. Later, when the National Revolutionary Army was formed in Guangdong, Dai was appointed as the commander of the 30th regiment of the 10th Division, serving together with Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai under Chen Mingshu.\n\nDuring the Northern Expedition, after Hunan was captured by the NRA, Dai and his troops advanced towards Wuhan. In August 1926, Dai Ji led the assault and fought with his soldiers in the forefront of Dingsiqiao, a strategically critical town with heavy Zhili defences and was severely wounded. As the Northern Expedition ended catastrophically in the spring of 1927, disillusioned by the reality, Dai Ji resigned and resided in Shanghai to recuperate.\n\nIn 1928, Chen Mingshu invited Dai to serve under him with his old comrades in Guangdong again. Dai Ji accepted and returned as Chen's staff, tutor of the officer corps and a divisional commander. Since then, Dai has been a trusted and reliable subordinate of Chen, assisting him in building up his forces.§!\n\n§YNotes: Dai Ji is always the first to be at the forefront, regardless of how fierce the enemy's firepower is. He is also a faithful follower of Chen Mingshu and will stand by him in all circumstances.§!
Tan Pingshan
Born to a tailor's family, Tan Pingshan was admitted to Guangzhou and Guangxi Normal School, and later Leizhou Middle School, where he first entered the fray of radical politics through joining Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Tongmenghui in 1907. During his tenure at Peking University, he participated in the burgeoning November 4th Movement, even committing vandalism and arson against government officials, later being one of 32 arrested for such acts.\n\nAfter his release from prison, Tan would return to his native Guangdong, and later aid in the founding of the Chinese Syndicalist Party in 1921, serving as Secretary of the Guangdong Branch. Concrete in his resolve that syndicalism was the way forward for the Chinese citizenry, the failure of the Northern Expedition would lead to a shattering of his dreams for progress in China, and force him into hiding.\n\nAligning himself with the MinGan insurgents and the Provisional Action Committee, Tan would cast away his CSP membership in favour of the Kuomintang, albeit never truly fitting in with the main PAC membership, due to his preference to maintain open ties with the CSP, Tan's following are considered outcasts slumming it in Guangdong. With the resurgence of the Kuomintang within Guangdong, Tan has attached himself and his branch to the reasonably agreeable Chen Mingshu, bolstering his connections with Song Qingling and Deng Yanda, alongside that of his old friends in the CSP.

Ye Jianying
§YBorn:§! §LApril 28th, 1897, in Meixian, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RGuangdong Provisional Action§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a Hakka family that ran a small business in rural Guangdong, he would excel in his education at a young age. During his period at his new middle school, Ye would start pursuing various progressive literature, and serve as President of the Student Union, graduating in 1915. Later, in 1917, Ye would enlist in Yunnan Military Academy, graduating in 1920 and joining the Kuomintang the same year.\n\nParticipating in the Yue-Gui Wars, Ye would even personally escort Sun Yat-sen out of a firefight. Later, during the counter-attack against Chen Jiongming, Ye would achieve a great victory at Yanling Pass, achieving him much renown within the National Revolutionary Army, and due to his achievements against the Federalists, he was appointed Chief of Staff of the Second Guangdong Army, and later invited by Liao Zhongkai to participate in the founding of Whampoa. During his tenure as an instructor at Whampoa, he would be lured by the socialist ideals of his students, gradually converting to Syndicalism, and later, in 1925, applying for membership within the CSP, albeit his application was stalled due to his connections to Chiang Kai-shek.\n\nParticipating in the Northern Expedition under the 1st Army, participating in the additional organisation of strikes during the German occupation of Guangdong. With the shattering of the Expedition, Ye Jianying would follow Deng Yanda and Song Qingling into the MinGan insurgency, serving as a source of rapport between Tan Pingshan in Guangdong, the CSP and the PAC.§!

Huang Yong
§YBorn:§! §L1900, in Pingjiang, Hunan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RGuangdong Provisional Action§!\n§YBackground:§! §LWorking as an apprentice and policeman at a young age, Huang Yong would leave Guangzhou in 1918, entering a martial arts hall in 1922, and later the Whampoa Military Academy in 1924. Having joined the Kuomintang during his tenure at Whampoa, Huang would graduate in 1924, and immediately immerse himself in the leftist politics of the various peasant movements around Guangdong, yet ultimately finding the worker based politics of the recently founded Chinese Syndicalist Party to be most alluring, joining them in 1925.\n\nWith his membership, Huang Yong served as the special commissioner for Dongjiang and Qiongya, successfully organising a series of armed riots, even occupying Lufeng, establishing a commune and the Second Division of the Workers' and Peasants' Revolutionary Army. However his time in the CSP would not be forever, as following the Northern Expedition and the CSP's Internationale alignment, Huang would find himself drifting towards the dreams presented by Tan Pingshan's branch of the Provisional Action Committee, reigniting his Kuomintang membership.\n\nBelieving strongly in the concept that Chinese socialism should be of an independent strain, Huang Yong has taken quite strongly to Tan Pingshan's Third Force politics within China, and serves to enforce Tan's ideas with violence if necessary.\n\nWhilst not particularly experienced in large scale combat, Huang Yong has an endearing capacity to see the National Revolution through, and will fight back against capitalists, warlords and bandits alike.§!
Xiang Ying
§YBorn:§! §LMay 1898, in Wuchang, Hubei Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RGuangdong Provisional Action§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn Xiang Delong in a village close to Wuchang, Xiang's father moved the family into the city for his career in the county government. After attending Wuchang Yucai Primary School and Wuchang Private Rixin Middle School, Xiang became a textile apprentice at the age of 13. After his three years of apprenticeship, he would become a proper textile worker. Four years later, Xiang led a strike of cloth factory workers. The following year, Xiang established a railway workers' club in Jiang'an.\n\nIn April 1922, Xiang joined the nascent Chinese Syndicalist Party through an introduction by Bao Huisheng. In October of the same year, Xiang led a successful strike at the Yangtze River Machinery Factory. In 1923, following stalled negotiations with Wu Peifu, Li Dazhao directed Xiang to launch the Beijing-Hankou Railway Strike, which the Jade Marshal put down with military force. Continuing to grow in renown within the Syndicalist League, Xiang entered into the Kuomintang due to the United Front.\n\nStationed in Wuhan during the Northern Expedition, Xiang prepared for the National Revolutionary Army to enter the city, though Wu Peifu ultimately turned the Nationalists back. After the fall of the Guangzhou Nationalist Government, Xiang fled to Shanghai, where he continued conducting trade union activities on behalf of the National Revolution.\n\nXiang would become a leading figure in the Shanghai Uprising of 1932, and ended up in MinGan following the League crackdown. While operating in the Insurgency, Xiang drifted into orbit around Tan Pingshan, a Provisional Action Committee member with CSP ties. A dedicated revolutionary, Xiang continues to dream for a China where the chains on the proletariat are shattered.§!
Ye Jizhuang
§YBorn:§! §LMay 1898, in Wuchang, Hubei Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RGuangdong Provisional Action§!\n§YBackground:§! §LRaised by a wet nurse due to his mother's death from his birth, Ye went into education when he was 7. After graduating, he initially sought a judicial career before going into teaching. While teaching in Hong Kong, he founded a news agency and small daily newspaper. While serving as editor-in-chief, he used the pen name Ye Jingtian. In 1925, Ye was a participant in the Canton-Hong Kong General Strike, helping to mobilise and organise the masses in Jiangmen, establishing a general labour union and a strike committee, as well as leading workers in their struggle against excessive taxation.\n\nDue to his revolutionary activities, he was admitted into the Chinese Syndicalist Party. Through the United Front, the Kuomintang appointed him and Liang Xinzhi as preparatory committee members of the Kuomintang Xinxing County Party Headquarters. By 1926, Ye served as the secretary of the Jiangmen branch of the CSP. In Xinxing, Ye oversaw the liquidation of the gentry-controlled Xingxian society, organised workers' and peasants' armies, and established several schools. After the Northern Expedition failed, Ye fled to Macao, where he continued his revolutionary activities.\n\nMoving to Hong Kong after being unable to contact CSP leadership in Shanghai, Ye returned to teaching and leading the Hong Kong Little Daily, the official newspaper of the LCS. After being suppressed by the Hong Kong authorities, Ye was ordered by the CSP to oversee expansion of syndicalist militias in MinGan. After the 1932 Shanghai Uprising, Kuomintang insurgents surged in the area, and Ye worked closely with Tan Pingshan and the PAC. With Guangzhou reclaimed by the NRA, Ye returned home, hoping to establish a revolutionary China that fights for the workers and peasants.§!

Liu Shixin would carry his brother's fiery torch of anarchism as he was heavily influenced by his brother's thoughts. Deng Fa
§YBorn:§! §LMarch 7th, 1906, in Yunfu, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §rChinese Syndicalist Party - Orthodox§!\n§YBackground:§! §LEnrolling into education at the age of 6, Deng Fa's education would be relatively unassuming, studying at a variety of public and private institutions. Albeit, the outbreak of the November 4th Movement would move the young Deng into a radical direction, seeing his active participation in the movement. In 1921, he would drop out of schooling, and work various oddjobs until joining the labour movement under the stewardship of Su Zhaozheng.\n\nIn 1925, Deng Fa would join the Canton-Hong Kong strike, serving as a representative of the Striking Worker's Congress, the leader of the worker's picket team, and leader of the propaganda department. Being introduced to the Chinese Syndicalist Party by Su Zhaozheng later that year, he would join and serve as a branch organisation officer, and secretary of the party branch.\n\nIn 1926, Deng Fa would also join the Kuomintang, serving as captain of the Northern Expedition Youth Team, and participate in the fateful Northern Expedition. Following the disintegration of the expedition, Deng Fa would return to Guangzhou to assist the local labour movement there, working underground against the watchful eyes of business owners and Zhili alike.\n\nWith the resurgence of the socialists within his home province, Deng Fa has been emboldened to act in conjunction with other union leaders such as Deng Zhongxia and Zhang Tailei to champion the rights of the workers, serving as a champion of their plight.§!
Deng Zhongxia
Having a reasonably normal education as a child, Deng's first foray into revolutionary politics would be in 1917, where upon accompanying his father to Beijing, and studying philosophy at Peking University, he would be allured by Li Dazhao's Marxist leanings, and would assist in the initiation of the Marxist Research Group at the university, wherein Li was elected party secretary.\n\nFurther radicalising due to his participation in the November 4th Movement, Deng would go on to becoming a founding member of the Chinese Syndicalist Party, engaging in the local labour movement within Beijing and assisting in the establishment of a trade union there. Later, in 1922, Deng would be welcomed into the ranks of the leadership of the CSP, and would later join the Kuomintang during the First United front.\n\nWithin 1925, Deng would collaborate with the World Society alongside the CSP to unite all non-Kuomintang socialists into the League of Chinese Syndicalists, and the All-China Federation of Labour, and later in the same year, would join the likes of Su Zhaozheng in hosting the Canton-Hong Kong strike.\n\nFollowing the calamity of the Northern Expedition, Deng would retreat into the urban labyrinths of Guangdong, heralding the plight of the workers as the leader of the local CSP branch. A fierce union leader and labour organiser, Deng has long climbed the political ladder to extol the defence of the workers, and will continue to do so as long as he breathes.

Yan Hanzhang
§YBorn:§! §L1903, in Haifeng, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §rChinese Syndicalist Party - Orthodox§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBound to be swooped up in the revolutionary fervour of his home province, Yan Hanzhang first engaged in revolutionary thought in 1921, when at the age of 18 and studying at his hometown high school, he would come into frequent contact with his radical principal — a devout leftist sympathiser, assisting Peng Pai's peasant movement whilst also spreading revolutionary ideals amongst his students.\n\nBecoming even further entranced by the allure of socialism, he would join one of Peng Pai's peasant academies to receive guerilla training alongside revolutionary experience whilst studying socialist ideals. After the success of the Eastern Expedition against Chen Jiongming, Yan would embark on a series of trips to various rural villages in the aim of promoting socialist ideals and mobilising the peasantry for the class war, having successfully organised a peasant association numbering 50,000 men.\n\nHowever, the Kuomintang's Northern Expedition would fall, and with it Yan's belief in radical agrarian peasant socialism. Following the rank and file of the CSP into their various splintered exiles, Yan would slowly but surely cast away his youthful radical notion of immediate action, and fold into the orthodox syndicalist approach espoused by the likes of Chen Duxiu, seeking to achieve his desired libertarian socialist China through the CSP's two-step revolution, and thoroughly enforcing the Li-Lisan line to achieve that ideal.§!
Zeng Sheng
§YBorn:§! §LDecember 19th, 1910, in Huiyang, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RGuangdong Farmer's Association§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to an overseas Chinese father, and a Hakka mother, Zeng Sheng had a reasonably stable upbringing, starting his education at the age of 6, and finishing primary schooling at the age of 10, albeit due to the upheaval in Warlord Era China, Zeng had to utilised family connections to move to Hong Kong to continue his studies. However this would only seek to fuel Zeng's radicalisation, as his principal during secondary schooling was a devout conservative, rallying against Dr. Sun Yat-sen's National Revolution, and likewise, the inequality in brazenly open display throughout Hong Kong — where the native Chinese are frequently oppressed by foreigners, and where the wealthy exploit the poor — further contributed to Zeng's radicalisation.\n\nWith Zeng's father planning to return to his home country of Australia in 1922, Zeng accompanied him, although during the journey to the country, Zeng witnessed a myriad of various Chinese labourers smuggle themselves onto the boat in the hopes that their destination will yield greater opportunities for them. Greatly admonishing this, it would confirm to Zeng that China was in dire need of radical action in order to soothe the needs of the citizenry.\n\nReturning to China in 1928 with a desire to revive his country and nation, Zeng was too late to participate in the Kuomintang's doomed Northern Expedition, but not too late to offer his services to Peng Pai's Guangdong Farmer's Association, seeking to wage a guerilla war against the warlords and capitalists alike. With his recent promotion on the battlefield, Zeng's heart burns with the desire to aid Peng Pai in providing true liberation to the Chinese people, whatever form that may take.§!
Zhang Tailei

Peng Pai
Despite being born into an elite family of landowners and merchants, Peng Pai has sworn his life to the Chinese peasantry after his experiences in his studies in Japan, in which he witnessed the rice riots of 1918, alongside the failed Bolshevik Revolution, serving as inspirations for his move from reformist views to the socialist cause.\n\nPeng Pai succeeded in forming the Haifeng County Peasant Association, that was the first country wide association of peasants in China and then later in 1924 joined the Kuomintang, promoting cooperation with the Chinese Syndicalist Party. Peng would later help form the Peasant Movement Training Institute to further educate the rural masses.\n\nAfter the failed Northern Expedition, he would later set his base of operations in his home province of Guangdong, where he has become a fearful figure to people such as Chen Jiongming. Becoming not only just a political rival to the other people of the provinces, but a cult-like figure, creating an army of fanatics that seek to see China step into an era of Communism, forming what he sees as \

Hailing from a rural Hakka village, Gu lost his father as a kid. During his studies, Gu began to embrace socialist ideas. Despite having studied in the same school as Chen Jiongming and Zou Lu, Gu would pick a different path.\n\nWith Peng Pai created the first farmer association in 1922, similar organisations emerged across Guangdong, and Gu soon joined Peng's ranks. After graduating in the winter of 1924, Gu joined the campaign against Chen Jiongming, organising peasant forces. Tan Furen
§YBorn:§! §LApril 1st, 1910, in Renhua County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RGuangdong Farmer's Association§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn into a poor peasant family, his family was able to secure him an education. Entering into a private school at the age of 6, Tan's education concluded at the start of the Northern Expedition. With Guangdong home to various workers' and peasants' movements acting in tandem with the Kuomintang, Tan was swept up by the revolutionary fervour. Joining the Kuomintang, he began serving as a secretary of the district peasant association and conducted propaganda work.\n\nIn November of 1926, he entered the Jiangbei Peasant Army School, established by the Guangdong Provincial Peasant Association. In 1927, Tan briefly entered into He Long's forces but lost contact with the main force after Tang Shengzhi led them north. Unable to relink with He Long and Tang Shengzhi, Tan accidentally joined the National Revolutionary Forces in Jiangxi instead. When the Northern Expedition collapsed and Guangzhou fell to German soldiers, Tan and his forces continued operating in the MinGan region, where the local warlords could only maintain control in urban centres.\n\nAfter the 1932 Shanghai Uprising, more Kuomintang forces led by Deng Yanda joined up with the remnant National Revolutionary Armies. During this period, Tan worked with other Cantonese exiles, notably Peng Pai, Chen Mingshu, and Tan Pingshan. Following the Nationalist restoration in Guangzhou, Tan has continued to work closely with Peng Pai as a fervent believer in the peasant revolution of which Peng seeks.§!

Studying in a variety of military schools at a young age, joining the Tongmenghui in 1911, and finally graduating from Baoding together with his friends Bai Chongxi and Huang Shaohong, it was natural that he would find himself within the New Guangxi clique.\n\nYu Zuobai would participate in the National Protection Alliance's war against Yuan Shikai, and would later serve under Li Zongren and Huang Shaohong during the wars to unify Guangxi, seeing battle against Lu Rongting, Shen Hongying and even Chen Jiongming's forces. In 1926, he would assist Huang Shaohong in the management of the provincial government under the auspices of the Kuomintang, successfully implementing policies aligned with the Three Principles of the People.\n\nDuring the Northern Expedition, Yu — alongside his cousin Li Mingrui — would assist in the nation's workers and peasants movements, maintaining connections within the Chinese Syndicalist Party despite his New Guangxi allegiances.\n\nFollowing the other Guangxi leaders into exile within Guizhou in the fallout of the Northern Expedition, his socialist sympathies would garner much ire amongst his comrades in the \
Yang Yin
§YBorn:§! §L1892, in Xiangshan County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RGuangdong Farmer's Association§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAdmitted to the Sacred Heart College in Guangzhou in 1910, Yang Yin would cut his academic career short by joining the Tongmenghui in 1911 and participating in the Xinhai Revolution that same year. From 1917 he would serve as adjutant of the guard of Sun Yat-sen's military government in Guangzhou and concurrently as a staff officer of the Military Affairs Office of the Generalissimo's Office. In 1922 he would join the freshly inundated Chinese Syndicalist Party, and at the end of the same year he would be sent to France to study.\n\nAfter returning to China in 1923, he would engage in the workers' movement in Guangdong, serving as an executive member and secretary of the Fourth District Branch of the Kuomintang, and would travel across the province to further the needs of the workers' movement. Deeply tied to the local railway workers, he would establish the General Trade Union, and introduce the workers to the CSP.\n\nAttending the Fourth National Congress of the Chinese Syndicalist Party, he would serve as a consultant to the Guangzhou Office of the National Railway Federation of Trade Unions. Leading striking workers in Guangzhou and Hong Kong, he would become famous in the Guangdong-Hong Kong General Strike. Becoming a local CSP kingpin and ardent worker activist, Yang has worked with Peng Pai alongside Zhang Tailei extensively to forment socialist revolution in Guangdong.§!
Zheng Jiemin
An early Kuomintang revolutionary, Zheng Jiemin attended the second phase of Whampoa military academy before going to Sun Yat-sen University in Paris. The failure of the Northern Expedition meant it would be nearly a decade before he returned home, instead becoming a political officer under He Zhonghan during the exile. A member of the RACA and CRS, he found employment in the National Bureau of Investigation and Statistics (BIS), assigned the prestigious position of station chief for Guangdong. He is noted for his fondness for French trained officers, his ideological fanaticism, and his ruthless efficiency at intelligence work - embodying the two wings of the CRS.\n\nWith few friends in the Liangguang political establishment, he is tolerated at best by those in power. An independent actor and a conduit to the underworld, he might still find work yet.

Chen Jiongming
Originally a lawyer, Chen entered politics as a member of the brief Guangdong Provincial Assembly, formed in 1909. He quickly made a name for himself as a successful and enthusiastic, albeit radical, reformer, with his republican and anti-Qing leanings being an open secret to local officials.\n\nWhen the Xinhai Revolution began in 1911, Chen, as a member of the Revolutionary Alliance, became commander of the Guangdong Army and was instrumental in helping Sun Yat-sen of the KMT set up the Constitutional Protection Movement. However, the two men developed a fierce rivalry from ideological differences, which boiled over in 1922 when Chen revolted against Sun. The KMT's Central Committee never forgave Chen for his \
§YBorn:§! §LJanuary 18th, 1878, in Haifeng, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$GXC_chen_jiongming_bio$§!
§YBorn:§! §LJanuary 18th, 1878, in Haifeng, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §lPublic Interest Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$GXC_chen_jiongming_bio$§!\n\n§YNotes: As a founder of the PIP, Chen is considered by many to be the leader of the Federalist Movement.§!
Ye Ju
Ye Ju began his career graduating in the first class of Guangdong Military Academy. Pursuing a career in military education, Ye Ju would serve as a teacher at the academy, and the Law and Politics Academy. During Xinhai, he participated in the organisation of the Guangdong Northern Expedition Army, serving as chief of staff of its Third Mixed Brigade and later commander of the 1st Brigade of the 2nd Division.\n\nJoining Chen Jiongming in the aftermath of the 1913 Revolution, he and Chen would strike a lifelong friendship. Ye Ju followed Chen to Fujian and became his Chief of Staff during the Constitutional Protection Movement in 1918, and returned to Guangdong in 1920. In 1922 as Sun and Chen fell out, Ye commanded his forces to shell Sun's Presidential Palace. Earning Sun and the KMT's eternal hatred, Ye Ju participated in the various conflicts against the KMT for Chen, until they were defeated and forced into exile in Hong Kong.\n\nWhen the Northern Expedition began fracturing, Ye Ju retook Haifeng in the chaos, running it as his own fief. While coordinating with Chen Jiongming in Guangzhou, Ye Ju has established a small alliance network in Eastern Guangdong, and engages in limited cooperation with Chen Lianbo's Guangzhou forces.

Luo Xianxiang
§YBorn:§! §LAugust 5th, 1891, in Sihui County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LNeutral§!\n§YBackground:§! §LLuo Xianxiang began his military career upon graduating from Baoding Military Academy in 1916, joining the Guangdong Army. In the following years, Luo served as the 17th Commander of Guangdong Provincial Defence Army, Adjutant of the Fourth Route Army Command of the Guangdong Army to Aid Fujian, Commander and Deputy Commander of the Sixth Infantry Regiment of the Third Brigade of the 13th Division of the Guangdong Army of Chen Jiongming.\n\nIn 1924, Luo was defeated by the KMT in the Eastern Expedition, and was subsequently absorbed into the National Revolutionary Army. Serving as a Garrison Commander in Guangzhou, Luo was defeated by the German Intervention Forces. After the German Empire pulled out of Guangzhou, Luo was recruited by Chen Lianbo's Guangzhou forces to keep the city from falling into anarchy. Luo served a short stint as the magistrate of Yangshan County in 1932 and 1933 and was hailed for his educational and administrative reforms and anti-corruption policies. In 1934, Chen Lianbo called him back into service as a staff officer in the Guangzhou defence forces.§!\n\n§YNotes: A Career Officer, Luo is not considered to be particularly close to any political faction and merely carries out his duty.§!
Ma Yuhang
§YBorn:§! §L1881, in Haifeng County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §lPublic Interest Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LMa Yuhang was engaged in early revolutionary activity against the Qing. Ma and Chen helped create the Zhengqi Society, and participated in the failed Guangdong New Army Uprising. Ma and Chen fled to Hong Kong, and then back to Haifeng. In the Xinhai Revolution, Ma planned the logistics for the Huanghuagang Uprising. In 1920, Chen assigned Ma to be the director of the Shantou Finance Bureau. In his capacity as Finance Director, Ma managed the logistics and finances of the Guangdong Army, ensuring that they were well supplied. When Sun and Chen fell out in 1922, Ma was sent to negotiate with Wang Jingwei in Hong Kong.\n\nChen, whilst attempting to reach out to the Zhili Clique, sent Ma up north to promote provincial autonomy in Tianjin and Beijing. Later that year, the Yue Army agreed to make Ma the Director of Political Affairs Department of Guangdong Army Headquarters. When the Kuomintang defeated Chen Jiongming's forces in the Eastern Expedition, Ma left for Hong Kong. When the Northern Expedition collapsed, Ma accompanied Chen to Guangzhou, now under the control of Chen Lianbo. Chen became a senator of the Guangdong Assembly, and Ma left his friend to assist Ye Ju's Haifeng administration. For the past decade, he has helped supply Ye Ju's armies, preparing for the day the delicate balance in Guangdong crumples.§!\n\n§YNotes: As Chen Jiongming's oldest and closest friend, there is no doubt where Ma Yuhang's sympathies lie.§!
Weng Shiliang
§YBorn:§! §L1880, in Huiyang County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LNeutral§!\n§YBackground:§! §LGraduating from the Guangdong Huangpu Military Academy, Weng joined the Tongmenghui in 1910. During the Xinhai Revolution, he led his men to seize Huizhou. In December 1911, he became a staff officer for Chen Jiongming, the governor of Guangdong. After the Revolution, Weng was rewarded with directorship of the Guangdong Huangpu Military Academy, and was made a major general of the republic. In December 1920, he served as the director of the adjutant department of the Guangdong Army, and later served as the commander of the second independent brigade of the Guangdong Army.\n\nIn October 1921, he led his troops to participate in the campaign to suppress the old Guangxi warlords, and served as the commander of the left wing of the Guangdong Army's aid to Guangxi Army and the commander-in-chief of the Central Army's advance army. When Sun and Chen fell out, Weng rallied his men in support of Chen. In the following years, he fought against the KMT, and was made a Lieutenant General by the Beiyang Government. In 1924, he left the army to pursue business opportunities in Hong Kong. In 1932, Chen Lianbo called Weng out of retirement to serve as the director of the Guangzhou defence forces.§!\n\n§YNotes: Although once full of revolutionary conviction, Weng finds himself saddled with old age and a growing sense of weariness.§!
Xiong Lue
§YBorn:§! §L1889, in Jiaying Prefecture, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gYue Army§!\n§YBackground:§! §LGraduating from the Guangdong Huangpu Military Academy, Xiong joined the Tongmenghui in 1910. During the early republican era, Xiong rose through the ranks of the Guangdong Army, becoming the Commander of the Eighth Route Army in 1916. In 1917. Xiong joined Chen Jiongming in Fujian, fighting off the Zhejiang Army. During the 1st Yue-Gui War, Xiong occupied Chao'an, and took Wuzhou in the 2nd Yue-Gui War. When Ye Ju resolved to shell Guangzhou during Sun's growing conflict with Chen, Xiong was responsible for commanding the siege.\n\nUnwilling to kill him, he told his confidants to tell Sun to flee the city. In February 1923, Xiong's troops moved to Zhaoqing. In April, Xiong's troops and Yang Kunru's troops fought fiercely with Liu Zhenhuan's troops in Shilong and other places. In July, Xiong led his troops to support Danshui, fought a bloody battle for a day and a night, and repelled the coalition forces. In 1925, Xiong was soundly defeated in the Eastern Expedition, and fled to Hong Kong. As the KMT forces collapsed in the Northern Expedition, Xiong followed Ye Ju back into Guangdong, helping him retake Haifeng. Xiong has been stationed up north in Ye Ju's territories, watching for any moves by Shen Hongying, the nominal governor of Guangdong.§!\n\n§YNotes: A Veteran of Chen Jiongming's Guangdong Army, Xiong can be counted as one of Chen's more reliable supporters.§!
Yang Kunru
§YBorn:§! §L1884, in Bolou County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gYue Army§!\n§YBackground:§! §LYang Kunru's military career began in 1917 when he was recruited into the Old Guangxi Clique during the Constitutional Protection War. However, with the splintering of the Constitutional Protection Movement, Yang went over to the Guangdong Army of Chen Jiongming. During the 1st Yue-Gui War he was promoted brigade commander, and during the 2nd Yue-Gui War he led the 5th Division in the capture of Wuzhou. After the June 16th Incident, Yang was ordered by Chen Jiongming and Ye Ju to defend Huizhou.\n\nIn 1923, Yang was ousted from Huizhou due to a Liao Zhongkai-backed coup led by Luo Fengxiang, his chief of staff. Yang offered his services to Xu Chongzhi, and then retook Huizhou from Luo. However when Sun died, Yang launched a rebellion against the Guangzhou Military Government, once again aligning Huizhou with Chen Jiongming. Chiang Kai-shek retook Huizhou using Luo Fengxiang's strategy, and Yang fled to Hong Kong alone. With the defeat of the Northern Expedition, Yang returned to Guangdong alongside Ye Ju. Ye Ju rallied a small army to retake Haifeng and assigned Yang back to Huizhou, where he has continued to be stationed for a decade.§!\n\n§YNotes: Yang only seeks to maintain his fiefdom in Huizhou, and will shift allegiances when necessary to hold onto power.§!
Ge Zhaohuang
§YBorn:§! §L1894, in Boluo County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gYue Army§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA relative latecomer to the political scene of Guangdong, Ge joined the 4th Army of the National Revolutionary Army under Chen Mingshu in 1925. The following year, he participated in the Northern Expedition. When the Kuomintang faced imminent defeat at the hands of the Germans and Zhili Clique, Ge abandoned the Nationalists to their fate, fleeing into the city of Guangzhou right after the Germans pulled out and Chen Lianbo took control.\n\nGe joined the criminal underworld, as part of the Five Continents Chinese Hongmen Southwest Headquarters. For the past decade, Ge has made a name for himself in the Cantonese crime world, with cooperation from the authorities in exchange for any intelligence he might have on hand. In particular, Ge has profited from collaboration with the Haifeng warlord Ye Ju, supplying him weapons whilst expanding his influence in Eastern Guangdong.\n\n§YNotes:§! Corrupt, shadowy, and nationalistic, Ge is a staunch anti-socialist and distrustful of Berlin while boasting the ambition of conquerors.§!
Chen Xiru
§YBorn:§! §L1859, in Xiangshan County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §lPublic Interest Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LSecond son of the Overseas Chinese businessman Chen Fang, Chen Xiru infrequently lived between Hawaii and Guangdong, to the point of being a classmate of Sun Yat-sen at the age of 11. Entering Yale University and meeting future first Prime Minister Tang Shaoyi, Chen would become a close friend of his, and return to Hawaii to help his father with business. In 1890 his father returned to Guangdong to settle down, and Xiru chose to follow him.\n\nReceived by Sun Yat-sen, who was studying in Hong Kong, Chen would fund the young Sun with one million Hong Kong dollars, and found the China Daily paper. After his father's retirement, Xiru inherited his business empire, serving as general manager of the Douglas Steamship Company and the Chairman of the Sino-japanese Bank in Hong Kong, alongside retaining all plethora of investments in Guangdong.\n\nDuring the progressive Cantonese governments throughout the Warlord Era, Chen Xiru commonly donated large sums of money to aid in their financing. With the June 16th Incident in 1922, Chen Xiru was floated by Chen Jiongming as a potential Governor of Guangdong Province, and following the latter's expulsion, Xiru would follow him to Hong Kong. Growing dissatisfied with Jiongming, Xiru contemplated abandoning the belated former Warlord, but stuck with him, financing the Public Interest Party, and establishing ties with Chen Lianbo.§!\n\n§YNotes: He has frequent contact with Tang Shaoyi\nHe is ailing, and particularly sickly, with Xiru himself preparing to settle his business empire with his surviving son and daughter.§!
Chen Qiyou
Born to a well-off family in the twilight of the Qing Dynasty, Chen Qiyou was one of the first Chinese to be exposed to western ideas via the new high school in Haifeng. Chen became fascinated with the revolutionary martyr Zou Rong, and strongly sympathised with the revolutionary movement to overthrow the Qing. In 1909 whilst studying medicine, Chen met members of the Tongmenghui and joined the movement in 1911.\n\nChen participated in the failed Huanghuagang Uprising, he helped assassinate Fengshan, a Han bannerman. During the Xinhai Revolution, Chen helped take Huizhou. After the revolution, Chen Jiongming recognised the young man's promising future, and sent him to the Tokyo Chuo University to study political economics. Upon graduating, Chen went to work for the Beiyang Government's financial department. After Sun Yat-sen declared the Constitutional Protection Movement and a rival government in Guangzhou, Chen left Beijing to work in the south.\n\nAs secretary for Chen Jiongming's Yue Army, Chen Qiyou found himself involved with much of the political affairs of Chen Jiongming, becoming a founding member of the PIP. With Chen Jiongming's political career resumed after the Northern Expedition, Chen Qiyou has been instrumental in rebuilding Federalist influence in Guangdong, and as the aging Federalist leader marches into his seventh decade, has been increasingly seen as a potential successor to his mentor.

§YBorn:§! §L1892, in Haifeng County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §lPublic Interest Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$GXC_chen_qiyou_bio$§!\n\n§YNotes: Chen Qiyou has helped keep the Public Interest Party in tune with the modern times, as new democratic movements spring up across China, breathing fresh air into the aging Federalist movement.§!
Chen Yansheng
§YBorn:§! §L1875, in Haifeng County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §lPublic Interest Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LChen Yansheng's father was known to be a charitable man who would help the needy and assist struggling neighbours. Growing up as the oldest of four brothers, Chen Yansheng became an expert at farming and knowledgeable on fish. Chen found success in the Imperial Examinations, becoming a scholar. As a young man, Chen Yansheng became acquainted with Chen Jiongming and Ma Yuhang alongside his close friend Zhong Xiunan. Chen Jiongming started a farm in 1899 in Tianxin Village, where he and his friends would discuss their aspirations.\n\nIn 1906, Chen Jiongming resolved to create the Zhengqi Society, with Chen Yansheng enthusiastically joined. After the Xinhai Revolution swept across Southern China, Chen became the magistrate of Wuhua County in Guangdong. During the Republican era, Chen Yansheng became an avid critic of Yuan Shikai's autocratic rule and monarchical ambitions, and also opposed Duan Qirui's rule in Beijing. In 1918, Chen Yansheng served Chen Jiongming's Guangdong Army as political director of the Yue Army Headquarters during its stay in Fujian.\n\nIn 1921, Chen became the telegraph administration supervisor. Chen Yansheng sided with Chen Jiongming when the latter split with Sun Yat-sen over personal and ideological differences, and was exiled to Hong Kong with the rest of Chen's followers after the Eastern Expedition. Since returning to Guangdong in the aftermath of the Northern Expedition's failure, Chen Yansheng has helped organise the finances of the Yue Army in Haifeng, retaining the same level of dedication to Chen Jiongming's dream as he had in 1906.§!\n\n§YNotes: Of righteous and charitable character, Chen Yansheng is proud and resilient. Embodying the societal motto that a drop of water should be repaid with a spring of water, Chen will fight for a free China for as long as he breathes.§!
Zhang Junmai
Entering the Guangdong Dialect School of the Jiangnan Arsenal in Shanghai in 1899, Zhang Junmai would take part in the Baoshan County exam and become a scholar in 1902. In 1906 he would study political economy at Waseda University in Japan as part of the Qing's student programme, and whilst there would meet his lifelong mentor Liang Qichao, and his close friend Zhang Dongsun. In 1907 he joined Liang's Political News Society, and in 1910 would return to China passing the imperial exam in political science.\n\nIn 1912 he organised a republican construction discussion with Tang Hualong, and worked to promote reformist political forces, inviting Liang Qichao to return to China. Formally joining the Democratic Party and electing Liang as the leader, he would be sent to Germany under his mentor's arrangment, earning a doctorate in political science. Returning again in 1915 at Liang's invitation, he would support the Anhui Clique, but after supporting the Zhili in 1917 would withdraw from warlord governments.\n\nBecoming affiliated with Jiang Baili and Ding Wenjiang, Zhang would study under Henri Bergson, and accompany Hans Driesch during his time in China. Infamously sparking a debate on science and metaphysics in 1924, Zhang would be ingratiated with the rise of socialism in China, and even co-founded a magazine with YCP founder Li Huang. Finding himself within the employ of Sun Chuanfang's inner circle, he would found his National Institute of Political Science in Nanjing. Ultimately purged in 1932 for being associated with leftist causes, he would form the National Renaissance Society as a leftist sect of the Chinese Constitutionalist Party.
§YBorn:§! §LJanuary 18th, 1887, in Jiading County, Jiangsu Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$GXC_zhang_junmai_bio$\n\nAfter participating in Chen Jiongming's revitalised federalist government, Zhang was able to secure leadership of the China Democratic League and was elevated to the Presidency. A committed social democrat with autocratic tendencies, all eyes are on Zhang as he leads China towards an uncharted future.§!
§YBorn:§! §LJanuary 18th, 1887, in Jiading County, Jiangsu Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SDemocratic Socialist Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$GXC_zhang_junmai_bio$§!\n\n§YNotes: Enamoured by the SPD in Germany, Zhang is the epitome of a Social Democrat in the Western sense.\nHe is considered Liang Qichao's de-facto successor.\nHe is reputed for his obstinate nature.§!
Zhang Dongsun
§YBorn:§! §LJune 2nd, 1886, in Qiantang County, Zhejiang Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SDemocratic Socialist Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA descendant of a family of officials, Zhang Dongsun would be sent to Japan in 1905 to study in the Department of Philosophy at the Tokyo Imperial University and Private Institute of Philosophy. Meeting Zhang Junmai, Lan Gongwu, and Liang Qichao, he would become a disciple of the latter, and close friends with the former. In 1912 he joined the Nanjing Provisional Government as a secretary in the Ministry of the Interior, and joined the Kuomintang thereafter, maintaing close ties with Liang Qichao and the Progressive Party. Entering into the journalist business, he would publish a large number of political articles attacking Yuan Shikai's restoration but similarly besmirching the Second Revolution, and attempting to bridge the gap between reformists and revolutionaries.\n\nIn 1917 he would succeed Zhang Junmai as editor of the Research Clique's Shishi Xinbao, becoming one of the clique's leaders in 1918. Participating in the year's elections, the Research Clique would ultimately lose to the Anfu Club, resulting in Zhang abandoning direct politics. In 1920 he would initiate a lecture society with Liang, and invite Guild Socialist philosopher Bertrand Russell to visit China. Becoming enamorued with Guild Socialism, he would participate in the Socialist Research Society organised by Chen Duxiu, but refused to join the Chinese Syndicalist Party.\n\nServing in the faculty of various universities, and editing multiple articles criticising revolutionary struggle, he would serve as Professor of Philosophy at Zhang Junmai's National Institute of Political Science, and ultimately would work with Junmai within the Chinese Constitutionalist Party to form the National Renaissance Society in 1932.§!\n\n§YNotes: One of the few members of Zhang Junmai's inner circle that can disagree with him and get away with it.§!
Xu Fulin
§YBorn:§! §L1879, in Heping County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SDemocratic Socialist Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LExcelling in his studies at a young age, Xu Fulin would pass the imperial exam in 1896 and follow his brother to enter Xunzhou Fenghu Academy, later changing to Beijing Law School. Graduating with Honours, he would travel to Japan, entering Waseda University and receiving a bachelor's degree in law. During his time there he would join the Tongmenghui, and would return to Guangdong in 1908 to serve as a lawyer. In 1912 he became a member of the Provisional Senate in Beijing, and served in the First National Assembly. After its dissolution in 1914, he travelled to Japan and joined the Gemingdang, but withdrew due to dissatisfaction with the choice of a different flag from the Five Races.\n\nJoining the European Affairs Research Society (A Proto-Political Science Clique precursor), he would go onto initiate the Republic Maintenance Society in 1915 with Yang Yongtai, and Gu Zhongxiu. Serving in a civil position for Yunnan during the National Protection War, he would return to the Assembly in 1916 and found the Political Science Society with Yang, Gu, Li Genyuan, and others. In 1917 he served in Sun Yat-sen's Constitutional Protection Government, serving as Minister of Justice and President of the Supreme Court. In 1924 he expressed his open disdain at the Reorganisation of the Kuomintang, and withdrew.\n\nIn 1927 he returned to Guangdong, raising funds to build schools lost due to the Northern Expedition. In 1929 he joined Zhang Junmai's National Institute of Political Science as a member of the faculty, and helped form the National Renaissance Society in 1932. In 1934, following Zhang to Guangdong, he would found the Xuehai Academy in Guangzhou.§!\n\n§YNotes: Utterly dedicated to democracy, he will refuse to participate in any form of authoritarianism.§!

Sun Baogang
§YBorn:§! §L1909, in Jinshan County, Jiangsu Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SDemocratic Socialist Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LGraduating from the Department of Physics of Soochow University, he would travel to Japan to study and enrolled in the Shikan Gakko. Returning to China in 1935, Sun Baogang initially became a physics teacher at Feng Yong University. However following the growing influx of reformist intellectuals moving towards the Southwest, Sun would enlist in Chen Lianbo's army, and join the National Renaissance Society that same year. Young, and ultimately untested on the field, Sun proves as one of the few within Zhang Junmai's sect with any form of military experience, or command capacity.§!\n\n§YNotes: He is noted for his fierce opposition to any authoritarianism, and the heavy-handed nature of Zhang Junmai's leadership.§!
Li Minxin
§YBorn:§! §L1890, in Panyu County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cLi Jishen's Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LGraduating from the Guangdong-Guangxi Army Middle School, Li Minxin would serve as a trainee platoon leader in the local army, and serve as a clerk in the Army Department. During his time there, he would meet Li Jishen from the Army University, establishing a deep friendship. In 1912 he would join the Kuomintang, serving as a colonel staff officer during the Second Revolution. Fleeing to Macau, he would intermittently engage in various revolutionary activities.\n\nIn 1924 he would be appointed Chief of Staff of the Xijiang Relief Office to assist Li Jishen in handling relief work in the area, and in 1925 would be appointed County Magistrate of Sihui County. In 1927 he was appointed Director General of the Anti-Smuggling Department of the Ministry of Finance of the Guangzhou Provisional Government. Later he would serve as Director of Military Affairs and Adjutant of the General Command, Director of Taxation, and Salt Transport Commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi within Chen Lianbo's government.\n\nMaintaining contact with Li Jishen in MinGan, and collaborating with Chen Jitang, Li would funnel funds and finances to Li in his struggle against the League of Eight Provinces — an activity unofficially enabled by Chen Lianbo as it weakened Shen Hongying's backer, Sun Chuanfang.§!
Li Zhangda
§YBorn:§! §L1890, in Dongguan County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cLi Jishen's Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a once prosperous landlord family, Li Zhangda would initially enter a traditional education before entering the Whampoa Military Primary School in 1906, and later the Nanjing Military Middle School in 1909. During his time there he bgun to spread revolutionary propaganda amongst the students, joining the Tongmenghui later on. Classmates with the likes of Chen Mingshu and Jiang Guangnai, he would take action with them to particiapte in the Xinhai Revolution. Following Zhu Zhixin south in 1912, he would then be admitted to the Baoding Army Officer School, and participated in the Second Revolution launched by Li Liejun.\n\nGraduating from Baoding's artillery department, he would serve as a major staff officer in the Huguojun in 1916, and would transfer to the Guangdong Army in 1917 to serve as a staff officer of Deng Keng for Sun Yat-sen's Constitutional Protection Government. Studying revolutionary theory with Sun and Zhu Zhixin, alongside English with Liao Zhongkai, Li would develop a deep friendship with Liao and Zhu in particular.\n\nWith Zhu dying in 1920, he would serve as commander of an engineering battalion in the Guangdong Army. During the June 15th Incident, Li Zhangda was placed in-charge of defending the Presidential Palace against Ye Ju's onslaught, and would fight against Chen Jiongming in the Yue-Gui Wars. Resigning from his military post in 1924 to assist Liao in the United Front, he cooperated with the likes of Peng Pai, and during the Northern Expedition served in the Guangdong Government as Director of Public Security. Following the fall of Guangzhou and the collapse of the Northern Expedition, Li would continue ties with the MinGan insurgents thanks to Liao Zhongkai, but otherwise remained within Guangzhou.§!

In 1917 he would serve as a guard of Sun Yat-sen's Presidential Palace, fighting in the Constitutional Protection War and against Fujian Governor Li Houji. In 1920 Xie would fight against Mo Rongxin and Li Genyuan, and later in 1921 against Shen Hongying, ending 1922 as division commander within the Guangdong Army.\n\nFighting in the Yue-Gui wars on the side of the Kuomintang, Xie would continue to faithfully serve Xu Chongzhi until his detainment by Chiang Kai-shek in the mid 20s Kuomintang power struggle. Now without a master, Xie would see the Northern Expedition as commander of the 48th Army of the National Revolutionary Army, however following the collapse on multiple fronts, he would be detained by Chiang briefly before the Generalissimo's assassination.\n\nEntering functional retirement thereafterwards, Xie would serve in a minimal capacity aiding Li Jishen in his struggle in MinGan, volunteering to fight with the NRA remnants on multiple occasions. Lin Hu
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 1st, 1887 in Luchuan County, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gYoung Guangxi Faction§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a Han father and a Zhuang mother, Lin Hu entered the Jiangxi Military Academy at 15 years old, becoming classmates with Li Liejun and Cai E. Leaving before graduation, he would receive his first appointment in 1905 as a sentry officer in Guangxi. In 1906 he would join the Tongmenghui with Cai E. During Xinhai, Lin Hu fought for the revolutionaries and led his troops into Nanjing. In 1912 he became a subordinate of Li Liejun, and participated in Li's Second Revolution, fighting valiantly.\n\nFleeing to Japan, he joined the Gemingdang in 1914, and founded the Law and Politics School with Li Liejun, Bai Wenwei, and Huang Fu. Further founding the Proto-Political Science Clique organisation known as the European Affairs Research Society with Li Genyuan and Zhang Shizhao, he would travel to Singapore with Xiong Kewu to aid Huang Xing. Crucially, Lin and Niu Yongjian returned to Guangxi in 1915 to persuade Lu Rongting to revolt against Yuan Shikai, with Lin arranging contact with Cai E and Li Liejun. Fighting in the National Protection War as Commander of the 6th Army, he would ultimately be one of the top leaders of the Old Guangxi Clique, only being defeated in 1920 by the Guangdong Army.\n\nRefusing Sun Yat-sen's offer of amnesty, he engaged in Anti-Sun activities, helping Chen Jiongming to contact Beijing in 1922, and in 1924 was appointed Governor of Guangdong by the Zhili. With the defeat of the Old Yue Clique in the KMT's Eastern Expedition, Lin Hu would take charge of the remnant Guangdong army just to lose it all at the Battle of Mianhu. Fleeing to Shanghai, Lin's retirement would be shortlived as he would seize the opportunity to return to the spotlight following the NRA's impending collapse. Returning to Liangguang, he has once again become a key player in the Old Guangxi Clique.§!\n\n§YNotes: A sworn brother of Liu Zhilu and Ma Ji, he is simultaneously a core of the Young Guangxi Faction, and a nascent ally of Ye Ju and the Yue clique.§!
Liu Zhilu
§YBorn:§! §L1891, in Meixian County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gYoung Guangxi Faction§!\n§YBackground:§! §LReceiving a basic education at Meicheng High School in Meizhou City, Liu Zhilu would be admitted to the Humen Army School, and later the Guangdong Army Military Academy. In 1910 he joined the Tongmenghui, and served in the Guangdong Army through Xinhai until the Second Revolution, where he was purged by Long Jiguang. Recommended by a family friend, he would join the Old Guangxi Clique, becoming an adopted son of Mo Rongxin. Granted various important positions by Mo, Liu would assist the Old Guangxi Clique in reorganising its army to fight in the National Protection War.\n\nFighting against Long Jiguang, he would be promoted to Commander of the Fourth Army of the Huguojun, becoming the warlord of Huizhou City. Eventually expanding to Meizhou and Shantou, Liu would again fight Long under Mo Rongxin's direction, deposing him in 1918. Becoming a major warlord under his adopted father, Liu would ultimately lose in the first Yue-Gui War, but would persist under Lu Rongting's leadership. Following Lu's deposition in 1922, Liu would then bounce to Chen Jiongming, becoming affiliated with the Old Guangdong Clique.\n\nWorking with Huang Dawei, Lin Hu, Lai Shihuang and others, he established the Joint Forces Office on behalf of Chen, and would engage in combat against the Kuomintang and the National Revolutionary Army. Fleeing northwards after the Eastern Expedition, he would become ingratiated within the Zhili Clique, and would return to Liangguang following the Kuomintang's collapse in the Northern Expedition. Reunited with his sworn brothers Lin Hu and Ma Ji, he forms a pillar of the Young Guangxi Faction.§!\n\n§YNotes: He has ties to Du Yuesheng and the Green Gangs.§!
Ma Ji
§YBorn:§! §L1888, in Baise County, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gYoung Guangxi Faction§!\n§YBackground:§! §LSon of Ma Dianxun, sworn brother of Lu Rongting, Ma Ji would be entrusted to Lu Rongting in 1909. Sturdy, strong, and good at martial arts, Lu treated Ma Ji akin to his actual son, and sent him to the Guangxi Military Academy. Recalled before finishing his education, Ma Ji became a close confidant of his adopted father. With Lu becoming Governor of Guangxi in 1911, Ma Ji continued to serve as his aide-de-camp, and was one of the leading conspirators negotiating for his adopted father to revolt against Yuan Shikai in 1915. Establishing the Wuwei Army on behalf of Lu, he would face off against Long Jiguang, successfully routing him from Guangdong.\n\nBecoming Commander-in-Chief of the First Guangdong Army, he would fight in Hunan, eventually developing a good rapport with Wu Peifu. Telegraphing his close friend Lin Hu for assistance, Wu eventually peacefully withdrew from Hunan to fight in the Zhili-Anhui War. In 1924 Ma Ji would send a subordinate to alleviate Shen Hongying's siege of Guilin, and with the assitance of Zhao Hengti and Ye Qi ulimately enabled Lu Rongting to escape and retire.\n\nIngratiated within the Zhili Clique from there onwards, Ma Ji would fight in the Northern Expedition against the National Revolutionary Army as Chief of Staff in Wu Peifu's HQ, and with Lu Rongting's return to Guangxi in late 1927, would take his place oncemore as the able aide to his ailing adoptive father. Working to consolidate Liangguang under the Young Guangxi Faction, Lu Rongting's death in 1934 has left Ma Ji and his adopted brother Lu Yuguang with the reigns of Guangxi's empire.§!\n\n§YNotes: Sworn brother of Lin Hu and Liu Zhilu.§!

Guo Chunsen
§YBorn:§! §L1876, in Wuxuan County, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §gYoung Guangxi Faction§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA scholar in the Qing Dynasty, Guo Chunsen started out passing the imperial exam at the age of 19. In 1905 he travelled to Japan to study law and politics, and during his time there joined the Tongmenghui. During the Xinhai Revolution, Guo participated in the Yunnanese Double Ninth Uprising, later serving as the Dean of Academic Affairs of the Yunnan Law and Politics School. Becoming a Senator in the first National Congress of the Beiyang Republic, Guo would travel south to Sun Yat-sen's Constitutional Protection Government in 1917, and after his arrival became ingratiated with Lu Rongting's Old Guangxi Clique.\n\nAppointed Secretary-General of the Guangxi Military Governor's Office, Guo would work with other senators to transition the Constitutional Protection Government's Generalissimo system to that of a Presidential one, and excluding Sun Yat-sen from office. Advising Mo Rongxin in the late 1910s, Guo would exile himself to Shanghai following Mo's deposition. Returning to Guangxi following Old Guangxi's revival under a rejuvenated yet ailing Lu Rongting, Guo would provide his amenable skillset to the new kingpins of the region, Lu Yuguang, Liu Zhilu, Lin Hu, and Ma Ji.§!
Zhang Gan
§YBorn:§! §L1897, in Guilin, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LNeutral§!\n§YBackground:§! §LGraduating from the Guangxi Army Speed training School, Zhang Gan would start his military career as a major adjutant in Lu Rongting's Guangxi Army in 1923. After Lu's defeat, Zhang Gan's troops were absorbed into the New Guangxi Clique, were he served as a battalion commander under Li Zongren. Flexible and not too ideologically cohesive, Zhang did not particularly mind which patron he fought for as long as he could protect Guangxi. In 1926 he became a lieutenant colonel adjutant and colonel adjutant in the 7th Army of the National Revolutionary Army. Following the collapse of the Northern Expedition, Zhang would just as easily melt into the resurgent Old Guangxi's ranks as he did with New Guangxi, serving as a division commander under Lin Hu.\n\nIn 1928 Zhang would attend and graduate from the Nanjing Army University, and return to serve as Chief of Staff of the 2nd Guangxi Army, a role he has served dutifully ever since. Overseeing Lin Hu's expansion into the free territory of Liangguang, Zhang is a relatively neutral player in the Young Guangxi Faction, all things considered.§!
Ma Junwu
§YBorn:§! §LJuly 17th, 1881 in Gongcheng County, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LIndependent§!\n§YBackground:§! §LClose ally of Sun Yat-sen, Ma Junwu would be an inquisitive and bright child, set on the path to becoming a scholar. Deeply influenced by Kang Youwei, who had travelled to Guilin to promote his ideas, Ma would believe that China needed westernisation to strengthen itself. Studying French in 1900, Ma would travel to Singapore to meet Kang, and then enter Shanghai's Aurora College.\n\nGranted a scholarship in Japan, Ma would meet Liang Qichao and Tang Rui, later meeting Sun Yat-sen in 1902. Transforming from Reformist to Revolutionary, Ma would become a close aide to Sun, being one of the first members of the Tongmenghui, and an enthusiastic revolutionary. Travelling to Germany in 1907, he would gain a bachelor's degree in engineering, and would see service in Xinhai, and then the new Republic.\n\nRemaining with Sun from Xinhai till his death, Ma would even be named Sun's preferred candidate for Guangxi Governor, albeit would be obstructed by the Old Guangxi Clique. Ma would oppose the 1924 Reorganisation, and as such would be expelled in 1926 for becoming Minister of Justice in Duan Qirui's provincial government; albeit would resign after the March 18th Massacre.\n\nCommitted to education reform, Ma would return to Guangxi to aid in the construction of the Guangxi University, his magnum opus. Working with Pan Zhuqi and the Old Guangxi Clique Reformists, Ma aimed to strengthen China through scientific research, ignoring political disputes, albeit has found himself the Guangxi Provincial Head of the developing Jingxing Society.§!
Shen Hongying
Son of a poor family, Shen Hongying had already joined a bandit gang at the age of 21. Becoming leader in 1905, Shen would expand the gang to include nearly 100 people, including his eldest son Shen Rongguang. Contacted by local Xinhai Revolutionaries such as Liu Zhenhuan, Shen decided to accept their offer of amnesty in exchange for service. Becoming increasingly powerful, he would ultimately betray the revolutionaries in the Second Revolution. Murdering and rampaging his way through Guangxi, Shen would ultimately end up under the employ of Lu Rongting.\n\nEngaging in the National Protection War under Lu Rongting, he would end up a close ally of Mo Rongxin, and de-facto warlord of Qiongya, and then in the East of Guangdong. On the eve of the First Yue-Gui War, Mo Rongxin floated Shen Hongying as his replacement for Governor of Guangdong, but following Ma Ji's interjection, he would be passed over. Underestimating Chen Jiongming's Guangdong Army, Shen would ultimately blunder his way into Hunan, wherein he would clash with Ye Kaixin and Ye Qi. Utilised as a tool by Wu Peifu to force the unification of the country, Shen would march into Guangxi in 1922, and would gain the support of Cen Chunxuan in Guangdong.\n\nRecommend by Cen to Sun Yat-sen, Shen's Army, the Yunnan Army in Guangdong, and the Guangxi Army under Liu Zhenhuan would fight Chen Jiongming for the KMT. Contacting Wu Peifu secretly, Shen was appointed Governor of Guangdong by the Zhili, but was ultimately ejected by Liu Zhenhuan and Yang Ximin. Clashing with Lu Rongting, Shen would ultimately square off against the nascent New Guangxi Clique alongside Li Jishen and Chen Jitang. Once again underestimating his opponent, he was utterly defeated by the KMT. Fleeing to Hong Kong and living a life of debauchery, Shen would return to prominence following the need of the Southern Zhili for their own man in Liangguang.
§YBorn:§! §L1871, in Luorong County, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$GXC_shen_hongying_bio$§!
§YBorn:§! §L1871, in Luorong County, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §PShen Army Faction§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$GXC_shen_hongying_bio$§!
Zhu Jiahua
Entering the Tongji German Medical School in Shanghai in 1908, and embroiled with revolutionary fervour, Zhu Jiahua would join the Revolutionary Dare-to-Die Corps in Shanghai during Xinhai. Returning in 1912, he would resume his studies as an Electrical Engineer. After graduating in 1914, Zhu would receive funding to study in Germany, where he learnt metallurgy at the Technical University of Berlin. In 1917 Zhu was unable to continue his studies due to the First World War, and so worked as a German Teacher at Beijing University.\n\nSoon afterwards he travelled to Switzerland to study and entered the University of Bern. In 1920 he returned to Germany and studied geology at the University of Berlin, receiving a doctorate in philosophy in 1922. Returning to China in 1924, he would become a professor and German instructor at the Department of Geology at Beijing University. In 1926 following the March 18th Massacre, Zhu was accused of being responsible for inciting the students, and was forced to flee to his hometown.\n\nBecoming head of the Department of Geology at the National Guangdong University, he would become acting chairman of the Sun yat-sen University Committee, and become a member of the Guangdong Provincial Government. Refusing to join the Kuomintang, Zhu would instead oversee the peaceful transition of power of the German Occupation of Guangzhou to the Chinese. Becoming a reasonably successful diplomat within the Chen Lianbo administration, he would move onto the retinue of Sun Chuanfang, and aid in negotiating the German Military Mission to China.\n\nHelping setup the Jingxing Society with individuals such as Tang Zaili, Li Linsi and Gu Weijun, Zhu would ultimately become the chief of the Guangdong branch of the Jingxing Society following the Shanghai Uprising; influential in Sino-German Circles, Zhu is an ambitious man with skill to match.

Shen Rongguang
§YBorn:§! §L1892, in Luorong, Guangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §PShen Army Faction§!\n§YBackground:§! §LEldest son of esteemed bandit turned warlord and politician Shen Hongying, Shen Rongguang was recruited by his father at a young age to serve in his bandit gang. Participating in all endeavours of his father, he would serve as a sentry officer and captain in Lu Rongting's army following Shen Hongying's integration into the Old Guangxi Clique. In 1916 he entered Guangdong and served as a battalion commander, and later brigade commander under Long Jiguang. Fighting under his father, he would serve as a brigade commander in the Guangxi Frontier Defence Army, and later in 1922 under the Guangdong Army.\n\nServing in the 6th Army under Sun Yat-sen in 1924, he would ultimately be defeated by the New Guangxi Clique in 1925, and followed his father into exile in Hong Kong. Returning to prominence following his father's bargaining with the Southern Zhili Clique, Shen Rongguang acts as his father's ever faithful stooge. Not marred by any consciousness of pride or nationalism, he is a bandit through and through.§!
Li Yaohan
Briefly educated in a private school when he was young, he would ultimately lead a failed business before joining local bandits led by his fellow villager. Becoming a sentry officer and receiving an official rank, he gradually rose to the rank of Commander of the Guangdong Navy Patrol Battalion and the Garrison Commander of Dong'an county. After Xinhai, the Tongmenghui contacted Li and instigated him to join the revolution. Forming his own battalion, it eventually grew into a regiment.\n\nInitially supporting Yuan Shikai in 1912, he assisted Long Jiguang and was appointed garrison commander of Zhaoluoyang. Expanding his army to more than 10,000 people, Li would fight in the National Protection War against Yuan Shikai, and would inadvertently join the Old Guangxi Clique. Taking over as Governor of Guangdong from Chen Bingkun in 1917, Li did not actually take the position out of fear of his enemies. Refusing to join the Constitutional Protection Government, he would resign from his official position and return to Zhaoluoyang, but would lose his post to Lin Hu and his army to Mo Rongxin.\n\nLater deciding to join Chen Jiongming due to Old Guangxi's actions, he would still lose all of his troops and be relegated to an advisor position. Dissatisfied with Chen, he would defect to Shen Hongying in 1922, and would serve as commander of the 5th army of the Guangxi Army, but was defeated by Liu Zhenhuan and Yang Ximin. Considering defection, he would return to his hometown of Xinxing County, establishing his own fiefdom there. Pushed out briefly, he would return following the chaotic interregnum in the aftermath of the KMT. With lack of better allies available for either, Li would reluctantly enter into an alliance with Shen oncemore.

Chen Lianbo
Born into a rich merchant family, despite being the eldest son he was adopted by his aunt. Chen Lianbo would initially study in a private school, at the age of 12 he would travel to Hong Kong to study English at Queen's College and obtain British citizenship. After graduating at the age of 16, Chen joined the Guangzhou Shamian Branch of HSBC Bank, and was later promoted to comprador due to his outstanding performance. He operated in own silk shop, and in 1908 founded the Guangdong Insurance Company. Becoming quite wealthy, he joined the Guangzhou General Chamber of Commerce.\n\nA celebrity within the Guangdong business community, he monopolised the local raw silk trade. Engaging in speculative business, he relied extensively on HSBC to control and manipulate the markets, and expanded into all sorts of economic endeavours. He served as Prime Minister of the Guangdong Export Association and President of the Guangdong Chamber of Commerce in 1915. Serving as president of various merchant associations, he had contacts directly with the Governorship. Soon in his lavish mansion he setup the \

Chen Gongshou
§YBorn:§! §L1877, in Nanhai County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cCanton Merchant Corps§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA graduate of the Guangdong Police School in 1907 who served as a patrol officer in Foshan, Chen Gongshou became the head of the Judicial Department of the Guangdong Police Department after the Xinhai Revolution. Climbing up the ranks and becoming director of the police department, Chen also lent his services as a consultant to the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company in 1920. In 1924 Chen established the Foshan Loyalty Association and served as the president of the Foshan Chamber of commerce and the Foshan Merchants Association. In 1924 he was elected Deputy Commander of the Guangdong Merchant Corps Joint Defence Headquarters alongside Deng Jieshi, and assisted Chen Lianbo in launching the Merchant Corps Incident, but after its failure fled to Hong Kong with Lianbo.\n\nBriefly flirting as a Buddhist monk, Chen would return to Foshan at the request of Chen Lianbo, he would build the Jiulian Shenghui temple and raise donations from believers, overseas Chinese, and businessmen. Returning to the position as Director of the Guangdong Police Department, Chen is effectively the main military arm within Guangzhou, operating its police force akin to a paramilitary.§!\n\n§YNotes: He is alleged for excessive abuse of power.§!
Deng Jieshi
§YBorn:§! §Lin Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cCanton Merchant Corps§!\n§YBackground:§! §LElected Deputy Commander of the Guangdong Merchant Corps Joint Defence Headquarters alongside Chen Gongshou in 1924, Deng would command the 8th Corps of the Merchant Corps, and see urban warfare against the Kuomintang and striking workers within Guangzhou during the Merchant Corps Incident. Fleeing to Hong Kong with Chen Lianbo and Gongshou, Deng would largely remain within Merchant Corps exile circles until Chen Lianbo's return to Guangzhou in 1927. Following his friend, he would once again take up a position of command within Chen Lianbo's military, alongside Chen Gongshou, and other hired generals.§!
Chen Lianzhong

At the age of 19, Chen began to enter the business world. In 1913 he was awarded a medal from the Beiyang Government for his enthusiasm in public welfare and meritorious service to local industry. In 1919 Chen Lianbo became the head of the Guangzhou Merchants' Association, and in 1921 was elected president of the Guangzhou General Chamber of Commerce. Similarly Lianzhong was appointed as director of the Guangdong Mint, but later he resigned.\n\nServing in various roles as manager of the Public Welfare Insurance company, director of the Dili Mining Company, director of Taihua Insurance, and founded several banks in Guangdong. Chen also served as the financial director of the Guangdong Food Relief Association, the Guangdong Charity Relief Association, and the Guangdong Merchants Association. In 1923 he was elected the president of the Guangzhou General Chamber of Commerce, replacing his brother, and in 1923 successfully maintained the value of the Guangdong Provincial Bank's banknotes.\n\nIn 1924 during the Merchant Corps Incident, Chen was forced to flee to Hong Kong, before returning in 1924 to serve as comprador of the HSBC Guangzhou branch in Shamian and head of the Merchant Corps, replacing his brother who was still in exile. Visited by Hu Hanmin in 1925, Chen would remit continuing to fund the Nationalist Government. Following the KMT's defeat, he would welcome his brother back into Guangzhou, handing the election of head of the Merchant Corps to him.§!
Jiang Kongyin
§YBorn:§! §L1864, in Nanhai County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LNeutral§!\n§YBackground:§! §LStudying under Kang Youwei, Jiang Kongyin would participate in the reform efforts of his teacher, including the infamous petition to the Emperor to prevent the signing of the Treaty of Shimonoskei by the Qing. Known for his literary talent, he passed the imperial exam in 1904 and served in various official capacities in Guangdong. As Governor, deputy admiral of the Guangdong Navy, and supervisor of the Guangdong-Guangxi Cleanup Campaign. A very popular man, he persuaded numerous officials to side with the Xinhai Revolutionaries, but thereafterwards quit politics almost entirely.\n\nLiving in Hong Kong for a time, in 1915 he was hired as the general agent of the British-American Tobacco Company in South China, participating in a fierce business battle with the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company. In the 1930s he returned to Guangzhou, renting more than 1000 acres of wasteland and established Jianglanzhai Bee Farm. Qiu Jingyun
A major landlord in Haifeng, Qiu Jingyun became increasingly anxious like much of the gentry at the growing popularity of the Farmers' Association. In reaction, the Grain Industry Maintenance Association was formed with Chen Yuebo as chairman, and Wang Zuoxin as vice-chairman. This iteration of the association did not last long, however, as it was immediately dissolved when Chen Yuebo resigned and fled to Hong Kong.\n\nQiu soon became the County Magistrate on May 12th, 1923, much to the joint-opposition of the Farmers' Association and local academic community. His term as County Magistrate did not last long, however, as Wang was soon appointed county magistrate in May 27th. The Grain Industry Maintenance Association was soon restored by Wang Zuoxin, Qiu Jingyun, and Liu Douwen, only for it to dissolve yet again after Chen Jiongming stepped down and the KMT began their rule in Guangdong.\n\nAs the Northern Expedition soon fractured, the association was revived yet again under Qiu's chairmanship in collaboration with Ye Ju to reestablish the gentry's position and suppress peasant activities in Haifeng.\n\n§YNotes: An old mentor of Chen Jiongming, his relationship with his former student remains strong.§!

Lin Douwen

As Director, Lin protected the landed interests whilst collecting rent from the farmers through force, causing much resentment among the peasantry.\n\nThis burden enflamed tensions between gentry and peasantry, as more farmers flock to the Farmers' Association led by Peng Pai. After Chen Jiongming's tenure as governor ended with his defeat by the KMT, the Grain Industry Maintenance Association was forced to dissolve whilst the Haifeng General Farmers' Association aligned themselves with the KMT and became the Guangdong Provincial Farmers' Association.\n\nAs the Northern Expedition faltered and Guangdong was rid of the KMT, Lin reprised his role as Head of the Security Force when the Grain Industry Maintenance Association was restored. Chaos lingered in Haifeng as both the gentry and peasantry dish out retaliatory actions against each other, stopped only by Ye Ju's military presence within the county.§!\n\n§YNotes: He was once driven out of a village and subsequently beaten up in another village whilst collecting rent.§!
