Unify the Volunteer and Conscription System
In Guangxi, we have reversed the old Chinese saying: \
The Threefold Self-Reliance Policy
Sun Yat-sen once spoke of Three Principles for the People: Democracy, Welfare, and Nationalism. In Guangxi, these form the foundation of our principles of self-reliance: self-government, self-sufficiency, and self-defence. We can ill afford to be dependent on foreign suppliers, and must produce our own guns, grenades, and mortars. Moreover, our militias must be willing to lend a hand in local reforestation, planting, construction, land registration and census-taking.
From a Budding Flower May Ferocity Grow
Youth is little excuse for meekness. Young boys will be taught military skills, girls nursing skills. Junior High School will compose of five semesters of normal academics, with the sixth semester largely dedicated to military training including a militarised final exam. University students will be required to attend five hours of military training weekly, female students three. By adulthood, all children will have learned how to defend the nation.
China's Sparta
Whatever conceited outsiders may think of Guangxi, no amount of disparaging remarks about our \
Mobilisation of the Masses
With the further advancement of our militia-programme into the newly reclaimed regions of China, the new citizens within our government struggle to integrate into the militia framework, with some even protesting vigorously. To this end, we must incentivise the expansion of the militia system with a further call to arms aimed at the peasantry, for without the participation of the Chinese people in our new model militia, how can they truly take their part in our society?
Understanding of the Land
Those native to Guangxi know of its terrain: rugged, mountainous, hardy. Yet the people are but a reflection of the land they develop in, and Guangxi soldiers are known for their ferocity in battle. Therefore we must enlighten the rest of our soldiers in understanding the lands they grew up in, for any foe — foreign or otherwise — should know to fear a combatant in their home territory.
Heart of the Soldier
A soldier and their gun is akin to a peasant and their plough. Inseparable. Therefore we cannot sit idly by as the world around us modernises their rifles and helmets, for what use is a bolt-action rifle against an armoured behemoth? The weapons of our soldiers must be as strong as their hearts, for good courage deserves to be backed by strong force.
Modern Methods for a New Age
Since the turn of the century, a new age of warfare has dawned. Automatic weapons, planes, artillery, and tanks all descend unto battlefields around the globe. Yet Chinese warfare has remained nominally stagnant, with few notable attempts at modernisation of the armies. Whilst lacking in industry for proper armoured divisions, we can still integrate modern vehicles into both our divisions and supply lines.
Good Iron for Nails, Good Men Serve the Army
Despite the militia system having been cemented into Chinese society, there remain those who object to the conscription system. In order to rectify such a misunderstanding, we must incentivise to the Chinese people the reasons to serve, the reasons to bleed. To meet this, a new round of conscription will be called for throughout the nation. For if we are ever descended upon by any foe, they must learn that the entire Chinese citizenry will oppose them.
Citizen-Soldier Unification
The ever striking advance of our citizen stratocracy comes closer to the apotheosis of our theorist's desires. New militia continue to be trained vigorously, and prove again and again their effectiveness in our wars. Our soldiers continue to serve the nation, be it in peace-time or during war, a truly coherent, coordinated society beating like a living being. Soldiers are no longer regarded as an unruly, lowly class but as a core part of Chinese society.
Preparing for the Great Bloodletting
Many theorists still criticise the lack of proper reserves comparable to other modern nation-states throughout the world. Our standing army could reach innumerable heights, and yet if a Chinese soldier were to die on the battlefield, our system would be so inept as to struggle to replace them despite the adequate numbers of trained citizen-soldiers. To rectify this, we absolutely must restructure and modernise the current reserves system to be fit for our new way of waging war.
Guangxi Tactics
The mountainous terrain within Guangxi carves it into small, isolated pockets. Such an environment is the premier developing grounds for unorthodox tactics employed by the denizens there, and this is not any more readily apparent than in the province's banditry. Despite the modern, numerically superior foes they would face, the bandits would continuously triumph through utilisation of warfare not found within textbooks. Our soldiers will learn to fight in the Guangxi way.
Unified Militia Framework
Unending in the desires for expansion of the militia system, our theorists have called for a \
Chinese Warfare Revitalised
Truly our militia system is not revolutionary, in fact it harkens to the days long past us. There existed such a framework within the Xia, Shang and Zhou dynasties. No distinction existed between a soldier or a peasant, the army and people were truly one being. Therefore our system is but the natural order of things within China, and we have merely returned to our roots. A true revitalisation of this traditional Chinese system in the warfare of the current age.
Building the Eliteheer
The logical continuation of our military reforms is to do what Sun Chuanfang and Wu Peifu have largely failed to do with German help: build a capable central army to serve as the core of China's military. We must act as auxiliaries no more: if China is to be saved an army must be created to protect it. We shall build an army along western lines, continuing the stratified structure already laid out for us.
Song and Dance of the Military Confucius
The Germans of course made their mark over most of China, but they are hardly the only ones with an interest in the region or a proud military history. We must take care to recruit further trainers to aid us in building our army, whether it be courting formal advisors from foreign powers or hiring private mercenary trainers with less diplomatic baggage. Still, we dream of the day we will again be at the forefront of military advancement.
Victory Secured Through Reconnaissance
Superior battlefield intelligence is invaluable in an age of rapidly improving communications and swift movement. Careful spotting, intelligence gathering, and communication to headquarters goes hand-in-hand with victory, foiling ambushes and supporting assaults. Whether it be conventional foes on the frontline or anti-partisan operations in the hinterlands, we must secure this advantage.
Modern Engineering Corps
Military engineering is an ancient part of the art of war, and one that continues to this day. Indeed, our old German advisors were always proud of their combat engineering corps, and we too must take careful stock of our own capabilities. Tasked with building fieldworks, paving roads, and breaching obstacles, engineers are a critical support arm for any modern military.
Form Mobile Detachments
In these days of mechanised warfare, and perhaps combined with the horrors of static warfare on the Great War's Western Front, it is often easy to forget that commanders have valued mobility long before the first truck or train. Taking inspiration from the \
Fight Without Thought of Retreat
To win a modern war, we must have a modern general staff. An capable army with an incompetent head is a doomed one, and the style of command many of our generals are accustomed to has largely fallen out of the times. We must take advantage of returning cadets from Baoding Military Academy and foreign schools to build a modern general staff, both in our individual armies and on a national level.
A Thorough Logistical Chain
Superior logistics have always been the key to victory in war, but rapid innovations across the last century have made it evermore potent. With trains, trucks, and an ever growing supply chain needed to feed, arm, and reinforce a modern army, a formalised and professional system is essential. Careful and centralised planning and procurement must be developed by our quartermasters, especially if we wish to send forces outside of our home provinces.
Guangdong's Troughs, Guangxi's Peaks
What we may not have in weapons or technology, we can make up for with our superior grasp of the land. Foreign invaders may come to Liangguang expecting an easy fight, but they will quickly fall victim to our rolling hills and mighty rivers. The transition of our local troops from regional militia to devastating light infantry may be a slow one, but it is essential to building an army capable of defending our homes.
Local Officer Initiative
For all the improvements in technology and tactics, the fundamentals that make for a great army remain the same. Small group leadership and independent initiative by inspiring officers win little battles that add up across campaign. Often local commanders know better of local conditions than their distant generals. We must teach our men to take charge, while still keeping the big picture in mind.
Victory Through Combined Arms
At the end of the day, our advisors warned us that we will always be fighting an asymmetrical war. Still, through their efforts and our own, we have found a way to maximise all the different branches of our army to their fullest advantage - the infantry hold the frontline, the irregulars the countryside, while elite mobile units act as a flexible reserve, puncture enemy weak-points as they emerge. Together, we can take down much greater foes.
Strength Through Mobility
The German military mission to the Zhili Clique brought with them ideas of mobile warfare, a doctrine centred around speed. While the industrial powers of the West utilise mechanised and armour divisions to achieve their needs of speed, we will achieve mobility in infantry, armed with light machine guns and trench mortars. We will seek to emulate Lettow-Vorbeck's example, and eventually surpass even his feats!
Modern Communication Networks
Core to a modern army is the utilisation of new technologies. The development of new communication technologies have played a central role in revolutionising how wars may be waged, and our military must make acknowledge this. A modern military must always be following the technological advancements of the time, or they will fall behind. We will not suffer the fate of the late Qing Dynasty, we will always remain one step ahead of our enemies.
Unity of Defence and Industry
A modern army cannot be developed without the necessary industries to fuel its needs. Nearly half of German military aid to China was economic in nature, and with large swathes of Northern China in our hands, we will utilise all captured industrial centres and arsenals. Whereas the Zhili Clique squandered their use with petty warlord disputes, we will use them to field an army loyal to the republic above all else!
Modern Railway Networks
In order to have a truly mobile army, transportation across China must be modernised. Not only will this help with our logistics chain, but more rails will go a long way towards exploitation of the natural resources in China. Connecting rails across the nation will allow us to more effectively defend all regions, and respond quickly to threats, be they internal or external.
Cult of the Innovative Officer
A good officer is more than a capable tactician and fighter; no, a good officer takes initiative to experiment with new and revolutionary ideas of warfare. We need an officer corps staffed with those who think outside of the box, those who can compensate for our technological backwardness and fight off all enemies who wish to dominate our nation. Let us exalt this new type of officer as the vanguard of the Chinese military!
Formulating Defensive Lines
Despite our modernisation efforts, it is clear that China remains behind technologically when compared to the Russian bear in the north and the Empire of the Rising Sun in the east. We undoubtedly cannot hold the entirety of the country, but we will make use of the terrain and essential supply and railway points to mark areas where we must consolidate our forces for an unbreakable defence.
The Nation as a Frontline
While China may be lacking in extensive and modern industry, our nation is blessed with manpower and land in plenty. The enemy will never be able to match us blood for blood, and we have space to lose in the name of time. We will bide our time, pull our enemies deeper into China to overextend their lines, and launch the counter offensive when the time is ripe.
Neutralising Enemy Air Power
In this age of warfare, the land force is often supplemented by fighters and bombers in the sky. While we aspire to make use of combined arms as best we can, the Chinese air force simply cannot march the industrial powers of the west, or the Empire of Japan. We will instead endeavour to neutralise their advantage in the air with anti-air guns and even the playing field.
Primacy of the Southern School
In America, the best and brightest cadets go to West Point, where they are bred into capable officers. In China, the Kuomintang developed the Whampoa Military Academy in the ideals of the Three Principles and Sun Yat-sen's will. However, we seek to not construct an army of revolutionary fanatics, but a professional officers corp. We will emulate Washington's example, and forge an academy capable of producing the next Sun Tzu, the next Zhuge Liang!
Prussia of the East
At long last, China's military reforms have developed a modern army. German military thought is pervasive throughout our new army corps, with General Hans von Seeckt's \
Supremacy of the New Model Army
Humiliation taught the Qing Dynasty that reform was necessary. However, sheer imperial incompetence produced the Beiyang army, a force tainted by corruption on all levels, and staffed with buffoonish officers like Yuan Shikai. Now, our reforms have produced a new army that China can be proud of, one where loyalty is to the very nation and not the purse strings. We have become what the Beiyang Army could not be, a shining example of modernity in the Middle Kingdom.
The Legion of the Republic
Much like the Roman Republic and the United States, our republic stands for great virtues respected by all who live under the flag. While the Kuomintang utilised the slogans of chaotic revolutionary zeal, we stand for true republican ideals, not professed loyalty to a party drenched in autocracy. While the northern warlords fight in nepotist squabbles, our military stands for the nation itself. We will defend China, defend republicanism!
Legacy of Whampoa
Years ago, on the docks of Whampoa, a military academy was established by the Kuomintang with the help of Red Russian exiles with the hope of creating a truly revolutionary army. They were not the best armed, they were not the best led, but for all their failings the National Revolutionary Army became legendary for their utter conviction in their party's cause. In this revolutionary spirit, we shall establish a new academy to seek out true revolutionary patriots for our cause!
Will Wins Wars
Whether it be the revolutionary zeal of the Bolsheviks, the heroism of the White Volunteer Army, or the Bushido code of the Samurai, great victories have come out of lesser armies through the utter tenacity and dedication of its soldiers. Our men was be inoculated with ideological fervour, taught in fine detail the lofty ideals they are fighting for. They will fight and die without hesitation.
Exalt the Martyrs
Since the early days of the Xinhai Revolution, brave young men armed sometimes with nothing but a blade or a grenade would charge better armed Manchu troops, leading the way for the revolutionaries to topple the old order. Today, as the fate of China is decided, we must cultivate another generation of courageous martyrs, the shock troopers that will irrigate our revolution with their blood.
Establishment of the Zhongyangjun
We will strive to create the finest army in all of China, and at the tip of the spear will be several elite divisions trained in the latest Western style and led by our brightest cadets. Imbued with unparalleled will and ceaselessly trained, they will sooner die than surrender. These units will be the first into breaches, exploiting enemy weak-points and turning the tide of battle under the cover of pounding artillery.
The Renaissance of Methodology
Slowly but surely, our men will be able to penetrate even well entrenched warlord units. Like clockwork, a combination of spotters, artillery, and shock infantry will find and pierce the weakest parts of our foes' forward defences across the front line. Afterwards, reserve units will flood through the openings, taking on enemy reserves that try to stop them, eviscerating enemy formations.
Quality at the Forefront
Modern Russian doctrine calls for quality over quantity. While old stereotypes remain about Russian and Chinese armies alike, what will set us apart from the corrupt, bloated armies of the warlords is the superiority of our wills and our weapons. We do not have much, but what we do have will be the best. We will train an elite army, properly equipped and led, that will sweep away those that oppose us.
Songbirds of Hellfire
Puncturing enemy lines will require us to mass large amounts of artillery into grand batteries, able to concentrate fire on wavering points in the enemy line. Artillery is a precious resource in China, and the logistics often difficult, but with extensive training in coordination between scouts, commanders, infantry, and artillery we can shatter even some of the best fortified enemy lines.
Constituting Tradition
In order to best exploit a breakthrough in enemy tactical zones and cause havoc in the rear lines, we must create an effective cavalry corps that can more speedily across rough terrain. Cavalry is the core of our second echelon forces, combining firepower with mobility to overrun our enemies before they can regroup. They will target communications hubs and supply depots, severing their ability to fight.
Battle in Depth
Battle in Depth is the latest development in Russian military theory, the evolution of centuries of warfare. Integrating multiple front-sized operations across several levels of operations, we can take on even the most advanced armies in China. Keeping up with military doctrines and technology, especially regarding manoeuvre, is vital in a landscape where many foreign powers have already spent years training and equipping our rivals.
Spirit of the Country
The soldiers of the New China must love their country. They must forsake local allegiances and ties to warlords for the sake of protecting the Motherland. As such, we must instill, this spirit of enthusiasm and nationalist zeal within our ranks.
Modern Revolutionary Soldier
Standing above all of their peers in China, the National Revolutionary Army was famed for their comparatively modern arms and equipment. Towering above the warlords, we should strive to emulate such superiority in the common soldier. No longer shall the Chinese soldier be seen as a backwards bandit, but as a contemporary of both West and East.
Instilling the National Bushido
Extolling the virtues presented by the famed Samurai of Japan, and other elite formations throughout history, the new China takes great pride in the ferocious mentality instilled in its cadets. Never faltering, the cadres the revolution will fight to the bitter end for the cause and the nation, and so we must place special emphasis on such a fact, for the new generations of cadets.
Modern Arms in the Middle Kingdom
The successes of our prior engagements show the absolute priority needed in maintaining our edge in the global arms race, for if any foreign power were to step into the Chinese theatre, we must be able to fight back with intense force. To this end, additional funds must be allocated to our budding domestic arms industry, for Chinese arms should be renowned around the world.
Suzhan, Sujue
A new dawn of warfare is upon us. Since the first light of tanks in the Weltkrieg, modern warfare has shifted to the superiority of a nation's capacity to produce and utilise swift mechanised and mobile divisions to pierce through enemy lines, and rapidly overrun their forces. Developing our own armoured forces, we must prioritise Suzhan, Sujue. Decisive attacks that inevitably force a quick conclusion.
Annihilate Enemy Fortifications
Renowned for the combined advance of tenacious infantry and thundering artillery, the National Revolutionary Army was capable of making striding advances, no matter what fort or foe stood in its way. It is of the greatest priority that our generals be trained in the most premier utilisation of artillery, and that new pieces be supplied to our whole army, for we can ill afford a stalemate caused by enemy defences.
Power of Tenacity
Tenacity, revolutionary fervour, absolute devotion. These are all hallmarks of China's finest. We should reward such virtues by taking the best of the best and incorporating them into dedicated special forces, focused on succeeding where the average soldier cannot. For the valour and praise won in such operations will surely raise the rest of the army with them.
Amassing Dedicated Artillery
Lacking in industry, and with limited capacity to expand operations, the inherent desire for an artillery force comparative to the finest armies in the world has led our nation to direct all efforts towards maintaining a stockpile of the finest modern pieces capable of obliterating enemy divisions. The Chinese army will be feared, for with every footsoldier's advance, a shower of shells shall precede them.
Stalwart Souls
Our virtuous soldiers are distinguished for their abilities to outperform the impossible. Time and time again, the Chinese soldier has been pitted against difficult odds and come out the victor. Never again shall we fall to the humiliating position of the Qing, used as a puppet by imperialist powers. The Chinese people are stalwart in the defence of their nation, and so too shall its army.
Dedicated Hearts
Every Chinese Soldier understands that their dreams, their hopes, their moments of happiness, it doesn't matter as they lie bleeding out on the battlefield. Everyone dies. Yet does it mean that their lives, the lives of their comrades, were they meaningless? The memory of the fallen serves as a permanent example as to the dedication of the Chinese soldier. No matter the cost, they will defend what they prize most dear, the nation, their loved ones, all of it.
Army for a Nation
To unify the country, we must first unify the spirit and mind of the army. The Chinese soldier must understand they are fighting for their country of China rather than just their local provinces, towns, and villages. Now more than ever, they must dedicate their hearts to the revolutionary spirit of those before them.
Mobilise the Pearl Delta's Might
China's tragic descent into the Century of Humiliation was precipitated by its failure to industrialise. Its ensuing efforts to catch up continually fell short. But we can ill afford to sit and bemoan the past. With what industry we do have, we must use to the fullest, bringing to bear Chinese grit and ingenuity against our rivals at home and the circling imperialist carrion abroad.
Secure Foreign Benefactors
For better or for worse, China's continued division and underdeveloped industrial potential means there is little large-scale weapons research and development. Many Chinese designs are foreign in origin, produced either with legitimate licenses or shamelessly reverse engineered and copied. Still, Chinese engineers have found plenty of areas for modification and improvement, a testament to our craftiness.
Expand the Guangdong Arsenal
The Guangdong Arsenal is perhaps the province's largest centre of military industry. Capable of churning out rifles for the revolving door of provincial armies, it has become an essential cornerstone for Liangguang's defence. We must continue to invest in further machinery, staff, and infrastructure, allowing us a critical industrial edge over our enemies. Cantonese industrial might will win us the day.
Swell Military Production
It is not enough for us to simply rely on Guangdong Arsenal or the menagerie of weapons warlord clans in Liangguang have collected over the years from underground purchases. If we are to survive a changing battlefield, we must be willing to rapidly expand subsidiary military production facilities, producing equipment ranging from rifles to grenades to gas masks, even venturing to produce artillery and trucks.
Combine the Aviation Programs
The warlord era may have sapped the nation of its treasure and unity, but it has not robbed it of its imagination. Men continued to look to the skies, and daring military officers soon followed. Even poor warlords raced with the central government to develop aerial capabilities, though like many Chinese projects they have been plagued by ineptitude, poor funding, and corruption. But if we were to unite Liangguang's efforts, it is not too late to win the skies!
Recall the Pilot Trainers
The world's fascination with the soaring feats of post war aviators has inspired many young Chinese men to seek our opportunities to learn how to fly. Likewise, various governments and even some private pilots have sought to court Chinese warlords, leveraging their (relatively rare) aviation experience as a powerful bargaining chip. If we are to build an air fleet, we must seek out this expertise where we can find it.
Construct Aircraft Plants
As we seek to build an air force of our own, we must not fall to the temptation of over-reliance on foreign suppliers, especially with the shifting international political climate. Plans are underway to build Guangdong Aircraft Repair Plant at Dongshan and to expand the plant at Shaoguan. Our staff have also drawn up plans for additional assembly plants deeper in Guangxi where they are less vulnerable.
Establish A Central Aviation Academy
With a final consolidation of our forces within China, we can finally pursue the goals of so many disparate Chinese factions throughout the Warlord Era. Too underfunded, mismanaged, or otherwise, prior Chinese attempts to establish a Central Aviation Academy and airforce have all ended in meager disappointment. However with a renewed effort of consolidation and integration, our forces will soon dominate the skies.
Cultivating a Chinese Airforce
Whilst Chinese industry and resources are more than sufficient to produce a suitable air force, our contemporaries within Europe and America have years, even decades of technological advancement in the school of flight. However with numerous outsider connections, ample currency, and plenty of experts available, we should seek to hire foreign expertise to further advance our own flight programme.
Air-Land Integration
One of the most devastating enhancements to warfare brought forth by the modern age is the integration of combined air-land offensive and defensive manoeuvres. With the utilisation of various tactical and close air-support bombers and swift moving soldiers, the Chinese army is sure to excel on the battlefield. No longer shall Chinese warfare be dominatedb by the outdated tactics of the past era, but of the direct air support of the next.
The Tactical Air War
The capacity of our fighters and bombers to be able to pursue not just strategic, but tactical objectives is surely not to be underutilised. With a focus on conducting air missions targeting tactical targets such as military infrastructure, factories and alike, we shall not only cripple our enemies armies, but their ability to wage war too.
Airborne Special Service
Inspired by developments throughout the world, our government has witnessed the expansion and creation of various elite paratrooper divisions, with the capacity to be deployed behind enemy supply lines for special missions requiring the utmost in skill and training. Such brave tactics are sure to result in numerous casualties, but these divisions are surely the future of warfare, in the palms of our hands!
The XP-0 Project
Inspired by various Russian fighters, namely the MiG-1, the XP-0 (developed by famed officer Chu Chia-Jen) is China's first attempt at a native fighter design. Armed with 4x20 mm Hispano-Suiza underwing cannons and with the capacity to additionally carry bombs, the goal of the XP-0 is to reduce China's dependency on foreign aircraft, and instead inspire our own native aviation industry.
National Military Aviation Programme
With our renewed efforts to develop our own domestic aviation industry and academy, the government has still found the overall number of planes in our skies and airfields to be drastically insufficient to protect the nation. Through another revitalised effort, with a focus on streamlining protection, may the Chinese airforce be forever feared and admired!
Prepare Air Defences
Even if our valiant fighters and pilots serve tirelessly in the darkness and the night to protect our nation, there will be times where not ever their dedicated heroism can prevent the enemies' own air fleet. For times like these, we must call upon our brave and willing soldiers to man various anti-air installations throughout the most integral cities within the country.
Centralise Air Doctrine
Whilst our airforce may be blooming ever so wonderfully, in combined efforts, many observers have brought critiques of the disarray in doctrine practised by individual units, another ghost from the previous Chinese airforce attempts. Ultimately to exorcise such a spectre, we must work to centralise our air doctrine behind a coherent one, understood by all.
Defend the Coasts
Fortunately, the Chinese mainland sits upon the Eurasian landmass, and so any invasion from the West must cross the Himalayas, Siberia, or even the vast expanses of Central Asia. Yet there remains a critical weakpoint of the Chinese coastline, for if any enemy were to best our navy, we would be defenceless. Let us invest in a naval bomber fleet to devastate enemy fleets from the coast!
Kings of the Southwest Skies
Truly the heroes of our airforce are its aces. Striving to fight above and beyond the standard call of duty, they continue to serve the nation dutifully in life, and in death. Fostering such sensibilites within our airforce is sure to breed generations upon generations of brave heroes, daring to take to the skies for China! For we are forever Kings of the Southwest Skies, wherever and whenever we soar!
Expand Guangdong Naval Academy
Guangdong, long a centre of global maritime trade, has similarly benefited from a large, experienced seafaring community. Protecting this trade similarly has pushed Guangdong to develop a naval tradition of its own, culminating in the formation of Guangdong Naval Academy. While the primarily land-based needs of the warlord era has caused significant neglect, it is not too late for us to reverse course and expand seats at the academy.
Purchase Light Patrol Craft
The Guangdong provincial government's traditional focus has been on light craft capable of patrolling the Pearl River. Torpedo boats, minesweepers, and gunboats, humble by global standards, are nevertheless the bedrock of our fleet. Staffing this flotilla will be the first steps in building a modern Cantonese naval tradition capable of competing with our old rivals in Fujian, Shandong, and Jiangnan.
Invest in Guangnan Shipyard
The Guangdong provincial government has traditionally sponsored a small, brown water fleet meant to protect inland rivers and coastal ports. But with the protection the Legation cities and their great power backers have provided now waning, it is critical we develop some naval capabilities of our own, lest we lose any hope of maintaining our sovereignty over the seas. Investing in Guangnan Shipyard shall foment a new naval tradition in a new era!
Reorganise the Republican Navy
Whilst limited in resources currently, there exists a plethora of experts on fighting on the high seas, who have recently been put out of a job. Through the contacts and connections with the old remnants of the Republican Navy, we can use these men and their skills for goals ultimately benefiting the nation. Whilst the ships may be unsalvagable, their talents aren't.
Refurbish Chinese Dockyards
Considered to be outdated blights on the coastline, the Chinese shipping industry of today is a sight for sore eyes. Whilst plenty capable of producing for economic and civilian use, when it comes to military means, we are drastically out engineered. Through expert use of investments and manpower, we can produce new dockyards for the Chinese fleet of tomorrow!
Modernise Coastal Defences
Ever a consistent weakpoint to our defence stratagems, our long and beautiful coastline is practically an open invitation to any invaders from the sea. To remedy this, we must restructure and modernise our currently outdated coastal defences, and bring forth an impenetrable coastline for the modern age.
Ingenuity at our Fingertips
For the past decades, naval doctrines have never been the priority for any Chinese government, be it the Zhili, or Fengtian, the main theatre of warfare in China has always been the land. Due to this, our adversaries and contemporary countries alike host modern curriculums studying the cutting edge of naval warfare. A new curriculum inspired by modern developments must be taught to our admirals.
Six Year Programme
Inspired by plans proposed by the government to achieve a capacity of 600,000 tons in 6 years, the Navy has been given the go ahead to fully implement their radical development programme. Relentless in their approach, hundreds of ships are to be constructed, alongside the requisite dockyards to produce them. Finally the Chinese fleet will rule the high seas.
Chinese Wolf Packs
Alongside modern advancements of naval doctrine has come the intrepid, stealthy march of submarine warfare. Merely a novelty in the previous era, now a fully practised mode of naval combat, submarine wolfpacks yield an exceptional capability to raid enemy supply lines and capitulate hefty capital ships, without requiring nearly as much material investment.
Marines of the Republic
Having been a tradition in the Chinese navy for almost as long as the Republic itself. The Marine Corps of the Republic of China has existed since 1914, where it was clutched from the wretches of the old Navy Sentry Corps, and transformed into reasonable force capable of conducting naval landings. Once more, we shall reinvigorate our naval infantry, to project power on foreign shores.
New Spirit of Maritime Life
Through our efforts, the Chinese navy has truly received a second chance at life. With valour and vigour instilled, new ships in production, and bounding campaigns on the horizon, our navy is no longer the laughing stock of Asia. The RCN is sure to rival that of the Kaiserliche Marine and the Imperial Japanese Navy.
Exporting the Revolution Overseas
As proven by the German victory in the Weltkrieg, the ultimate zero sum factor of naval warfare is that of quantity of battleships each side has. The hulking monstrosities are capable of dominating any engagement, and with advancements all around the world, our navy must work to secure its sphere of influence. Towering amongst giants, the Chinese navy will be felt around the globe.
Guangdong's Naval Tradition
Overstepping our boundaries following recent unification is sure to result in the hammer striking the anvil. Whilst our navy is in its relevant modern infancy, let us focus on smaller ships and fleets. Revitalising Guangdong's naval tradition, the China seas shall become a hub of Chinese trade once more. With the intent on focusing on protecting our coastline and convoys, the safety of Chinese shipping is sure to be secured!
China's Gravest Hour
Flags are fluttering, sword is drawn, and gun on our shoulders. That which we have come to fear, has finally come at last and now our centuries' old civilisation risks total cultural and racial annihilation at the hands of the Japanese imperialists. It is time to put petty warlord squabbles away from us, for us to bury the hatchet, and for us, the Chinese people to unite once more in the face of this adversity!
The Chinese Hindenburg Line
China's vast land expanse means that the enemy will most likely attempt a naval invasion of our country rather than a direct land invasion. Given the economic and political importance of the coastal regions, we would do well to prepare in advance of the enemy's invasion by fortifying and preparing the coastline with bunkers, pillboxes, and other defences - creating our very own Hindenburg line.
Wartime Industry Relocation
With much of China's domestic and military industries located along the coastal regions of the country, they will no doubt come under pressure and attack from the enemy. In order to preserve our industrial capabilities, we will seek to move not just industries, but also heavy machinery and civilians into the country's interior so we can fight on and exhaust the enemy's advance.
Heroic Revolutionary Fighters
Our soldiers are like no others. In the face of complete annihilation at the face of the foreign intruders, they continue to display relentless bravery and patriotism. With guns in hand, ferocity in their hearts, and an undying will, may we exalt our brave revolutionary fighters, as they continue to fight both in life and death. Forwards!
One Thousand Sons, One Thousand Soldiers
It is true that an army feeds on its stomach. As the enemy marches across our beloved great country, his supplies lines grow increasingly thin and he will grow emboldened as we seem to fall back towards the interior. In times of crisis, all must be expected to give up whatever they may have in order to achieve the final victory. We will seek to utilise anything of use we may find in the countryside, before attacking our exhausted enemies through the means of guerrilla warfare.
Prepare Guerrilla Cells
Even if we cannot match the enemy in the sea, in the air, or in conventional combat; there are ways that a people can fight. From every town, village, and farm; we will encourage all who are willing to fight for their country's salvation to create resistance groups. They will lay in wait behind enemy lines; in order to wreck havoc and destruction among the enemies' morale, supply, and logistical capabilities.
Blockade Runners
Incapable of posing anything more than a papercut to the foreign invader's navies, we lament that we cannot extend our protection beyond our immediate coastline. Outside of our harbours, our rivers, and our airfields, the enemy is perfectly capable of cutting off major foreign shipments using their navy. It is imperative that we develop strategies and ships capable of evading enemy patrols and circumventing the blockade.
Begin the Yue-Gui Three Year Plan
Canton (Guangzhou) has long prospered because of its exclusive access to foreign trade. The Canton System carved a southern economy partially independent of the rest of China, to our strategic advantage. Nonetheless, the northern warlords prevailed over us thanks to our infighting and their foreign aid. To survive, we must join together Yue (Guangdong) industrial might and Gui (Guangxi) material resources.
The Good Earth
Life in the Chinese countryside continues to be plagued by poverty and strife as the Chinese nation turns a new page away from its agrarian past. Guangxi has it worse of the two Guangs, with its rugged terrain, fewer available capital, and rampant banditry. The leading theorists disagree about the direction the province must take - mirroring the continued disagreements between intellectuals across the nation.
Land-Rent Caps
Many farmers do not own the land they endlessly till throughout the year. The most common form of tenancy is fixed payment in kind, then share cropping, and cash rental the least common. Share cropping arrangements often require a 50/50 split, and renters are often charged 10-20% of land value. Payment is often expected even during blights. Regulations capping rent at 37.5% and requiring six months notice before eviction will protect our farmers from extortion.
Deal with the Peasants' Association
The Peasants' Associations organised by Peng Pai and other agrarian socialists have long been a thorn to the side of the revolving door of governments in Liangguang, befuddling even ostensibly leftist ones. Still, while governments have come and go, the peasants and their struggles remain. To show our commitment, we must work with the honest ones in good faith, and sideline the radical factions.
Form the Farmers Bank of Guangxi
Farmers live in a cycle of perpetual debt, taking on loans in the spring in hopes of reaping a fruitful harvest in the fall. To alleviate their plight, a farmer's bank will be created to lend money to rural granaries and farmers, accepting grain as collateral. Credit Offices for the Common People are to developed by shopkeepers under government regulation to facilitate rural business. We will not leave our farmers behind.
Root Out Guangxi Banditry
A campaign against the bandits, the vile men who rob and bully the hard-working peasants of the land, will commence at once. Guangxi will be divided into twelve militia regions, with district magistrates given wide discretionary powers to root out these vagrants. These militias will patrol the roads and villages, while our security forces root out the hills and mountains. Guangxi will be a home to bandits no more.
The Guangdong Cooperatives Plan
Guangdong has been home to several attempts at creating a workable rural cooperatives programme, an attempting to organise farmers into workable economic units. The Guangdong Cooperative Commission has been authorised to take the lead in the latest iteration of this plan, though the priority must be national integration, even if it means sacrificing village autonomy for the sake of unification.
Ambitious Water Control Projects
Guangxi receives heavy rainfall annually, its inconsistency causes both droughts or flooding. Deforestation due to slash and burn agriculture has worsened floods, and some 80% of farmlands we have tested show excessive acidity caused by soaked roots of vegetation throwing off carbon dioxide. If we are to turn this farmer's bane into a boon, we must undertake massive provincial water control projects.
Promote Harmonious Land Cooperation
The solution to the crushing poverty in the countryside is not redistribution, which only creates chaos and makes everyone equally poor. Rather, we must create local public capital for the benefit of all people. Village finances must go into building granaries, dikes, holding pools, fish ponds, and markets for the benefit of the people, and expropriation limited only to the untilled lands of absentee owners.
Ally with the Sugar Barons
Feng Rui, a local sugar magnate, has drafted a plan for five new sugar districts, each equipped with three factories. Heavy regulations will squeeze out any rivals, ensuring our government and its allies will have an effective monopoly. The sugar trade is expected to be immensely profitable as we secure distributors across the entire Yangtze region including the competitive and lucrative Shanghai market.
Intensify Wet Rice Production
The College of Agriculture of National Guangxi University and Guangxi Agricultural Experimentation Station have done great work in increasing wet field rice yields. This included promotion of new seed strains imported from Guangdong and also the introduction of potatoes, a nutritious crop which can be planted during the autumn and winter while rice fields normally lay fallow.

Guangxi Infrastructure Development Scheme
Perhaps the most visible sign of our commitment to Liangguang's reconstruction is our mass road and highway building projects, both Guangxi and Guangdong each are expected to exceed all other provinces except perhaps Shandong. Built primarily through corvee labour or by mobilising the unemployed, it has had the added benefit of aiding in our bandit suppression efforts, to the delight of the locals.
Rural Educational Effort
The call of various reformist intellectuals across China to eradicate illiteracy must not go unheeded. Whether it be the slums in Guangzhou or the farthest reaches of Guangxi, every child ought to have access to a primary school education - if not for their sake for the advancement of the nation. Teachers are in short supply, money is thin, but our determination to build new school buildings is limitless.
Expand Guangdong Universities
Guangdong is home to several large-scale education facilities, though many have fallen into neglect thanks to the ongoing warlord era. We must mobilise the patriotic students and thinkers of the province, investing what wealth we can into scholarships, grants, and other educational programs to get an edge over our rivals. A new age dawns, and we will be ready for the challenge.
Simplify Tax and Duties
The people are crushed under the weight of burdensome taxation, as competing factions and interest groups extort overlapping fees. This stifles trade, causes severe unrest, and strengthens local tyrants at the expense of the provincial government. We must streamline taxation, abolish special duties and tax farming, balance the budget and bring everything under the control of the provincial treasury.
Harness Southern Industrial Might
The industrial portion of our Three Year Plan calls for the creation of a solid foundation for industrialisation by ambitious projects including the construction of 24 new factories in Guangdong as well as additional industrial infrastructure such as hydroelectric plants, iron and steel mills, and even fuel refineries, as well as training a large modern industrial workforce capable of staffing these new projects.
Develop Guangdong's Rails
The lack of railroads has long forced Liangguang to depend on the river for transportation. While that is unlikely to change in the near future, it is vital that we develop efficient transportation infrastructure where we can, particularly along the Guangzhou-Hankou line. Moreover, we must break ground in local highway projects, helping us clear out bandits and allow for greater economic integration.
Promote the Cement Industry
Guangdong already has a fairly established cement industry in Guangzhou, Henan, and Xicun thanks to municipal construction projects guaranteeing a stable market, so further capital investment is thankfully not needed. That said, we can place heavy de facto duties on foreign cement and requiring the use of local cement, ensuring the industry's profitability as we \
Domestic Textile Industries
Cloth and yarn represents the single highest import in Guangxi, and nationalist figures in both Guangdong and Guangxi have called for an expansion of domestic light industry to meet these needs rather than continue to rely on foreign purchases. A government sponsored Meilu Linen Goods Factory has been mired by delays. With further funding and attention, one final push will complete this project.
Qiongya's Green Gold
Qiongya is an extremely resource rich island, home to reserves of iron, tungsten, copper, gold, silver, and other valuable metals on top of various cash crops. Its capture by the Kuomintang during the 1920s was an extensive boom to Sun's fledging government. We must make the most out of the island, providing extensive investment and tapping into its material wealth to fuel our growing industrial base.
The Wealth of the Hinterlands
The mountains of Guangxi and its history of poverty and banditry has long prevented the exploitation of its vast mineral reserves. But the growing needs of our war machine and the consolidation of control our Three Year Plan brings us deeper into the provincial hinterlands. We will build the necessary infrastructure and investment to open up what was once seen as an inaccessible backwater to the rest of China.
Addressing the Urban Plight
The suffering of Guangzhou's poorest have not gone unnoticed. Although genuine care and alms giving does exist, many see the city's poor as a resource to be exploited and even small acts of aid politicised. Various political actors both left and right have worked either with or to subvert the dominance of the Ten Charitable Halls but it is time now for our government to act on its own initiative.
Promote Pearl River Trade
The Pearl River is the economic lifeblood of Liangguang, bringing trade up and down the river for centuries. At the end sits the Pearl River Delta, home to major export cities such as Guangzhou (Canton), Hong Kong, and Macau. The wealth this has generated has created prosperity, but an unequal one. Despite this, we must push onwards to connect our two provinces to each other and the world.
Protect the Trade Balance
For too long, the Chinese people have been exploited by Western Imperialists and their Comprador lackeys. From their coastal concessions, they extract the wealth of the land, leaving us to suffer in poverty. We must reverse the trade balance and build self-sufficiency. We can start by promoting simpler dress and a more disciplined lifestyle for our people as we gear up for a long economic campaign.
Mobilise the Guangzhou Syndicates
Guangzhou is a centre of union activism in China thanks to its relatively high industrialisation, sympathetic government factions, and its history as the cradle of the Chinese Syndicalist movement. Their revolutionary, anti-concessionist fervour, if correctly mobilised and controlled, is essential to our efforts to organise the workers and check the power of the Merchant Corps' thugs.
Nationalise Foreign Assets
With the world's attention shifting away from China and a growing sense of unease among investors about the future prospects of their investments, many have chosen to liquidate their investments in face of Black Monday. But they cannot as easily move physical capital, and we shall ensure that we purchase integral Guangzhou infrastructure at a fair price...with a little \
Regional Fiscal Independence
While it would be impossible for us to achieve true autarky, we have come a long way in keeping our province on sound economic footing while avoiding over-dependence on outside, subversive actors. Foreign treaties and their unfair trade terms continue to be subverted by our de facto tariffs, as we dare the wretched imperialists to enforce them now. Anyone that trades with us must do it on equal terms.
Seek Continued External Investment
Provincialism has long been a bane of Chinese development. Despite the fact that the vast majority of experts aiding us in economic reconstruction in Liangguang are from outside the two provinces, even those from within a province are sometimes seen as foreigners. We must work to integrate the best of what Chinese and foreign ideas have to offer, propelling Liangguang to modernity.
Facilitating Cross-Border Exports
We must build and expand our profitable relationship with the concessions, particularly Hong Kong and Macau. Although the trade terms thus far have been largely unequal, we will make the most of it to ensure a more prosperous future for our people. Furthermore, we must take down trade barriers between our two provinces, further opening up the Pearl River as an economic artery to our heartland.
Alliance with the Merchants
The Yue Merchants have banded together in their Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce, investing heavily into their militias out of fear of socialist radicals and bandit raids. But this not only destabilises our security but also cuts into their profits. The Provincial Government and the bourgeoisie must work together as partners, so that we can generate wealth that will lift all people in Liangguang.
A Thriving Southeastern Entrepôt
The central problem plaguing China is that there simply was not enough wealth for everyone. The warlords, bandits, and socialists all fought for the scraps, tearing each other and the nation apart while plunging China into a spiral of destruction and poverty. The true way out of China's malaise is and was to promote peace and build rather than destroy. Through our efforts, we have brought Liangguang together to create an island of prosperity amidst China's anarchy.
A Model for the Nation
The people of China, long disappointed by the continued failures of the Beiyang central government, look far and wide in desperation for hope. In our two provinces, vastly different though they may be, we have created a new vision for the future. A model for change. A blueprint for prosperity. As we turn the page from the Three Year Plan and go forward, no matter what destiny has in store history will remember the accomplishments we have made in Liangguang.
Cradle of the National Revolution
After being cast out and driven underground by Yuan Shikai and the treacherous Beiyang government, the Tongmenghui was reborn in Guangzhou. Second chances soon became third, and now this is perhaps our last opportunity to free China from its enslavement and carry out Dr. Sun's will. Once more, Guangzhou finds itself the bulwark of national salvation and nurturer to our revolutionary future!
Intensify Propaganda Efforts
\
Consolidate the Revolutionary Junta
Although our end goal is a free, prosperous and democratic republic, the sordid realities of the warlord era has required the formation of a party-state operating under the principles of tutelage. The provisional council that rules Guangzhou must differentiate itself from the warlords surrounding them by operating collegially as true comrades in a democratic-centralist model, combining discourse with decisiveness.
Subdue the Gentry
The gentry have long operated independently of the provincial government, the bane of agrarian reform and the root of peasant unrest. The Kuomintang have long had an uneasy relationship with the landlord classes, and in our absence the warlords that have come after us have allowed the gentry to further entrench themselves. We must break their haughty power and bring them to heel, there is always the question of how far...
Revitalise Primary School Education
The Kuomintang have a deep-seated commitment to expanding access to public education, including the eradication of illiteracy and the proper instruction of Dr. Sun's teachings to the masses. Guangxi, with its education system lagging behind, requires significant effort to catch up, including the mass construction or conversion of buildings into schools in every village and four year high schools in every district.
Expand Social Services
The third of Dr. Sun's principles is Minsheng: guaranteeing the welfare and livelihood of the nation. The needs of our revolution has placed such great demands on the people, and it is only right that we return their faith with tangible protections for the poor and suffering. Given the abject poverty of the province, the New Guangxi clique is expected to benefit the most from these policies, leveraging it as a means of inspiration...and control.
A Kuomintang United Front
There was a time when the Chinese Kuomintang was united, joined together by a shared devotion to Dr. Sun and the Three Principles. But such unity quickly vanished following his death, and now the party trades accusations of being foreign lackeys and doctrinal heretics. But in this dire period of Chinese history, we have little choice but to work together to survive. Let us bury the hatchet, at least for now.
Deal with the Remnants
Guangzhou has long been home to both idealistic dreamers and cynical compradors. As the White Sun flies once again over the city, many have fled to the concessions or hide in their homes in fear of reprisal. Still, plenty remain politically active in spite of fears of repression. It seems that even as governments change, the restless energy of Canton remains. But we must be willing to tame this beast, lest we all perish.
Rally the Mass Movement
It is no secret that our revolution can only be won with the support of the people. Our enemies are better armed, better trained, and the world is with them. But if the people are with us, nothing can stand in our way!
Local Government Initiatives
During the military stage of the revolution, we must immediately deploy party officials to newly liberated territories to train them in self-government. These cadres must work as a vanguard, abolish excessive taxes, protecting the interests of peasants and workers, eradicating loan sharks, and organises public relief. This is the only way to prevent warlordism and to plant the seeds for a better future.
Reach out to Overseas Contacts
The Chinese diaspora stretches from Singapore to Hawaii and have long been patrons of Dr. Sun. Although faith in the movement and the funding that came with it has ebbed, in this last chance for our country's salvation we must make an impassioned appeal for aid. Every last piece of silver and gold shipped, every dollar wired, every volunteer returning home - with enough droplets we get a rising tide.
Return of the Moscow Committee
The great struggle is only just beginning. We reclaim not just our rightful position within the party but also to prepare for our great mission to totally liberate the Chinese peoples against the foreign imperialists and their warlord lackeys. Hu Hanmin, who's shadow looms over all the Kuomintang's right, is coming home. For all comrades who have not forsaken the Three Principles, it is time to come and unite.
The Second Return to Canton
Such is our triumph! Over a decade ago the Yue Army had once marched from Fujian, descending upon the Old Guangxi defilers of Guangdong, and ejecting them from Guangdong. Yet again have we triumphed! Mayor Chen Lianbo would like to have postured himself as the true protector of Cantonese affairs, but the province knows that only her army may shield her from injustice.
Rein in Expenditures
In the Warlord Era troop numbers have skyrocketed to sheer insane levels. Provincial Warlords have spent considerable amounts of their budget on merely maintaining or growing their militaries. The arms race between the North and South Zhili nearly resulted in the bankrupting of the nation, and opened further concessionism. By reducing the military budget, we can allocate more to civilian affairs and local reforms.
Building a New Federalist Coalition
Building a revitalised Federalist China is not a task worthy of short order. The once grand Federalist coalition of the early 1920s constituted multiple provinces, and had the intellectuals of China in its grasp. Yet it fell apart in the mid 1920s, and plummeted even further after the Zhili proved Unification by Subjugation to be the true way forward. However, not all is lost, and with Governor Chen's return, perhaps the Federalist Project shall see the light of day.
Reviving the Guangdong Constitution
The Guangdong Constitution of Chen's last Governorship instituted local democracy on a level never before seen within China. With local village and district level committees, reforms were implemented to allow greater autonomy for policing, self-governance, and elections. Democracy From The Bottom Up
City and village magistrates are the keystone of building the new Federalist democracy. For every district constitutes a county, and they constitute a province. The magistrate must be tasked with suppressing local evildoers, punishing gentry, enforcing compulsory education, promoting local industries, and establish local militias. As for their appointment? They must be curated by having a trusted official travel from county to county, building up a portfolio.
Canton Shows the Way
Governor Chen has long been out of the true seat of power of Guangdong, with the city being swept up by Chen Lianbo and the Merchant Corps since 1927. Finally returning to power proper in the province after a tenure on the backbenches, it is necessary for Chen to transfer the centre of power of the Yue Army from Haifeng unto Canton. Revitalising the city and modernising it, alongside a few backroom deals, the Yue Army shall never be ejected.
An Educational Cornucopia
Through the establishment of an independent executive and budgetary system, and the abolishment of the Department of Education in lieu of an independent Provincial Education Committee, it is hoped that Guangdong shall transform into a hub of intellectualism and forward thinking applications. Of course, financing such endeavours will necessitate a portion of stable revenues such as taxes on tobacco and spirits, and at minimum 20% of the provincial budget.
Intermixing of Triad and Tiandihui
Perhaps an unknown quality of the Public Interest Party is its origins in the Hongmen Overseas Chinese Community. With individuals such as Guan Wensen and Chen Xiaoyue sent to Southeast Asia to generate support for the party, the intermixing of the traditional Fujianese Tiandihui with the Cantonese Triad has become ingratiated with the Party. Managing Guangxi's Reconstruction
A travesty of the Warlord Era and of the Trouble in the Twin Provinces, Guangxi has been devastated by war and bloodshed. With the power of the Old Guangxi Clique seemingly broken for the third time, the societal structure of the province has been ruptured. However, Guangxi itself was a highly militarised province before the recent struggle, and reamins as such. With the Old Guangxi remnants folding into Chen's government, let us begin the time of healing.
Laying Down the Law in Liangguang
To reconstitute order in the chaos following the League Collapse, it is absolutely necessary to control Liangguang's policing and judiciary. Through the expansion of the number of districts and local courts, preferential utilisation of local militia rather than state troops, establishment of a modern police force and police academy alongside new prisons focused on rehabilitation, we shall revolutionise justice within China.
Assuring Our Honest Partners

Heirs of Lu Rongting
Lu Rongting may have perished in the 1930s with a mission left unfinished, but it is his heirs, that of the Old Guangxi Clique, and his rivals, the Merchants and Political Science Clique, that remain to carry the torch of the Liangguang model. With opposition both from the Federalists and the Revolutionaries, it is the old order that has prevailed, and it is the old order that must restore balance to China.
Putting Down the Spectre of 1927
Ever since the failed Northern Expedition, the Kuomintang have long been a shallow vestige of its former self. With one last hurrah in the face of the Shanghai Uprising in 1932, they have continued to exert an increasingly diminished presence within the nation. Their Central Committees lie in exile in Moscow and Paris, and their operations within MinGan and Guizhou are undeniably running on limited time. Let us help expediate things further.
Approaching the Yue Clique
Still a formidable presence despite being overshadowed by the presence of Shen Hongying and Chen Lianbo, the Yue Clique exerts itself within Chaomei and the surrounding areas as a certified stronghold of, at least in overtones, Federalism. In an effort to secure their support, or more accurately, to enable them to put down their arms, it would be prudent for the provincial government to come to terms and compromise with Chen Jiongming's subordinates.
Legacy of the Cohong
The Cohong was once the only way for Western powers to trade within Chinese markets. A legalised merchant monopoly by the Qing, the Cohong was the sole arbiter of any and all trade travelling through and out of Canton, but it was ultimately disbanded with the conclusion of the First Opium War. However, many of its descendants form the ranks of the present day Cantonese merchant society, and it is through generations of wealth that they can assert their influence.
Relief of the Rurals
One cannot blame the peasantry for turning to the demagoguery or mass populist appeal of the Kuomintang revolutionaries, for their lot in life has often been hard, and rife with injustice. But it is merely the humble order of Chinese society that they serve their purpose dutifully, and without complaint. In order to restore harmony to the countryside, we must but first provide at least the notion of leverage and relief to the peasantry and their qualms.
Five Races of Many Cultures
Lu Rongting himself was of the Zhuang ethnic minority; with Guangxi and Guangdong both notably retaining significant minority populations of all stripes and colours. Lu Yuguang himself is Vietnamese, and Ma Ji is Hui. It is in the very foundations of the Old Guangxi Clique that cultural traditions and identities of its minority peoples be respected, and as such state policy should reflect significant care and consideration granted towards these minorities.
Blending Confucianism and Progress
Most would deem Confucianism to be a restrictive force, restraining progress and modernity within the Chinese nation. But Confucianism can be modernised, it can be adapted, it can forever serve as a binding force within the common Chinese polity, as long as it is modified for the times. Neo-Confucianism has provided itself with a new, refreshed interpretation of Confucian Ideals, one inherently intermixed with allures of progressivism.
Nine Charitable Halls
The Nine Charitable Halls, otherwise known as Jiushangtan, are a lasting remnant of the late Qing's non-government charitable institutions, with the Nine Charitable Halls themselves having been the largest pre-Republican organisation within Guangzhou. Whilst their influence was briefly diminished in the mid 1920s, they have seen a resurgence in the Beiyang world order, and it is crucial that their resources continue to be tapped for leverage and stability.
Salutations to the Kingmakers
It is the Zhili that have entrusted the various Liangguang factions with their local polities, and it is the Zhili that will ensure the continued success and stability of not only Liangguang, but the whole of China. And so it is with great grace and servitude that Shen Hongying send his finest regards to his benefactors in the North; perhaps they'd even lend a division, or maybe some guns?
Liangguang's Destiny
It is the natural state of Liangguang to observe a leading role in Chinese unification; it was the seat of many rival governments, and is practically a de-facto capital of the Southwest. If the nation is to be united, then it must be decided by those whom control Canton, and thus it is the Old Guangxi Clique, and the Association of All Classes to Save Guangdong, that will persevere in the new Chinese national order.
A New Federalist Conference
At the height of the Federalist Movement in the early 1920s, the leading Federalist intellectuals, warlords, and other leaders gathered together in various cities to debate the merits of provincial autonomy, constitutionalism, and national reunification. Though unsuccessful at the time, we can spark renewed discussion by hosting a new conference in Guangzhou.
Avenge the Northern Expedition
Though warlordism and regionalism remains a persistent issue, the real divide in the nation has been North-South. Dr. Sun recognised this fact from the beginning, calling in vain for a Northern Expedition to bring down the corrupt Beiyang Republic for good. Years of betrayal, failed negotiations, infighting, poor military leadership, and foreign intervention have delayed Dr. Sun's dream from coming true. But we are not deterred, and together we will find our destiny in Beijing!
March on Manchuria
Manchuria has changed considerably since the Manchu conquest. It has gone from a wild frontier to an integral part of the China, but unfortunately foreign predators have fought among themselves for control over the region, it's railways, and its resources. They have found no shortage of collaborators to aid them in their conquest. No more - we know Dongbei belongs to the Chinese, and we will fight any who dare to stop us!
Seize the Guofu's Capital
The League of Eight Provinces was established by Sun Chuanfang in his mad quest for power, an instrument of unfathomable oppression and untold avarice by foreign imperialists and domestic compradors. When the house of cards inevitably came crashing down, it created a significant power-vacuum in the East Coast. It is up to us now to liberate the people of the League, including the city of Nanjing where Dr. Sun first assumed the post of President of the Republic!

Return of the True Chinese Patriots

The Eye of the Storm

So it was no surprise that the French and their lackeys sought to divide us, and even when the right was purged they continued to divide the left. We must play this game, influencing the central committee to ensure the best outcome for ourselves.
Clear Out Fourth Army Remnants
The Fourth Army has largely been dismantled since Chen Mingshu's momentum collapsed from under him. This process will take time, not going too fast avoid the wrath of the central committee, but eventually it will consolidate Chen Jitang's control over the region, a necessary step for his future agenda.

Preparing for a Change
Change is coming to China. Since the first revolutionary took up arms in 1911, an end to the old order was inevitable. Rally the Intelligentsia

Escalate Rent-Reduction Campaigns
As part of the commitment to the social revolution, the initial nationalist leadership had began to reduce the power of the gentry and to draw more power to the masses. Re-establish the PMTI
The Peasant Movement Training Institute or PMTI, was established as one of the outcomes of the first United Front between the Kuomintang and the League of Chinese Syndicalists. The idea of the institute was to invite hopeful revolutionary leaders to help come and educate the rural masses and to prepare them for the national revolution. Let us seek to re-establish this institute in order to increase our party's support with the masses.
The Third National Labour Congress
The Second National Labour Congress was held in Guangdong in 1925 and helped organise the HK-Canton Strike and furthermore trade union activity had been actively persecuted under the previous regime. With the return of leftist leadership in revolutionary guangdong, calls have come from syndicalists and other communists to demand a Third All National Labour Congress to dictate the true worker's revolution in the cities.
Follow the Haifeng Commune Model
It is a fundamental truth that the revolution described by revolutionaries such as the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen, is a revolution that must be fought for and led by the vanguard of the Chinese peasantry. Let us follow Comrade Peng Pai's example in the Haifeng Commune, to establish similar like-minded peasant-led associations and communes across Liangguang in order to prepare the country for the social and national revolution.
Bolster the Nanjing Government

As the nation still remains disunited, it is up to us as well to help bolster their ranks and strengthen the revolutionary cause to ensure it does not fail again.
Sound Heart! Sound Mind! Sound Body!
Inspired by America's own Y.M.C.A, the national and social revolution aims to rectify the sicknesses and ailments that plague the Chinese people. The new government in Liangguang has issued efforts to curb social excesses such as smoking opium, but also promoting physical activities such as rigorous environmental sanitation, jumping, basketball, and tennis in order to improve the overall strength of Liangguang revolutionaries.
Living Newspapers

Reorganise the New Fourth Army

The Pupils of Ma the Big Beard

Form Southeast Political Council

Fostering a Chinese Middle Class

Guangdong in particular is blessed, as well as Guangxi, in regards to hosting strong industrial bases; let us use these strengths to develop the economy further.
A Piece in Chinese Unification
Most auspicously, Guangxi and Guangdong are merely pieces on the chessboard of Chinese unification. It would be entirely out of place to claim anything more than that, at least for the moment. It is the Five Races Under One Union that promulgated a new era of Chinese prosperity, and neither the Well-Field, White Sun, or Rising Sun can dim its bright future. Establishing Our Own Domain

Light the Torch of the Future

Embrace Autarky
