Cementing Dangguo
With our foothold secured, and our government willing, we can finally work towards securing Dangguo, or the Party-State, and with it, ensuring that the National Revolution as set out by Dr. Sun Yat-sen is followed to the utmost, and in its most orthodox interpretation. Cementing the Party-State and Tutelage will ensure the safeguarding of not just the people, but our democracy.
Fostering National Consciousness
Whilst we may control vast swathes of territory, many citizens within our territory are not politically conscious nor active enough to participate in the National Revolution. To this end, we must develop and foster a budding national consciousness, for the Kuomintang must guide the people to the ultimate display of their participation in government: democracy.
Harness Youthful Vigour
The Chinese youth are radical, and primed for action. Enduring years of exploitation by geriatric bureaucrats, cruel warlords and evil gentry alike, who are we to further quench youthful vigour? The Kuomintang will work to harness their spirit, for they are the future generations upon which the National Revolution is made for!
The Revolutionary Woman
Whilst we have made great strides in broader economic, social and political equalisation, we cannot let our female comrades fall to the wayside in the march through the National Revolution. Let the party cooperate with various feminist movements, to further their global struggle for pure gender equalisation. The Kuomintang must bring liberation for all, no matter the gender.
Quell Reactionary Dissent
Ultimately our control of the Nation is not as resolute and concrete as the party would like it to be. With local warlords, bandits and dissidents roaming our land, we must work swiftly to exorcise such blights upon our rule. With the establishment of the Public Security Bureau, we can ensure Party-State control, bowing to nobody but the people's will.
The Dawn of a New Era
By seeing to it that the Northern Expedition has been avenged, we have finally seen Dr. Sun and Chiang Kai-shek's final endeavour to its conclusion. Under his most principles and orthodox disciple, and with assistance from the whole shield of the Kuomintang, and the people, we have secured the National Revolution for decades to come. A New Era has dawned for the Chinese people!
Establish a Provisional Legislature
Following our re-establishment in Beijing and Nanjing, it is finally necessary to establish a governmental organ capable of handling all of the disparate provinces under our rule. With such an act, we can ensure the people of China in our truthful goodwill, as we are not just a new warlord, but something truly greater.
Expand the Civil Service
With Kuomintang control at its all time zenith, our bureaucracy and civil service is proving exceptionally lacking to sufficiently meet the demands of the government and state. Ultimately, by necessicity we must allocate resources to the expansion of our civil service's capacity, to ensure fair, equitable and efficient governance of the new provinces.
Complete the Revolutionary Mission
With the unification of the nation finally complete, finally we have seen the end of the grand revolutionary mission passed down to us by Dr. Sun. With the soul of Xinhai finally being put to rest, we have seen to it that a true revolution has emerged from the embers of 1911. The Trumpets of the Third National Congress await, and who else to promulgate it than the exceptional Hu Hanmin?
Fallout of the Baise Uprising
It has finally come. In a brilliant and swift move, the workers and peasants have unified in a revolutionary vanguard and have driven out the reactionary warlord Li Zongren and his counter-revolutionary New Guangxi Clique from Liangguang once and for all. In the chaos and ensuring political struggle however, a new contender has emerged in Liangguang...one strong enough to challenge perhaps Nanjing's legitimacy.
In the Dark of the Night
A true, pure revolution requires strength and discipline in order to ensure the success of the divine mission bestowed upon us. It is impertinent that in this time of great civil strife, we invest our resources into \
The Allure of Totalism
There are some more radical members of the national revolution within our ranks who profess to follow the extreme form of socialism, demanding that we turn the revolution's course to one akin's to Mussolini or even Savinkov's National Populism. While their voices may be a minority, few can deny that if the revolution is to be secured, foolish dreams like democracy and liberalism must wait until liberation is here.
Expand the National Sun Yat-sen University
The National Sun Yat-sen University had been named in honour of the beloved eternal premier of the Chinese Kuomintang, and it continues to hold its position as the pinnacle of academic excellence in Guangdong. In order to foster greater national consciousness amongst the intellectuals and students, we should seek to expand the university's curriculum to include studies on Marxism and socialism.
Assert Authority over Guangxi
At long last, we have driven the reactionary warlord Li Zongren and his despicable New Guangxi Clique cronies far from the cradle of revolution. It was only a matter of time before our forces were to triumph over the reactionary faction in Liangguang. Nonetheless, we should prepare efforts to pacify and stabilise the province of Guangxi, in order to earn the trust and support of the rural masses in the region.
Initiate Pioneer Reforms
In accordance with the goals of Sun Yat-sen's theories on reaching democracy, we must take the first steps towards organising democracy within the masses. Let us encourage not only unions but agricultural cooperatives and farmers' associations to practice local democracy, to include both men and women, and to organise representative councils that would allow the masses to have their voices heard on behalf of their unions and cooperatives.
Launch the Liangguang CICs
Launched by the National Revolutionary Government in the former League of Eight Provinces, the Chinese Industrial Cooperative Programme aims to create industrial cooperatives for labourers and workers to seek employment and to also aid in national defence and reconstruction. Emboldened by the successes of the Nanjing programmes, our government has sought to create CICs within Liangguang in order to strengthen our economy.
Our Revolutionary Sisters
Women do indeed hold up half the sky. As the National Revolution aims to free all Chinese from the chains of imperialism, it is highly critical that we address the situation of our sisters and mothers, who also desire liberation from not just imperialism and capitalism, but also the chains of the patriarchy. We must seek to abolish decadent practices such as foot-binding and child-marriages, in order to secure women's true liberation.
Consolidate the Unions
Most unions within China's industrial and coastal cities fall under the League of Chinese Syndicalists, and the relationship between the Kuomintang and the LCS is one that is strained yet mutually beneficial as the Party does seek to mobilise the urban proletariat to work alongside it for the sake of national revolution. We must seek to reorganise the unions under our leadership in order to strengthen party unity and discipline.
Sway Hawaii's Ambivalence
The Crown Prince and his so-called Reconstruction Faction seek no future of a socialist China but nonetheless, we certainly respect their commitment to the pursuit of constitutionalism and democracy as illustrated by the late eternal premier. As the Nanjing Government continues to splinter over its various factions, perhaps it may be wise to see if the Reconstruction members are willing to work with us.
Reaffirm the United Front
The united front between the Chinese Kuomintang and the League of Chinese Syndicalists organised in 1924, was orchestrated in order to secure the support of the Third Internationale and to rally the revolutionary masses against the corrupt imperialistic Zhili government. With the situation in China still just as precarious, we must seek to work together with our fellow comrades in order to fight for a free China once more.
Establish the RCA Guangzhou Branch
As the factions in Nanjing bicker over their differences, perhaps we may find sense in reaching out towards Chen Gongbo and his Reorganisation Comrades Association. Long associated with Guangdong politics, Chen and his RCA cronies possess a considerable degree of support within the workers and students, and we may strengthen their cause by opening a branch of RCA cells in Guangzhou.
Connections within the WMARCA
The true revolution belongs to the people, and the people look to no one further than the charismatic General Deng Yanda. Long familiar with the politics of Guangdong military men, Deng's influence within Liangguang is pervasive and many officers within the NRA are loyal to his WMARCA. As many of our brothers have long fought and shed blood with General Deng, we should seek to utilise these connections to develop our own influence.
Challenging the Central Committee
The central committee takes and takes from the people but gives so little in return. Not freedom, not food, not protection from the warlords and imperialists. Not even hope. Only an never ending march to tyranny, the same thing we brave revolutionaries stood up against in the first place. We all know where this is heading - it is better we prepare for the likely confrontation now than surrender to fate.
Taking the Reins
One way or another, we have toppled the old Central Executive Committee. No more will the two-faced Wang Jingwei disseminate lies to the Chinese people, no more shall the scheming Song Qingling and imperious Deng Yanda bark treasonous counter-orders. Now, in wake of the old Kuomintang's demise, we must rise to the occasion and free the people from their slavery. Only under our fair rule can we assure the proper application of revolutionary principles.
The Kuomintang Civil War
At last, the time has come for the true national and social revolution. The degenerative party elements in Nanjing have fallen to the interests of counter-revolutionary, bourgeoisie, warlords, and traitorous imperialists. With the fate of the late Dr. Sun's revolution in jeopardy, it is time for us to rise up and fight - to rally the people of China for a true new China.
Rally the Red Guards
The Red Guards of Guangzhou were established by the Chinese Syndicalist Party's Central Committee to come to defence of the workers and sailors of Guangzhou in order to combat rightist counter-revolutionary activities especially from the Merchant Corps. With the civil war against Nanjing now in full swing, we must mobilise these detachments to prepare for the defences of the city of Guangzhou.
Meritocracy on the Battlefield
Liangguang's Revolutionary Army prides itself not on elitist discrimination or corrupt incompetence, but the finest revolutionary officers in all of China - men and women who are willing to make as many sacrifices as is needed, in order to save China from destruction. As we are greatly outnumbered in this conflict, we will increase the number of front-line officers through series of rapid promotions.
Mobilise Guerrilla Detachments
While we are largely outnumbered by the numerically superior Nanjing NRA, there are still ways that a people can fight. It only takes a rifle to rally the people to the war of national liberation. We should rally guerrillas from the peasant associations, who are long accustomed to guerrilla tactics, in order to join us in China's great proletarian revolution.
Encirclement and Annihilation
Against a greater military force, we must seek to take the initiative and use the speed and terrain to our advantage. Due to our exceptional knowledge of terrain and geography, we are able to find enemy weaknesses in their frontline. We will focus our doctrine on encircling the enemy, then destroying these pockets with speed and brute force - allowing us to capture enemy prisoners and equipment en masse.
The Peoples' War
The War of National Liberation calls for not just the soldiers of the National Revolutionary Army but also the women and all who are able-bodied to fight for China's freedom against capitalism and imperialism. Whether it be outright partisan efforts such as sabotages and ambushes, or subversive activities to uncover enemy intelligence, let all who seek true freedom join our righteous cause against Nanjing.
Keep the Red Flag Flying!
Since the beginning, the odds of the war had been stacked against us simply due to the numeric size and economic strength of the Central Government. Nonetheless, it is by the will of the people that revolutions are won and it is clear that Nanjing can no longer represent the National and Social Revolution. If we should fail in our efforts, the dreams of socialism in China shall never be truly realised.
The National Unity Cabinet
In order to navigate the difficult road ahead, the great parties of our young Republic have formed a national unity government, banding together once again in defence of our federalist future. Though cabinet members are ostensibly chosen purely by merit, in practice it is dominated by the GRA and CDL. Nevertheless, it is a step forward - but they have many ways to go before they can truly save their nation.
A Five Year Plan for China
Upon the election of the first parliament of a united China, the DSP insist that they come together to draft and implement a Five Year Plan which is to be immutable regardless of any changes in government. United, efficient, and stable, this political system seeks to balance the need for free debate with decisive action. Once the plan is promulgated, there will be no turning back.
Promoting an Intellectual Revival
In order for China to truly return to its traditional place as the Great Power in the Orient and in order for China to achieve its democratic future, Zhang Junmai and the CDL believe there must be an cultural revival spearheaded by Chinese intellectuals. It must incorporate Western technology and political theory without abandoning the essence of Chinese culture.
Cementing President Zhang's Grip
Zhang Junmai has many opponents - in the Republic, in the CDL, and in the DSP. There always seems to be infighting, whether it be over ideology or patronage positions or just plain personal grievances. With Presidential power however, Zhang can finally establish himself as the paramount leader of the CDL, sidelining opponents and implementing his vision for the republic!
Bringing Social Democracy to China
Educated in Germany, Zhang Junmai's experiences learning under SPD intellectuals profoundly influenced Zhang's political thinking. He and many others in the DSP are at the forefront of importing European reformist and libertarian socialist thinking to China, albeit with a Chinese spin. Once fringe outside of intellectual circles, now that Zhang is in power many are now willing to give it a second look.
Nationalising Socialism
The DSP believe that nationalism and race are the most important principle in society. The French were able to survive on their own despite the lack of a world revolution for years because of their ability to nationalise their socialism, and similarly the various socialist states of the world endure as nation-states rather than embracing excessive internationalism. The Chinese way to socialism will similarly be in harmony with Chinese nationalism.
A Utopian Vision for China

Reconnecting with the Diaspora
Amid the instability of the warlord era and fears that China's higher educational institutions were inadequate for the modern world, many wealthier students went abroad to study- often never to return. Other families left home generations prior in better times, building their fortunes in nations abroad while retaining their ancestral ties. Whatever the case, their skills and money are needed at home now as we rebuild!
Bringing China into the Modern Age
Chinese culture has always prized education, but the endless needs of the military over the past few decades has sapped much of our funds for schooling - and with it our children's future. If we do not want our boys and girls to have nothing to look forward to but military service and poverty, then we need to fight to lift China out of its decay!
Promoting a Chinese Renewal
Modernising China does not simply end by building new roads or improving our schools - for China to be modern it must feel modern. Chen Jiongming has always had an eye for \
A Strong Hand in Uneasy Times
The Federal Republic was built under Chen Jiongming's strong leadership in Guangdong, and now that it stretches all the way from Guangzhou to Beijing the government continues to revolve around the Federalist President. Chen will arbitrate disputes between the grand coalition in legislature, and his men will ensure the continued good governance of the executive.
Constitutionalist Promises
The bedrock for any future Democracy in China is the promulgation of a Constitution and the universal respect of it afterwards. Petty things like campaigning and voting can wait until the nation is saved and a constitution is drafted. Until then, respect for rule of law is paramount, from peasant to President.
Protecting Regional Autonomy
Regional Autonomy is the raison d'etre of the Federalist Movement, and protecting it is an essential function of the Federal government. A certain balance needs to be struck between the Yue Army (which has done so much to aid in the reconstruction of provincial governments) and these fledging assemblies. Properly managing this relationship is what will stabilise our rule.
Revising Democracy
Zhang Junmai once said \
Continuing Federalist Reforms
As our movement expands its reach northwards, it is imperative that we continue to implement the various local government reforms that we promised in Guangzhou. Reforming local judiciaries, appointing new magistrates, and empowering local assemblies are essential to winning over the support of the regional gentry, intellectuals, and other powerholders we need to stabilise our government.
Modernising the Federal Police
Governing a vast modern nation-state requires modern police tactics and inter-provincial coordination in order to crack down on cross-border felonies such as banditry, insurgency, or organised crime. Hiring experts from abroad, particularly veterans from the relatively new American FBI, will go a long way in showing our commitment to a modern, professional police force.
Promoting Higher Education
The Federalist movement has always acknowledged the importance of educating the people and the youth of the future - after all democracy cannot function if its population is illiterate. In December of 1920, Governor Chen Jiongming had invited Chen Duxiu of the CSP to promote educational reforms and to encourage salons of thought, provocative ideas, and philosophical rejuvunation.
Enshrining Parliamentarianism
The key to a functioning democracy is a parliament that is run by the people and led by the people. This is where the former Beiyang Government failed in their destruction of trust for popular soverignty. We will create a republican unicameral legislature with members representing the agricultural, industrial, commercial, and educational sectors of society - thus bringing together a true democracy run by the people.
The National Mobilisation
Let the nation come together and the spirit of democracy to guide the organs of society into a true national being. In the aftermath of the great civil war, we should unite organisations to prevent price controls and hoarding and to aid private businesses in stimulating production and capital.
Aid to the Recovered Areas
Portions of the national countryside lay in devastation following the conclusion of our victory against the North. In order to revive these areas and to build public support and trust, the new Central Government shall direct aid in currency and resettlement to those displaced by war.
Safeguarding the Peasants
The new Federal state shall safegaurd the peasants' right to land, utilisation, and enjoyment of private property. However, property shall be limited in order to combat land competition and to take the preliminary measures towards nationlisation. By working with the peasantry we shall earn their trust and faith lest they turn to more radical ideas.
Protecting Private Property
Implied and inherent in every covenant is the right for every man to own his property. To appease conservatives who fear we may be submitting to the will of the peasantry, a Recovered Area People's Property Registration Commission (RAPPRC) will be set up to protect original owners of land and to arbirtrate disputes to ensure due process and protection of property rights.
Nationalising Vital Resources
The Chinese Democratic League has urged and emphasised that the natural resources and bountiful treasures of the land should be used in for the benefit of the general public. No longer shall we tolerate greedy landlords or warlords hoarding these resoruces rather the government should nationalise them for the enrichment of the Chinese nation.
Mixed Industrial Planning
China must catch up with the rest of the world. The past few decades of republican failure and warlordism have contributed to the sorry state of our national economy even if we do have the potential for a large industrial base. Production should be increased under adequate planning for both private and national productive enterprises. In both the public and private industry, workers should have the right to participate in or be consulted in management.
Progressive Tax Reforms
There should be a thorough-going revision of the taxation system. Lenient taxes on wealthy gentry and landowners have contributed to corruption while higher taxes discourage members in the economy to spend and thus contribute to economic growth. As part of the new federal national reforms, we shall initiate a progressive system of taxation which will provide for inheritance, income, and excess profits taxes.
The Equalisation of Wealth
It is the very goal of the Chinese Democratic League to enshrine equality and to end the gaps that have driven inequality throughout centuries of feudal order. It will not be through the dictatorship of the proletariat that we achieve this but rather economic democracy ensure adequate livelihood economic security as well as equalisation of wealth and the end to inequality.
Building a National Defence Industry
The war may have been won against the North and Beijing secured in true Republican hands but China's enemies are far from defeated. Across the world and within our domestic borders, imperialist nations and reactionary forces pose an ever present threat to our democratic vision. Under the leadership of the new Federal government, we shall repossess former arsenals into federal military control.
Postwar Economic Reconversion
With the end of war in the country, the time has come for us to address the Chinese economy. For too long, industry has been directed towards the procurement of small arms and artillery. With conflict subsided, the time has come for the Chinese economy to revive with drastic regulations and nationalisation efforts directed towards pivoting wartime industry back towards civilian purposes.
Unity on Our Terms
The nation has been united, somewhat, at least under the terms dictated by those men of words and guns with the right vision for the future of China. A strong nation, a wealthy and prosperous one, that is the goal of all the men whom wave the Five Races Under One Union, and whilst China lurches under its own weight temporarily, the people can rest assured that the nation will never again suffer injustice or a fate of inglorious servitude.
Following Through With Philanthropy
Serving as financial director of the Guangdong Food Relief Association and of the Guangdong Charity Relief Association, Chen Lianzhong has been nothing of a stellar gentleman in terms of philanthropy. Dedicating large amounts of his own personal wealth with abounding enthusiasm to public welfare and municipal finances, Lianzhong has set a model to be emulated. Lauding his achievements, and rewarding his service, we shall surely see more merchants like him.
Reopen the Guangdong Mint
The Guangdong Mint was once the earliest factory in China to use machines to cast silver and copper coins. Buitl in 1887 and proposed by Zhang Zhidong, it was a sign of true success of the Qing's Self-Strengthening movement. Surviving the Xinhai Revolution, it would become the Republic of China Guangdong Minting factory, but alas, due to lack of funding it would end up close in 1931. By reopening the mint, the government can secure some level of financial security.
Modernising the Nation Through Rail
Railways are a tried and true example of the successes of an industrial revolution, and for its merit China's interior remains relatively untapped. Railways largely dominate the central and coastal areas of the nation, and even they are decade old behemoths that have been ill-maintained, or otherwise damaged through fighting and warfare. Ling Hongxun, a local railway mogul, has signalled his intention to connect the nation's cities together, and we must only fund him.
Exporting the National Guangxi Model
Popularised in the National Guangxi University, created by Ma Junwu and Pan Zhuqi, the teaching of militaristic skills and combat abilities alongside the cultivation of scientific knowledge and works skills has seen a large amount of success, with many of the Guangxi alumni having been imparted with a sense of duty to the nation. Engage in Mass Environmental Projects
Considered a regional Guangdong hero and a famous gourmet, Jiang Kongyin turned from a mere jinshi into a popular community figure through his convincing of the Governor-General of Guangdong and Guangxi to declare against the Qing in 1911. Having retired since then, Jiang has spent much of his life investing in the development of environmental projects. Through a national campaign popularised by his methods, we shall revive China's greenery once more.
Initiating the Agricultural Revolution
Something of a pioneer, Ding Ying has become a relatively famous name within the agricultural research sphere for his revolutionary work in the breeding of various rice strains, some of which have managed to achieve thousands of grains per panicle. Whilst a professor of the Guangdong University, it is imperative that the state both recognise his achievements, and fund their implementation nationwide; to spurn forward a new agricultural revolution.
Favouring the Banks
Without the banks, the Chinese Yuan would be more worthless than it already is, and without the banks, it is very likely that none of the officials in the present government would be occupying their positions, let alone be in relative prosperity. Their contracts, favourable loans, and assured deals have managed to keep provincial governments afloat in times of desperate need, and it is time that they receive their due diligence.
Investing in the Revival of Industry
The nation has been brutally bloodied and battered after decades of nigh perennial strife, and yet its richest officials remain aloof, sitting upon piles of finances of which see no beneficial use to the state that provided for them. Through a mass media campaign, ushering in the masses as a chess piece, the wealthy and well-off must be forced into conjuring their cash for various state investment projects; it's only right.
Elevating the Merchants of China
Merchants are the very financial lifeblood by which Chinese trade and commerce remains afloat, and it is crucial that they retain their cut of the pie. Perhaps the institution of a plutocracy is considerably extreme, but nonetheless they must have a valued say. Combined with the businessmen, bankers, and Chambers of Commerce, China will undergo a financial revolution of its own in the near future; worthy enough to rival Japan, or even that of Europe.
Establishing a Nascent Petroleum Industry
Ling Hongxun, whilst similarly in-charge of vast amounts of China's railways, has begun to invest in a nascent petroleum market within the nation. Whilst the largest deposits of extracted Chinese oil remain largely within the Northwest Frontier, synthetic reproductions of oil, and of rubber, have proven remarkably successful within Europe. Ling has begun to discuss acquisition of refinery plants himself, and nationalising his deals surely cannot hurt.
Freedom of Thought and Inclusiveness

Continuing the Crusade
Such a shame that the successive governments of the North could not restore order to the nation. Despite corralling perhaps their biggest adversary of the Warlord Era, Guangzhou, they still continued to persist in infringing upon autonomy, disrepecting regional prerogatives, and in a general whirlwind of self-opposition. It is time to finalise what Cai E started, and do what he could not: March on Beijing.
Re-Establish the Military Affairs Council
The Military Affairs Council of the Republic of China was a brief institution founded on the fading lights of the National Protection War as an effort to politicise the Jingguojun's crusade against Yuan Shikai, and force a Republican settlement. Joined by the Warlords of the Southwest, the Progressive Party, and parts of the Political Science CLique, it was a noble institution that was pre-maturely dissolved, and we must remedy this.
Protecting the Nation from Itself
Revolutionaries and bandits have run amok and thrived in the collapsing stability of the Zhili World order, and it has become such an issue that the very hoisting of the White Sun on a Blue Sky has become rapidly apparent; this evidently cannot be a state of affairs to abide by. The people seem intent on cannibalising their own prosperity for the words of demagogues, and it must be the Public Safety Bureau that reminds the people of the right path of a citizen.
Solicit Support from Germany
The fading of the Sino-German Military Mission in much of the North Zhili's territories has been nothing short of a tragedy. For it is with the German Intervention into Guangzhou that the hammmer struck upon the National Revolutionary Army in 1927, and it is for that of which the Zhili owe much. Sun Chuanfang was many things, but few can say that his pragmatic arrangements with Germany had sullied his potential; Jinbao has seen the benefit, and so do we.
Opening the Universities
Ever since the Warlord Era engulfed the nation in nigh perpetuity, educators and professors have found themselves scattered in unstable jobs that rely open the good will of their local warlord, or the stability of the government at the time. Drifting towards Beijing University, the wrong political opinion could see you shuttled to Kunming or Nanning, as so many have witnessed since the 1932 Uprising. It is time to turn over a new leaf, and open the universities once more.
Embracing Constitutionalism
Constitutionalism is the guiding light by which good governance by good people can be achieved, maintained, or even expected. And it is the moral dignity of every good official to pry themselves out from the mindset of a warlord, or a merchant, and realise that only by legality and constitutional rule can orderly implementation of national policy be swift and efficient. Organic Law, or Military Government, is but a pretence for blatant dictatorship after all.
Ascension of the Young Marshal
Trained and cultivated as his de-facto successor since the 1920s, Lu Yuguang has long been the gem of Lu Rongting's political legacy. Inheriting his father's position of Viceroy of Liangguang, he has managed to both circumvent the revolutionaries and warlords that saw Rongting's attempted consolidation in the 1920s end unanswered. In the true image of his father, he has become something of a popular folk hero within Guangxi.
A New Baojia
The Baojia was a noble system that, like so many throughout the nation, entered into disrepute as various officials abused the militia to collect extra-ordinary \
Reconcile with Beiyang
For some time it has appeared that the Young Guangxi Faction has drifted away from its roots in the Beiyang National Order, intent on retaining its regionalist control and contesting passive influence within the Southwest. With the Young Marshal of the South's new stature however, it is undoubtedly necessary to once again light up the old communication networks into Northerner circles, and remind them that we have always been compatriots.
Cooperate with Southern Intelligentsia
Whether the Old Guangxi Clique likes it or not, Liangguang and the Southwest as a whole has become something of a hotbed for political dissidents and various gatherings of intelligentsia. Revolutionaries, socialists, democrats, federalists, all of them flock to Guangzhou, or Kunming, or Changsha, or Chongqing. And it would be wise, prudent, and ultimately meritable to cooperate with these men of words; to build a modernised nation-state.
A Legacy of Heroism and Chivalry
There is no stronger call to arms than that of glory, or that of innate heroic duty for the nation, or the community. Constituting a militaristic state-people, it is only through sheer courage, bravery, and devotion to the nation's struggle that its gallant soldiers can carry on. And it is to this legacy that the government must extol; resistance to authoritarianism, and to autocracy, and unto which a sense of duty can be instilled within the masses.
The Merchant Government
In an ever flowerly coup de grâce, well-renowned and nationally prominent merchant-mayor Chen Lianbo has managed to secure leadership of the informal Liangguang Cliques, binding them to his Association of All Classes to Save Guangdong, and its numerous key financial assets within the nation. Prosperity is what holds the minutiae of today, and democracy is the goal of the future. Under Governor Chen, a new Cantonese-British style of government shall flourish.

Solicit the Third Party Vote
Many within the nation see the Merchant Government as nothing more but a vile assuaging of democratic norms in place of a relentlessly capitalistic and commerce dominated government, but that is not the whole picture. As merchants it is natural that the government value its assets, however, individuals like Zhang Jia'ao of the DSP, are close to the Merchants, and we can prove similarly that we are democrats as well as financiers.
\
The Merchants have long stood as a pillar of Chinese community, and of the nation's commerce. There have been thousands of years of kinships built between them, and yet only years of government. Governments may come, governments may leave, one thing is for certain, commerce remains. And it is this commerce that binds every merchant in China, and it is for them that Chen Lianbo welcomes into a broader national plutocracy.
Filling the Void in the Nation's Guanxi
With the institution of a Merchant government, something truly only dreamed of in the heyday of the Merchant Corps Uprising, the nation's delicate balance of handshakes and arrangements has nigh been upended. Warlords now answer to the merchants in suits, not to politicians or themselves. As such, a grand whole has been left in the various patronage networks all throughout China, and it is necessary to reconstitute a new working arrangement.

Clearing House and Paying Debts
Shen knows too well that one cannot rule unfairly, or without close allies. So many have come and gone in Shen's assortment of allies, that he himself may have indirectly caused, that it has become a surprising issue for his governance. Even so, the Zhili have continuously courted and sometimes properly backed him in his endeavours, and so it would be prudent to solicit their commitments once again, or otherwise descend upon Political Science for aide.
Reconstituting the Confucian Order
The nation has seen an influx of new thinking ever since the November Fourth Movement of 1919, but one of its greatest travesties was the insistent disregard for the Confucian World Order, replaced by that of New Life. And yet, it has only resulted in the wrong sort of thinking, or depravity, the spouting of nonsense and the institution of a disharmonious national mindset. It is imperative that order is restored to China, bound together by our mutual beliefs.
The Government's Handsome Face
Despite all pretence, it is evidently clear that Shen is ailing, and in an unflattering fashion. But there is one ambitious, and at least somewhat pliable, local intellectual who has a sizable provincial following. The Qi has long served as an example and inspiration for the New Guangxi Clique, who now seek to replicate its extensive reforms.

Promote Rapid Industrialisation
While now under a socialist government, China still suffers from a poor industrial base and a population that is still heavily reliant on the plow and the soil. In order for China to rapidly catch up with the West, it is impertinent that extensive resources and efforts are devoted towards promoting hard labour and rapid industrial growth as we transform our country towards a true socialist nation.
Towards True Socialist Education
Children and students must attend schools to learn not only of the heroic deeds committed by the martyrs during the War of Resistance and the War of Liberation but they must also pay heed to revolutionary orators and heroes such as Karl Marx, Vladimir Lenin, Tom Mann, and Jean Zyromoski. By devoting efforts towards educating the masses and the youth, we prepare the next generation of socialists to continue carrying on the revolution.
The South Triumphant
Seizing upon its natural prerogatives, the South has finally managed to topple the North for contention and control over the Chinese nation-state. Now, a broken and shattered nation lies before the Guangdong and Guangxi warlords, one they have been entrusted with to repair and restore as they see fit. Hardly advocating revolution, it is evidently clear that the Auspicious Cloud is here to shine forever more.
Enshrine Regional Autonomy
Our war was never that of imposition, or that of enforcing the dictatorship of Guangzhou unto the whole nation. It was a democratic war, a war for the rights and autonomies of all the provinces. The Provincial Self-Governance movement at heart is a valuable and noble one, dedicated to ensuring the freedoms of each Province's rightful rulers. We must but merely elevate it to national policy.
Taking the Brave Step Forward
With the avenues of governance in hand, the time has arrived to certify and arrange the outlook of the national government. Many before us have made attempts to unite the nation by constitutionalism and legality, and alas the constitutions produced in such a period were rubber stamps for autocrats or regimes. It must be such that the constitution is a fair and free one.
Demonstrate the Power of Banking
There is no greater source of power in national politics than that of finance; as is often claimed, money makes the world go round. The only shield against the right amount of investment is that of stubbornness, or morality. But in a Gentleman's Republic ruled by suits and sabres, the banks are but a cornerstone of the republican foundation, and it is time they exercise full power.
On the Military and Its Excesses
Whilst the Yue Jun, Gui Jun, and all other Provincial armies fought, bled, and died for our victories, it has become rapidly evident that military occupation zones, and other forms of temporary military rule in parts of the nation has resulted in insubordination at best, rebellion at worst. Oversized, unloyal, and uncentralised, it is time that warlordism be brought to heel.
Student Self-Sufficiency
As advocated by Ma Junwu, the students must pick up hoes, and participate in the construction of their institutions of education. Not only shall their cooperative work facilitate the development of their work capacity and enduracne, but it shall enable students of poor families to receive compensation through their labour to supplement student living, and prepare them for the workforce.
Constructing a Single Economic Organ
The Chinese economy has been compared to that of a fallible playground for foreign venture capitalists, able to flaunt labour laws, fair wages, and all other infractions due to the nation's weak political state, and economic strength. However, by controlling key enterprises directly through nationalisation, the nation's independence will be won swiftly.
Privileges to the Merchant Classes
Merchants are the very core of the Chinese economy, walking hand-in-hand with businessmen, they signal a form of native, middle-class capitalism that is a sign of a burgeoning mass industrialisation. By granting privileges to existing merchants and future entrepreneurs, the Chinese state shall develop whilst being a cornucopia of economic advancement.
Apotheosis of Chinese Capital
Never before has China's native capitalistic business classes been so intertwined with statecraft and development; the Cohong held the nation's exports in the palm of their hands for but a brief period, ultimately overturned by the state. As dreamed by individuals such as Chen Lianbo, the state should be that of one that prioritises finance and the economy.
The Wealth of New Culture
Only fools would hold on so feverishly to the dominion of past tradition and culture. Of course, one cannot dispose of China's millennia old history, but one can advance and modernise it for the times. Synthesising Western sciences, culture, and advancements with Eastern traditions, China will be the hallmark of a new cultural rival in East Asia.
A Young Face for an Ancient Civilisation
In an ode to his adopted birthright, Lu Yuguang has reached the highest office of the nation at an age that is entirely outstanding of his contemporaries. Finishing what his father started, Lu has become a Marshal for a New Generation of Chinese.
Triumph of the Crisp Handshake
Securing victory over the militarists, the Guangdong and Guangxi Civilians of the Merchant Corps and Political Science have emerged to be the brokers of a new Beiyang Republic. Shirking the rifle for the pen and paper, all eyes are on the Merchants and Politicians to see who will overcome the other, instituting their own form of Western-inspired governance by the ballot.
Beiyang of the South
Whilst not a true son of the North, [ROOT.GetLeader]'s Army and its associated contemporaries have reigned in Liangguang and led the march of unification. Without a clear ideological outlook, at least in regards to [ROOT.GetLeader]'s acolytes, the nation looks upon the new Marshals and Ministers without fear or exclamation; ultimately, it is more of the same.
Maintaining the Delicate Balance
Governance is a delicate game, lean too hard on one side and the whole scale will topple. In order to prioritise all meritable governance, it is important to remain open-minded and pragmatic. Mass education, economic development, and a strong, centralised military are all points the majority of the Central Government agrees upon, and as such that shall be the policy of the day.
Employ New People, Implement New Policies
In order to rejuvenate the Chinese state, it is necessary to no longer excessively rely upon those of the old generations. For too long, statesmen have ruled in perpetuity, reaching ages close to their 70s and beyond. By refreshing every bureaucrat from the magistrate to the ministries, the nation itself will inevitably be ruled by a new age of fresh, modern politicians.
The Teacher-President
Zhu Jiahua has been nothing short of a rising star. Through political Machiavellianism, expert statesmanship or plain old politicking, he has managed to rise through the ranks of academia and government alike. With prolific contacts amongst groups such as the Jingxing Society, Zhu connects Ex-Presidents, educational innovaters, industrialists, and officers under his watchful eye.
Adopting the Merits of Jinbao
Perhaps the greatest statesman in China of the recent era has to be that of President Cao Kun. Having managed to corral the disparate Zhili factions under one banner, few could compare to his ever auspicious long-term vision for China. Whilst many would decry him to have been a sellout to German interests, only Cao and his Jinbao faction truly understood the price for progress.
Order and Progress
Order and Progress; such a notion shall be the very modus operandi by which the state shall operate. It is only under Order and Progress that the Chinese nation shall economically skyrocket. Guaranteeing safe economic investments, and a free utopia for enterprises, China will be an efficient, centralised, and strong state. Only then shall notions of political reform be viable.
Old Guangxi's Canton Comprador
Perhaps few would have expected that Li Yaohan, Zhao Army leader and independently-minded ally of Shen Hongying, would have become Marshal of the whole Nation. With ties to local Guangdong gentry, and having once been almost cast aside in the fires of the Northern Expedition, Li's tenure is an ode to the early days of the Beiyang Republic; an all encompassing marshal overseeing progress.
Cult of the Young Marshal
Lu Yuguang is the epitome of an enlightened ruler. Implementing the benefits and merits of revolution and reform without the trampling of tradition or the loss of national essence. He has neither sold the nation to compradors or betrayed his own ideals. Even further, the nation would not have been united without its Grand Marshal, and it is so that the Young Marshal is a national hero.
Studying the Zhili System
The Zhili, for all of their faults, carried with them the most recent bout of national stability and economic development within the nation since the Qing Dynasty's collapse. And as such, their system of statescraft and politicking must absolutely be studied, and improved upon; obviously avoiding the excesses of factionalism whilst ensuring the efficiencies of statesmanship.
Protector of Tradition
Akin to Wu Peifu, Lu Yuguang is the strongest example of the courteous Confucian statesman. Auspicious, placing primacy in intellectuals and scholars, whilst exercising dominant restraint in light of sweeping fervour, he and his adopted brother Ma Ji are tokens of stability, concrete pillars of the nation's politics for future generations, and signs of a modern Beiyang.
Primacy of the Military Arm
There is no greater service to the nation than that of servitude in the national military. To defend the state with honour, and to protect its citizens, those are the greatest responsibilities that could ever be bestowed upon China's brave soldiers. No longer shall the army be viewed with fear, or with disgust, instead only admiration shall remain. Hail to our national protectors!
Victory of the Southerners
Ostensibly retaining its routes within the traditionally rebellious and progressive South of the nation, the Old Guangxi Clique has taken on a modern and refreshed outlook within national politics. Straddling the line between Reform, Revolution, and Warlords, the Young Guangxi faction of the clique has brought together various ex-revolutionaries to advance national progress.
The Progressive General
Under Marshal Lu Yuguang, and his close allies Ma Junwu, Ma Ji, Liu Zhilu, and Lin Hu, the Old Guangxi Clique has cast aside the eras of stagnancy under Beiyang, and brought forward revolutionary progress without the tyranny of Dangguo. Walking the middle path, the nation has been set onto the road of stability, and perhaps even democracy, at least in the future.
Bringing Down the Eternal Enemy
For too long, the Chinese community has had to endure fear and turmoil at the prospect of raids from bandit clans, marauding armies, and local misfits. And so it is crucial that the state finally exercise its full might, rejuvenated by recent nigh-total reunification, and finally excise the plight of banditry from China forevermore.
Looking Towards the Whigs
Under the Whigs, Britain experienced untold social and political progress, advancing freedoms and rights never before seen within the British isles. Ruled by a progressive and benevolent oligarchy, they emancipated the people, exhibited strength on the national stage, and championed the supremacy of the legislature. To liberalise China, it is crucial that we emulate their example.
Freedom of Commerce
Only through commerce and trade are the plights of national collapse, revolution, and civil war prevented. And China has long been in dire need of thoughtful, stable, and wise national economic management. And so it must be that the Merchants and the Middle-Class Liberals join together to further healthy economic development, and national stability, without demagoguery.
Raising the Chinese Plutocracy
Many would believe that the rise of the supremacy of China's businessmen and merchants to the avenues of the legislative and executive offices would be the mere substitution of the dictatorship of militarists for that of capital, but they would be fools. It is not dictatorship that the Merchants bring, but economic development, national progress, and Cantonese Liberalism.
An Era of Good Feelings
The time for civil war, bloodshed, and retribution is over. The only goal of government must be the sustenance of its people, the ensurance of their liberties, and a democratic future. The nation's purpose must be that of national reconstruction, and an end to partisanship within politics. Are we not all Chinese? United by common belonging to the nation; Five Races Under One Union?
The Democratic Ideal
One cannot expect the masses to understand their civic rights all at once, when the majority can hardly sustain their households, or are ruled by their local elites. But you cannot rule a state through dictatorship, or divide it unnecessarily through Federalism. A democracy, if imperfect, but a democracy nonetheless. With abounding optimism, the parties must unite in harmony.

Intrigue in Lingnan

In Guangdong, the south remains under the control of §cChen Lianbo and his Merchant Corps§!, centered in the city of Guangzhou (Canton), while north is controlled by §PGeneral Shen Hongying and the Shen Army Faction§!, barely clinging onto power in Shaoguan. To the west in Guangxi, §gMarshal Lu Yuguang and the Young Guangxi junta§! holds onto their province, their hegemony over the twin provinces still intact... for now.

Reaffirm Inter-provincial Hegemony
Under Governor Lu Rongting, the twin provinces of Guangxi and Guangdong were briefly joined together under the rule of the Old Guangxi Clique, which did not last long, however, as Guangxi dominance over Liangguang disintegrated following the devastating Yue-Gui Wars. Although the twin provinces went through years of a tremendous power vacuum after the collapse of the Northern Expedition, Governor Lu Rongting returned to power in Guangxi and, through his pragmatic alliances, managed to secure himself the position of 'Viceroy of Liangguang'. As heirs to his legacy, with the dust having settled across the wartorn provinces, we shall reassert our dominance and remind those who oppose us who the true masters of Liangguang are.
Attract Foreign Support
Our control over the territories we rule is limited, to say the least. With us lacking allies within Liangguang, and those that we do have only doing so out of pragmatic self-preservation, we lack the means to overcome our precarious military and economic situation. Despite the rest of the country being either too busy dealing with their internal struggles, or outright hostile to our cause, we are fortunately still able to obtain foreign support through our contacts. By attracting their favour, our misfortunes shall be reversed, even if it comes at a price.
Harmony with the Business Class
For centuries, the merchant and business class have been the backbone to China's prosperity, accumulating wealth and building local economies through trade. Should our relations with them remain harmonious and cooperative, the prosperity and wealth brought on by these merchants would be of great use to us, assisting in our construction of Liangguang. Unlike the Kuomintang, which had needlessly antagonised and suppressed these merchant associations, we will continue to acknowledge their role within society and build a tranquil peace together.
Rebuilding A Southern Political Establishment
Through endless warfare and administrative fragmentation due to political infighting on all sides, Liangguang fell into near-anarchy. Swept away by the Kuomintang's takeover of the twin provinces, the Beiyang-friendly political establishment in the South was in ruins. Even as our control over Liangguang returned in the aftermath of the Northern Expedition, the political landscape has never been the same as the local bureaucracy stumbles to regain its grip. With the help of local administrative experts, the construction of a more efficient and well-oiled political machine will assist in the process of political centralisation.
Treading the Lawful Path
To rule lands through the iron grip and the army's strength is easy, but to maintain stability and social harmony is difficult if the rule of law is ignored, especially by the rulers who intend to govern their lands. Public perception of the governments in Liangguang has been at an all-time low, as crimes go unpunished and are, in many cases, encouraged as a path towards social mobility. With the calls for constitutionalism and democracy grow louder and louder, this is an opportune time for us to kill two birds with one stone by restoring public trust in our administration alongside calming democratic voices by demonstrating our commitment to a strict adherence to law.
Pressure Liangguang into Alignment
Our efforts in Liangguang have begun to bear fruit as those loyal to our government are starting to wield enough power to contest the current authorities in the region. With their mandate in the twin provinces on the verge of collapse, it is high time we apply pressure upon the region and mobilise loyalist forces within Liangguang to seize control!
Allure of Money and Flattery
The sorry state that Liangguang finds itself in is merely another opportunity for us to expand our influence in the South. Having recently repelled a devastating invasion by the Kuomintang alongside internal rebellions by bandits and local warlords, many within Liangguang are insecure about their positions, financially and militarily. By sending financial aid to assist in their reconstruction alongside flattering words of their leadership, they will become more receptive towards our government. After all, everyone has their price.
Bribing the Disaffected
Liangguang may be in a semi-stable state on the surface, but to those who look within, it is clear that not everybody is satisfied with the current arrangements. Whether it be out of petty grudges, ideological disagreements with their superiors, or simply willing to do anything for the sake of personal enrichment, many within Liangguang are willing to switch sides if bribed enough. Discreetly, we can dismantle the organisational structure of an opposing faction easily, allowing our preferred candidate in Liangguang to gain control without much bloodshed.
Issue Threats to Liangguang
With their military in tatters having recently come out of devastation, their inability to put up much of a resistance should another invasion march into Liangguang, and the need for time to rebuild their army has made Liangguang prone to appeasement. To further expand our influence within the region, we should pressure the leadership in Liangguang with threats, and hopefully, they will be scared enough to comply with our demands of accommodating our preferred side within their administration.
Accommodate Local Warlords
Aside from the incursions by Kuomintang forces, Liangguang was also plagued by rebellions staged by bandits and local warlords. Crushed by regional authorities along with the repelling of KMT forces, these warlords fled across the South, either retiring into obscurity or still hopelessly planning a comeback, intent on reclaiming the position they had lost in their rebellion. With them at our mercy, we could accommodate and use them to further expand our influence within the twin provinces.
Send Out Peace Feelers
The South has notoriously been the most rebellious region in the country, having been the host to Sun Yat-sen and the revolutionary Kuomintang, which had marched on the north in their Northern Expedition. Although the expedition collapsed and was unsuccessful, fears of a second Northern Expedition have yet to subside. Thus, it is necessary that we send peace feelers to Liangguang and ensure that conflict between our two administrations does not emerge, as well as strengthen those within their ranks who are sympathetic to our cause.
Expand the Guangxi System
Conceptualised as a fundamental framework in which local Guangxi leaders are able to organise their Guangxi Reconstruction Movement, the Guangxi Militia system finds its historical precedence in the Xia, Shang, and Zhou dynasties. Having no professional armies, no distinction existed between soldiers and peasants, with the army and people acting in unison. When the nation faced war, all in the nation took up arms. When peace returned, troops dispersed to till their lands. This system was referred to as \
Expand Guangxi System in [FROM.GetName]
Whilst the Guangxi system has found remarkable success within Guangxi itself, it has always been the ambitions of its progenitors to see it expanded to the whole of China. By dividing [FROM.GetName] into a series of militia regions, district magistrates will be indebted with the responsibilities of transplanting the Guangxi system to their local communities.
Add Reconnaissance Detachments
By incorporating various cavalry detachments into the Guangxi militia formations, we can ensure superior combat effectiveness and reconnaissance gathering capabilities within the paramilitaries. We shall be more than just the old provincial militia system, we shall be a new citizen's army.
Add Support Artillery
Expanding the firepower capabilities of our Guangxi militias are imperative, as the lone rifle cannot strike a semblance of the carnage or fear that a barrage of artillery shells can. Of course, it will be necessary to incorporate artillery training into the militia curriculum, but that is a simple matter.
Add Support Engineer Company
Including trained specialist engineer companies within the Guangxi militias will undoubtedly increase their effectiveness not only in field duty, but also in that of infrastructure efforts, and in the shaping of the new Chinese state.
Incorporate Additional Militia Formations
Whilst the initial militia's formation has proved themselves successful in all facets required of them, the time has come to advance from a mere militia to a full volunteer army. Utilising long term enlistments, and a working draft system, every able bodied male of military age shall be trained in the way of warfare. As when the inevitable final struggle dawns upon the Chinese people, every one will take up arms to fight for their nation.
Expand the Wehrstaat in [FROM.GetName]
Three Year Plan Decisions
Although Guangdong is a rich region in China, much work remains to be done if this province is to be brought into the modern age. The collapse of the League and Black Monday have laid bare our economic weaknesses, which has prompted the Guangzhou Government to lay out plans for an ambitious economic project that will modernise and develop our economy. The Three Year Plan will make use of Guangxi's material resources as well as Guangdong's industrial capacity to address both agricultural and urban issues in order to bring prosperity for all, and a beacon for the rest of China to emulate!
Wengjiang Hydroelectric Plant
Close in proximity to the city of Shaoguan is the Bei Jiang (North River), which flows south into Guangzhou. The Guangzhou Government's economic planners have decided that it is a prime spot to construct a hydroelectric plant, which will help with electrification efforts in Guangdong province.
Guangdong Beverage Factory
The Beverage Industry is a burgeoning part of Guangdong's economy. Many in China and indeed the world love to drink beers and soft drinks, and the architects of the Three Year Plan have laid out plans to seize on this opportunity by investing funds for a new beverage factory in Guangzhou, which will attract more commerce in Guangdong.
Guangdong Iron and Steel Mill
As part of our three year plan to modernize the economy of Guangdong, a plan has been formulated by the ministry of industry to develop Guangdong's iron and steel production. Despite being in abundance in China, steel output is low throughout the nation with the exception of the Anshan steel facility in the Northeast. Developing this steel and iron mill will help us reduce Japanese influence over our national economy and provide us a solid foundation for greater economic development.
Guangdong Chemical and Fertiliser Factory
Although a primarily agricultural nation, China still lacks a modern fertilising industry. Economic planners have outlined an ambitious project to develop a chemical and fertilising plant in Guangzhou which will hopefully kickstart China's fertilising modernisation.
Expand the Fuguo Coal Mine
We are still fighting shortages of important resources such as coal and the mines in Fuguo remain small. They should be expanded, for coal is one of the most important resources in the world and we must limit our imports of it.
Guangdong Farmer's Association Collectivisation
Whilst the Chinese nation may be united under the auspices of Peng Bodhisattva, day in and day out, the peasantry continue to lament under the perfidious gentry and landlord. No longer shall this be the case! Through any methods necessary, the peasantry will overthrow their chains and masters, rising to a new utopia!
Mass Collectivisation Efforts in [FROM.GetName]
The peasantry within [FROM.GetName] suffer under captialistic and feudalistic tyranny. Let [ROOT.GetLeader] and his loyal followers offer them their salvation.
China's Revolutionary New Culture Movement
Resolute in his beliefs, Tan Pingshan has seen the faults and fallacies in traditional Chinese culture. Such methods of living life has brought nothing but turmoil, pain and suffering to the Chinese people. This destructive influence has even destroyed the National Revolution of our forebearers. The true Chinese culture is that of a revolutionary one, a class conscious people exnoerating the Revolution.
Ensure Revolutionary Culture in [FROM.GetName]
[FROM.GetName] is rife with Counter-Revolutionary sentiment, and continues to remain unenlightened by the Third Party and our methods. Let us work towards their eventual integration into the mass Revolution.

Unification and Reconstruction
There can be no unification of the nation without reconstruction, and no reconstruction without unification of the nation! These are the principles by which the China Democratic League holds the whole nation accountable towards, and it is under these principles by which the new pseudo-military pseudo-civilian government of Li Jishen functions under. Under this policy plan, the nation must work towards the fulfillment of democracy and civil rights, independence and equality of the nation on the international stage, unification under the principles of self-governance, development of production and improvement of the lives of the peasants and workers, advancement of China's national culture and development of its scientific spirit, and above all else, a focus on peaceful reconstruction in national progress.\n\nThrough the affirmed recognition of basic political freedoms and human rights in conjunction with rulership by those with legitimate social positions — producers, educators, and servicemen — the nation shall advance beyond partisan politics. All under the expedient and diligent President-Marshal, the nation shall be ruled not by warlords nor egoism, and it shall not fall into the trappings of a Party State nor dictatorship; so that in the future, however far, the nation may yet experience democracy.
§YWaning enthusiasm in the Federalist Dream reduces the strength in integrity of the state! You will lose stability proportional to how much §cSocial Conservative§!, §nNational Populist§!, §PPaternal Autocrat§! and §lSocial Liberal§! influence you had.§!

Beiyang of the South
The Beiyang Republic undoubtedly has a complex legacy; under noble intentions revolutionaries sundered an autocratic and collapsing monarchy, instituting a fresh republican national order. And yet the abounding optimism of revolutionaries can hardly compare to the harsh realities of power brokering and establishment politics. Under the affairs of individuals such as Duan Qirui, Yuan Shikai, and Feng Guozhang, the Southern-led revolution became one that was contorted under the ambitions of military strongmen and force of arms. Shattered, broken, and then promptly reunited once again in 1928, the aspirations of the original Xinhai revolutionaries would be but a faint memory in only the oldest soldiers and politicians. But the legacy of the Five Races Under One Union still shines true in some of its most devout descendants and believers, of whom occupy the seat of power within the Chinese nation-state.\n\nAffirming the right of the Southern militarists over that of the North, the new Beiyang Republic has avowed to be an evolution of previous efforts to unite and centralise the Chinese Republican project. Despite national apathy to the new incumbents, the Chinese nation can at least breathe a sigh of relief, knowing that the nation has been reunified, and the time of rebuilding is sure to follow. Whatever form the reconstructed Republic will take, is ultimately up to the new political leaders of the Republic.
